Good man, it is like butter being churned from curds, water, the churn, the vessel, the rope, and human effort: the curds do not think, "I produce butter," nor do the water, churn, vessel, rope, or hand think, "I produce butter," nor does the butter say, "I generate myself." When conditions converge, butter is produced. The Heavenly Venerable is likewise, never thinking, "I turn the Dharma-wheel."

Good man, if there is no production, this is called "turning the true Dharma-wheel"; this turning of the Dharma-wheel is the Heavenly Venerable.

Good man, it is like a sprout arising from a seed, earth, water, fire, wind, fertile soil, season, and human labor: the seed does not say, "I generate the sprout," nor do the earth, water, fire, wind, soil, season, or labor say, "I generate the sprout," nor does the sprout say, "I generate myself." The Heavenly Venerable is likewise, never thinking, "I turn the Dharma-wheel."

Good man, if there is no such action, this is called "turning the Dharma-wheel"; this turning of the Dharma-wheel is the Heavenly Venerable.

Good man, it is like sound arising from a drum, space, skin, and human effort; when conditions converge, sound is produced. The drum does not think, "I produce sound," nor do the other conditions, nor does the sound say, "I generate myself." The Heavenly Venerable is likewise, never thinking, "I turn the Dharma-wheel."

Good man, one who turns the Dharma-wheel is called "one who does not act"; this is the Heavenly Venerable.

Good man, one who turns the Dharma-wheel is the Great Master of all immortals, a realm beyond the comprehension of disciples.

Good man, empty space is neither generated nor produced, neither created nor made, nor is it a conditioned phenomenon. The Heavenly Venerable is likewise: neither generated nor produced, neither created nor made, nor a conditioned phenomenon. The nature of the Great Master and the nature of the Dao are also thus: neither generated nor produced, neither created nor made, nor conditioned phenomena.

Good man, the teachings of the Great Masters of the immortals have two meanings: one is worldly speech, the other is transcendent speech. The Heavenly Venerable speaks worldly language to disciples and transcendent language to perfected ones.

Good man, among this great assembly, there are two kinds: those who seek the lesser vehicle and those who seek the greater vehicle. In the past, in the Primordial Yang World, I turned the Dharma-wheel for the immortal disciples; now, for the first time in the City of Ambrosia, I turn the great Dharma-wheel for the perfected ones.

Furthermore, good man, there are two types of people: those of middling roots and those of superior roots. For those of middling roots, I turned the Dharma-wheel in the Primordial Yang World; for those of superior roots, such as the Dharma King, Radiant Light, and others, I now turn the great Dharma-wheel in the City of Ambrosia, widely raising the banner of the Dharma for those of great faculties.

Good man, for those of the lowest roots, the Heavenly Venerable never turns the Dharma-wheel. Those of the lowest roots are the deluded followers of demons.

Furthermore, good man, those who seek the supreme Dao are of two kinds: one is single-minded in diligence, the other is supremely mindful in diligence. In the *Primordial Yang Sutra*, for those most diligent, I turn the Dharma-wheel.

Now in this city, for those supremely mindful in diligence, I turn the great Dharma-wheel.

Furthermore, good man, in the past, when I first turned the Dharma-wheel in that City of Ambrosia, eighty thousand perfected beings attained the natural fruit of the Dao. Now in this city, eighty thousand myriads of koṭis of people, their minds unwavering, all attain purity in the true and correct Dao.

Furthermore, good man, in the City of Ambrosia, Primordial Yang Perfected One bowed his head and entreated me to turn the Dharma-wheel. Now in this city, Radiant Light Perfected One bows his head and entreats me to turn the Dharma-wheel again.

Furthermore, good man, in the past when I turned the Dharma-wheel in that City of Ambrosia, I expounded on impermanence, suffering, emptiness, permanence, and bliss. Now in this city, when I turn the Dharma-wheel, I truly expound on the bliss of the everlasting.

Furthermore, good man, in the past when I turned the Dharma-wheel in that City of Ambrosia, the sound of my voice reached the Heavenly Venerables above in the Great Luo Heaven. Now again in this city, when I turn the Dharma-wheel, the sound of my voice pervades all the lands of the Empty Song Realm, the Nine Heavens, and the Ganges Worlds—east, west, south, north, the four intermediate directions, above, and below, all are likewise filled.

Good man, whatever the heavenly perfected beings say is all called turning the Dharma-wheel. Good man, it is like a king who is haughty and does not generate faith and reverence; those not yet subdued, he is able to subdue

The Dao can divide one body into many bodies at will, and then merge many bodies back into one, yet without attachment to such transformations, like a precious flower.

Good man, when perfected beings and Daoists attain entry into this true Dao, the Dharma King, they abide in the realm of freedom. Dwelling in this realm of freedom, they gain the power of autonomy, and wherever they wish to be born, they are born accordingly.

Good man, it is like a sagely king who rules the four heavens and goes wherever he pleases without obstruction. Perfected beings and Daoists are likewise: in all places of rebirth, if they wish to be born there, they go as they will.

Good man, if perfected beings and Daoists see beings in hell who can be taught and guided to dwell in wholesome roots, the perfected ones will immediately be born among them. Though they are born there, it is not due to their own karmic retribution; rather, dwelling in the realm of freedom, they are born there for karmic conditions’ sake.

Good man, though perfected beings and Daoists enter hell, they do not suffer its torments.

Good man, the wholesome roots that perfected beings and Daoists accomplish are boundless and immeasurable, beyond reckoning even by the Ganges’ sands. How much more so are the inconceivable merit, virtue, and power of the Heavenly Venerable’s majestic deeds and fields of blessing?

At that time, among the assembly was a perfected one named Worthy Wisdom, possessed of great majesty and virtue, accomplished in spiritual penetrations, master of the Great Total Retention, perfect in dharma marks, and fearless. Rising from his seat, he came forward, made obeisance, knelt with joined palms, and said: “As the Heavenly Venerable has expounded, the merit and wisdom accomplished by perfected beings and Daoists are boundless and immeasurable, beyond hundreds of thousands of myriads of koṭis, truly beyond expression. Yet in my mind, I still think they do not compare to the *Primordial Yang Scripture*.

Why? Because it is by the power of this *Primordial Yang Mahāyāna Sūtra* that all the Heavenly Venerables’ supreme, correct, and true Great Dao is brought forth.”

Then the Heavenly Venerable praised him, saying: “Profound indeed! Inconceivable! Good man, it is just as you say. Though these scriptures of the great sages are replete with boundless merit and virtue, to compare them to this sūtra would be no comparison at all—hundredfold, thousandfold, boundless and immeasurable, beyond the sands of the Ganges, beyond all analogy.

Good man, it is like milk drawn from a cow, from which curds are made; from curds comes butter; from butter, the sweet and exquisite flavor of ghee. Whoever partakes of it is cured of all illnesses, and all medicines are subsumed within it.

Good man, the Heavenly Venerable is likewise: from the Heavenly Venerable comes the wondrous *Primordial Yang Sūtra*; from the *Primordial Yang Sūtra* comes the Great Dao Dharma; from the Great Dao Dharma comes the Dharma of diligence; from the Dharma of diligence comes the Dharma of forbearance and precepts; from forbearance and precepts comes the natural Dao fruit. The natural Dao fruit is the sweet and exquisite flavor of the Dharma. What is called the sweet and exquisite flavor of the Dharma is an analogy for the Dao-nature. The Dao-nature is the Heavenly Venerable.

Good man, for this reason it is said that the Heavenly Venerable’s wholesome roots are beyond reckoning, like the sands of the Ganges.”

Worthy Wisdom Perfected One said to the Heavenly Venerable: “As the Heavenly Venerable has said, the *Primordial Yang Sūtra* is like the sweet and exquisite flavor of the Dharma, most wondrous. If ordinary beings partake of it, their illnesses are cured of themselves, and all medicines are subsumed within it. Having heard this, I privately reflect: if there are those who cannot listen to and receive this sūtra, they must be greatly foolish, devoid of wholesome minds.

Heavenly Venerable, from this day forth, I will wholeheartedly transcribe this *Primordial Yang Sūtra*, receive, uphold, read, and recite it, ensuring its profound benefit. Thereafter, I will widely expound its meaning to others.

Heavenly Venerable, if there are beings attached to wealth and possessions, I will first offer them wealth, then urge them to read this *Primordial Yang Sūtra*. If they are noble and esteemed, I will first speak gently, aligning with their minds, then gradually urge them to read this *Primordial Yang Sūtra*. If they are ordinary and foolish, I will compel them with authority to read it. If they are arrogant and haughty, I will serve them as a servant, aligning with their minds to bring them joy, then teach them with the *Primordial Yang Sūtra*. If there are those who slander the Mahāyāna sūtras, I will subdue them with power, and once subdued, urge them to read and recite the *Primordial Yang Sūtra*. If there are those who delight in the true Dao sūtras, I will personally go to them with reverence, make offerings, honor them, and snap my fingers in praise.

Then the Heavenly Venerable praised Worthy Wisdom Perfected One, saying: “Excellent, excellent! You now cherish and long for the true Dao scriptures, delight in and believe in the true Dao scriptures, receive, uphold, make offerings to, and bow in worship to them.

Good man, by this wholesome mind and karmic condition, you will transcend boundless and immeasurable realms, beyond the sands of the Ganges. You will accomplish the supreme, correct, true, and natural fruit of the perfected being and Daoist, and before long, you too will be like me. You will widely expound this *Primordial Yang Sūtra*, the Heavenly Venerable’s secret treasury, to the great assembly.

Good man, even before the Heavenly Venerable of the past appeared, I was then practicing diligence, cultivating the Heavenly King, and perfecting the practices of the perfected ones. I was able to comprehend all the scriptures and treatises of the immortals. I practiced the true and constant conduct, was replete in majestic deportment, my mind pure, untainted by heterodox views. I was able to be born wherever desire arose, extinguishing the fires of anger and delusion. I received and upheld the bliss of karmic merit and the true and constant. I sought throughout the Great Vehicle’s wondrous scriptures, yet never even heard the name of the *Primordial Yang Sūtra*.

At that time, I dwelt on the Mountain of Wondrous Bliss. That mountain was pure, with flowing springs, ponds, and pools. Trees bore sweet fruits, filling the land in abundance. Among the cliffs and rocks flowed clear streams. Many fragrant flowers covered the entire region. Birds and beasts, wondrous and rare, could not all be named. Sweet fruits flourished, and myriad fragrances filled the air. There were also boundless fragrant roots.”

At that time, I dwelt alone amidst these surroundings, subsisting only on fruits and fragrant roots. After eating, I struck my breast and reflected upon the practices of diligence, endurance, and forbearance. For countless ages, I never even heard the name of the Heavenly Worthy’s most wondrous scriptures.

Good man, as I cultivated such arduous practices, the gods and devas were greatly astonished. They gathered together and spoke to one another in verse:

*"The Heavenly Worthy expounds the supreme canon,
Unfolding the Dao and revealing the primordial essence.
Proclaimed as the Father of all beings,
The King adorned with virtue and majesty.
Severing the paths of greed and delusion,
Dispelling the madness of ignorance.
On the pure and wondrous Mountain of Bliss,
A carefree realm of sweet dew."*

Then, among the assembly, a Heavenly King named Universal Wisdom spoke in verse:

*"Among all such perfected ones,
You are foremost in purity.
Profoundly understanding the Great Vehicle’s meaning,
Deeply comprehending the secret and mysterious.
If one seeks the supreme Way,
One must abandon mental indolence,
Realize the practices of suffering and emptiness,
And forever be free from the illness of afflictions."*

Thereupon, another immortal, named Radiant Stillness, spoke in verse:

*"The supreme Dharma’s essence is profound and wondrous,
Its quiescent principle difficult to fathom.
Unless one possesses the power of total retention,
Who could grasp the rites of the Primordial Beginning?
Now that we have heard this teaching,
We may establish a noble standard,
Sever all evil karma,
And freely enter and abide in the unconditioned."*

After these verses were spoken, the perfected ones and Heavenly Kings said: "We now praise and speak in verse, entreating the Heavenly Worthy on behalf of this worthy man and all beings—not for his own sake, but to benefit all ordinary beings—who cultivates myriad and boundless ascetic practices.

Such a person, perceiving the faults within birth and death, would not generate desire or delight even if rare treasures filled the earth, all mountains, and seas, regarding them as filth and excrement.

This worthy man, abandoning jewels and treasures, forsaking beloved wives and children, flesh and blood, marrow and brain, limbs and digits, dwellings and homes, cattle, horses, and carriages, does not even wish to be born in the heavens. He only wishes that all beings may attain joy, as I understand it.

Such a worthy man, pure and unstained, with all fetters forever extinguished, desires only to seek the supreme, correct, and true fruit of the natural Great Dao."

They further declared: "As you have said, this person is one who gathers beneath the Tree of the Way, able to eradicate afflictions and slander. If all beings abide in the cool shade of this Tree of the Way, all afflictions and karmic deeds will be extinguished. If in future worlds one becomes a Tathāgata, we shall all attain the extinction of boundless afflictions. Yet such matters are truly difficult to believe. Why is this so?"

All beings who arouse the natural intention of the Dao, upon perceiving the slightest conditions, immediately waver within their natural resolve—like the moon in water, which sways when the water moves. Just as a painted image is difficult to complete yet easy to ruin, so too is the natural intention of the Dao: difficult to arouse yet easy to destroy. For instance, when many men, clad in armor and helmets, prepare to march against bandits, if at the moment of battle their hearts fill with terror, they will turn and flee. All beings are likewise: though they arouse the natural intention of the Dao and fortify themselves, upon seeing the perils of birth and death, their hearts grow anxious and fearful, and they immediately retreat in regret. Having observed how all beings, after arousing such resolve, become unsettled, I now, though I see this man single-mindedly practicing austerities, free from affliction and vexation, abiding in the Dao with pure conduct, still cannot believe it. I must go myself to test him, to know whether he is truly capable of bearing the weighty eaves of the supreme, correct, and true fruit of the natural Great Dao. Just as a cart with two wheels can bear a load, or a bird with two wings can take flight, so too must one who practices austerities be thus. Though I see him steadfastly upholding the precepts, I do not yet know whether he possesses wisdom. If he has wisdom, then he will be able to bear the weight of the supreme, correct, and true fruit of the natural Dao. It is like a fish with many eggs—few come to maturity. Or like a fruit tree—many blossoms, few fruits. Though beings arouse the intention to seek the true and boundless, in the end, few are worthy of mention.

"True One, let us go together to test him, just as true gold is tested in three ways—by fire, hammering, and polishing—so too shall we test this ascetic. Then, O Primal Yang True One, you transformed your body into a fierce beast, terrifying in form, descending near the Mountain of Wondrous Joy, standing not far from him. At that time, the fierce beast, fearless and mighty, unmatched in eloquence, with a voice pure and refined, proclaimed the teachings once spoken by the Heavenly Venerable of the Past, reciting these verses:

*All conditioned things are non-action,
Such is the law of arising and ceasing.
The wheel of rebirth turns through causes and conditions,
Though cast aside, they reunite.*

*With focused mind, purify the three karmas,
The true Dao may be attained in due time,
To deliver the destitute from poverty.*

After reciting these verses, the beast stood before him in its fearsome form, glancing left and right, surveying the four directions. The ascetic, upon hearing these verses, rejoiced in his heart—like a traveler lost in perilous lands at night, separated from his companions, filled with dread and anxiety, who suddenly encounters a fellow wayfarer and rejoices immeasurably. Or like one long afflicted with illness who, without meeting a skilled physician, suddenly finds a wondrous medicine in an instant, his ailment cured, and his heart overflows with joy. Like a drowning man who finds a boat and crosses to the far shore, his heart filled with delight. Or like one parched with thirst who suddenly comes upon a sweet spring, drinking his fill and quenching his thirst, his heart rejoicing. Like one pursued by enemies who suddenly escapes, free from all afflictions, his heart filled with joy. Or like a prisoner led to the marketplace who suddenly hears a pardon and is set free, his heart rejoicing. Like a farmer suffering drought who suddenly receives rain, his seedlings growing, his grains ripening in abundance, his heart filled with joy. Or like one on a distant journey who suddenly returns home, his heart rejoicing.

"Good man, when I heard these verses at that time, my heart likewise rejoiced. I rose from my seat, looked in all four directions, and said: 'Who spoke the verses I just heard?' I looked around but saw nothing else—only the fierce beast. I then said: 'Who has opened this profound and wondrous gate? Who thunders with such subtle and marvelous sound? Who, in the slumber of birth and death, can yet awaken? Who can, in this place, guide the hungry beings of birth and death to the supreme flavor of the Dao? All beings are lost in the bitter sea of suffering—who can serve as the great helmsman within it? All beings are constantly entangled in the sickness of afflictions—who can be the skilled physician among them?'

After reciting these verses, they awakened my heart like the waxing moon gradually revealing its light. Good man, at that time, I saw nothing else—only the fierce beast. I thought: 'Could this beast have spoken these verses?' My heart grew doubtful, for it seemed unlikely. Why? Its form was so terrifying that had anyone heard these verses, all fear and ugliness would have vanished—how could such a creature bear this form? One who could speak such verses should not be like a night-glowing fungus sprouting in fire.

"Good man, I then thought: 'I lack wisdom, but perhaps this beast has encountered the immortals of the past and heard these verses from the Heavenly Venerable.' I decided to ask it and approached the beast, saying: 'Excellent! Excellent! Where did you encounter the verses spoken by the fearless one of the past? Where did you attain the meaning of these luminous jewel-verses? They are the true and correct Dao of the Primal Heavenly Venerable of the past, future, and present—boundless and immeasurable throughout all the worlds. Ordinary beings are forever shrouded in the net of doubt, and in their entire lives, they cannot hear such profound teachings as those spoken by the Heavenly Venerables of the ten directions.'"

"Good man, upon hearing this, I immediately replied, saying: 'Great true one, you should not ask me about this matter. Why? I have not eaten for many days, and despite searching in every way, I have found nothing. Hunger and suffering have confused my mind, and my words are deluded—not what my original heart truly knows. Though I now possess the power to fly through the void and seek food everywhere, I still cannot obtain it. For this reason, I spoke these words.'

Good man, I then said to the beast: 'If you can recite these verses in full for me, I will become your disciple for life. What you have spoken is neither complete in name nor exhaustive in meaning. For what reason do you refuse to recite them? Offerings of wealth and treasures may be exhausted, but the causes and conditions of Dharma-giving cannot be depleted. The gift of Dharma is inexhaustible and brings great benefit. Now that I have heard these verses, my heart is filled with doubt. If you would kindly dispel it for me by reciting them in full, I will become your disciple for life.'

The beast replied: 'Your wisdom exceeds all things, yet you care only for yourself and show no concern for my present state. Pressed by hunger and suffering, I truly cannot recite them.'

I then asked: 'What do you eat?'

The beast answered: 'You need not ask me. If I tell you, it will inspire terror.'

I replied: 'This place is perilous, and there is no one else here. I do not fear you. Why will you not speak?'

The beast answered: 'What I eat is only the warm flesh of humans, and what I drink is only their hot blood. My sustenance is human flesh alone. Though I search everywhere, I cannot obtain it. Most people in the world possess good fortune and are protected by the gods and benevolent spirits. Powerless, I cannot kill them.'

Good man, I then said to the beast: 'If you recite these verses in full, once I have heard them, I will offer this body of mine as an offering to you. Even if my life ends, this body of mine is of no use—it will only be devoured by vile insects and yield no merit. Now, in seeking the fruit of the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao, I abandon this impure body to exchange it for a pure one.'

The beast replied: 'Who would believe such words of yours—that for the sake of the true Dao, you would abandon your beloved body?'

Good man, I then answered: 'You are greatly lacking in wisdom. It is like someone who gives away a common vessel to obtain a true treasure. I, too, abandon this unworthy body to gain a steadfast one. As for your question of who would believe me, I now have witnesses: the countless Heavenly Kings all attest to this. Moreover, the true ones and Daoist masters with the Heavenly Eye, who cultivate and uphold the Mahāyāna scriptures for the benefit of all beings, and who possess the Four Immeasurables and the Six Perfections, can also bear witness. The Heavenly Venerables of the ten directions, who benefit all beings, can likewise confirm that I abandon this body for the true Dao.'

The beast then said: 'If you are truly able to abandon your life in this way, focus your mind attentively, and I will explain the verses for you in detail.'

Good man, upon hearing these words, my heart rejoiced. I immediately removed the clothes I was wearing and spread them out as a Dharma-seat for the beast, saying: 'True one, I pray you ascend this seat.'

I then knelt before it, joined my hands, and said: 'I only pray that the true one will expound the verses for me, that I may hear them in full.'

The beast then recited the verses:

*When arising and ceasing are extinguished,*
*Quiescent extinction is constant bliss.*
*Roaming the seven-jeweled terrace,*
*Wandering the fourfold luminous pavilion.*
*All defilements have been extinguished,*
*Pure and undefiled by evil.*
*Abandoning life to receive the true body,*
*Good causes without attachment.*

When the beast had finished reciting these verses, it said: 'Divine immortals and assembly, you have now heard the verses in full. Your wish is entirely fulfilled. If you truly seek to benefit all beings, you may offer me your body.'

At that time, I deeply pondered this meaning. Then, I wrote down the verses in various ways and tied them to my clothes, fearing that after death, my body would be exposed. I then climbed a great tree.

The tree spirit then asked me: 'Alas! What is the matter with you, good one?'

I answered: 'I wish to abandon my body in repayment for the verses.'

The spirit said: 'What benefit do these verses bring?'

I replied: 'These verses were expounded by the Primal Heavenly Venerable. For the sake of this Dharma, I abandon my life—not for fame, profit, or material gain, but only to benefit the countless ordinary beings.' Thus, I abandoned my body.

Good man, as I was about to abandon my body, I thought: 'May all miserly and greedy people see me relinquish this body. If there are those who cling to it, may they also see me abandon my life for a single verse, as if discarding filth.'

When I had spoken these words, I immediately cast aside my life and threw myself from the tree. Before I reached the ground, a hundred kinds of sounds arose in the empty sky.

At that moment, the beast also abandoned its body in midair, caught mine, and gently placed it on the ground. The Perfected of Primordial Yang, along with the assembly of divine immortals, bowed and paid homage before my seat, praising: 'Excellent! Truly wise and virtuous, you bring great benefit to all beings, desiring to kindle the great Dharma-fire within ignorance. For cherishing the wondrous Dharma of the Heavenly Venerable, you have endured such affliction. I only pray that the great virtue will permit me to repent and confess my transgressions. In the future, you will surely attain the natural fruit of the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao. May you be saved and delivered.'"

At that moment, the Perfected and the great assembly took their leave and suddenly vanished.

*The Upper Scripture of the Numinous Treasure’s Primordial Yang Wondrous Canon, Scroll Two concludes.*

*The Upper Scripture of the Numinous Treasure’s Primordial Yang Wondrous Canon, Scroll Three*
**The Chapter on Compassionate Conduct**

Then, the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning addressed Wondrous Joy Perfected in the Nine-Bend Chamber of the Purple Tenuity Jeweled Palace, within the Golden Radiance Jade Hall of the Primordial Yang Realm: "You now cultivate compassion, joy, and loving-kindness in this land, abiding in the realm of cherishing love as one cherishes an only child."

Wondrous Joy Perfected bowed and paid homage, then addressed the Celestial Venerable: "By what cause and condition is this called the realm of cherishing love as one cherishes an only child?"

The Celestial Venerable replied: "Just as parents raise their child in peace and their hearts fill with joy. Good man, abiding in this realm is likewise: you regard all beings as sharing one ground. Seeing those who cultivate goodness, you feel great delight. Therefore, this realm is called *cherishing love*. Just as parents, seeing their child afflicted by illness, feel sorrow and distress yet never abandon them, good man, abiding in this realm is likewise: seeing all ordinary beings entangled by the sickness of afflictions, your heart fills with sorrow and compassion, as if blood flowed from every pore of your child. Thus, this realm is called *the realm of the only child*.

"Just as when a child is small, they pick up filth and place it in their mouth, and the parents, seeing this, feel dread and fear, anxious for harm to come, so they rinse with water and remove the filth. Good man, abiding in this realm is likewise: seeing all ordinary beings whose bodily, verbal, and mental actions are mostly unwholesome, the Perfected, seeing this, uses the hand of wisdom to pluck it out, pitying the ordinary beings, not wishing them to wander in birth and death and suffer afflictions. Thus, this realm is called *the only child*.

"Just as parents, thinking of their beloved child, suddenly encounter illness, and in an instant, the child perishes, the parents weep in grief, wishing to share the same fate. The Perfected likewise sees all beings falling into the three evil destinies and wishes to descend with them into hell. Why? When all beings suffer, if even for a single thought they generate the intention to repent, I then teach them the methods of cultivating goodness. In that single thought, they plant the roots of goodness. Thus, this realm is again called *the only child*.

"Just as parents who have only one child, whether walking, standing, or lying down, constantly cherish and think of them, and if the child commits faults, they speak with gentle words, skillfully comforting and guiding, never adding to their wrongdoing, the Perfected and Daoists likewise, seeing all ordinary beings falling into the three evil destinies, feel compassion and pity, never generating anger or adding harm to them. Thus, this realm is again called *the only child*."

Wondrous Joy Perfected addressed the Celestial Venerable: "As the Venerable has spoken, these words are profound and hidden. My wisdom is shallow—how can I comprehend them? If all Perfected abide in the realm of the only child and can do so, why did the Celestial Venerable, when formerly the King of Sweet Dew, practice the conduct of a Perfected yet sever the life of the Dharma Dragon Elder? If one attains this realm, one should generate a heart of love for ordinary beings. If one does not attain it, what cause and condition prevent falling into the three evil destinies? If one pities all beings, regarding them equally as an only child, with no partiality in the heart, how do these words not contradict in meaning?

"When the Celestial Venerable abides in the realm of emptiness and wishes to seek alms for food, you must observe people. If anyone harbors jealousy toward you, you do not proceed, even if extremely hungry. Why? The Perfected and Daoists constantly think thus: *I recall that in a past kalpa, at a field of merit, I generated a single evil thought. Due to this cause and condition, I fell into hell and suffered afflictions. Now, though I am extremely hungry, I will not beg for food, lest I cause them to doubt me and fall into hell, suffering afflictions.*

"Further, they think: *If any ordinary being doubts that I stand, I will sit upright all day. If any ordinary being doubts that I sit, I will stand all day without lying down.* Such is the heart of the Perfected and Daoists in protecting and thinking of beings—how much more so the great sage, spiritually penetrative! If one attains the realm of the only child, why would the Celestial Venerable utter such words, causing ordinary beings to generate grave evil?"

The Celestial Venerable addressed Wondrous Joy Perfected: "You should not pose such difficult questions. I create the causes and conditions of afflictions for ordinary beings. Even if I had the power to exhaust the waters of the sea, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. Even if heaven and earth were entirely transformed into non-form, water into solidity, fire into water, and wind into pouring, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. Even if one violated the four alliance prohibitions and a single ordinary being slandered the true Dharma, attaining the ten fearless powers of a sage in this very life, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. Even if the disciples of lesser immortals and a single heretic held unchanging views, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. Even if all Perfected violated the four alliance precepts and engaged in slandering the true and correct teaching, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. Even if all immeasurable beings severed their Dao-nature, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. Even if a thrown rope could bind the wind, and blowing fierce fires could burn stone mountains, I would never become the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings. I would rather dwell with venomous snakes and fierce tigers than utter words that make the sage the root of afflictions for all ordinary beings."

"Good son, the Heavenly Worthy truly can sever afflictions for all ordinary beings, and never becomes the root of afflictions for them.

Perfected One of Wondrous Joy, as you have said, in a past kalpa the Heavenly Worthy killed the Dharma Dragon Elder.

Good son, even the tiniest insects and ants I would not kill—how much less the Dharma Dragon Elder! He was a virtuous man, always employing skillful means to bestow blessings upon beings, granting them immeasurable lifespans. To give food is to give life. When Perfected Ones and Daoists practice generosity, they constantly bestow upon all beings immeasurable vital existence.

Good son, practicing the precept of non-killing leads to long life. When Perfected Ones and Daoists uphold the precepts, they thereby grant all ordinary beings immeasurable lifespans.

Good son, guarding the mouth from evil yields long life. When Perfected Ones and Daoists practice forbearance, they constantly exhort all ordinary beings not to harbor resentment, to ascribe rightness to others and faults to themselves, to be free from anger, and thus attain long life. Therefore, when Perfected Ones practice forbearance, they have already bestowed upon all ordinary beings immeasurable destinies.

Good son, single-mindedly cultivating goodness leads to long life. When Perfected Ones and Daoists practice diligence, they constantly exhort all ordinary beings to cultivate wholesome dharmas. When ordinary beings practice thus, they obtain long life. Therefore, when Perfected Ones and Daoists practice diligence, they have already bestowed upon all ordinary beings immeasurable destinies.

Good son, cultivating the dharma of collected mind leads to long life. When Perfected Ones and Daoists practice meditative concentration, they observe all ordinary beings cultivating the mind of equanimity. When ordinary beings practice thus, they obtain long life. Therefore, when Perfected Ones practice meditative concentration, they have already bestowed upon all ordinary beings immeasurable destinies.

Good son, not being heedless regarding all dharmas leads to long life. When Perfected Ones and Daoists cultivate wisdom, they exhort all ordinary beings not to be heedless regarding wholesome dharmas. When ordinary beings practice thus, by this cause and condition they obtain long life. Therefore, when Perfected Ones cultivate wisdom, they have already bestowed upon all ordinary beings immeasurable destinies.

Good son, for these reasons, Perfected Ones and Daoists never abandon any ordinary being.

Perfected One of Wondrous Joy, regarding your earlier question about the killing of the Dharma Dragon Elder—did he attain this state at that time?

Good son, at that time I had already attained loving-kindness, and thus severed his life-root, not out of malice. Good son, it is like parents who cherish their only child. If that child violates the law, the parents, out of fear, may either cast him out or kill him. Though they cast him out or kill him, they do so without malice. Perfected Ones and Daoists, in upholding the good Dao, are likewise.

If any ordinary being slanders the *Yuanyang Sutra*, they may be disciplined with whips and staves, or even have their life taken, in order to turn them from evil and cultivate the good Dao. The mind of the Perfected One constantly contemplates thus: By what means can ordinary beings be caused to generate wholesome minds? Whatever skillful means are necessary must be employed.

After the Dharma Dragon Elder’s life ended, he was born in the Northern Prison of Black Sand. There he had three thoughts: First, he wondered, ‘From where have I come?’ Immediately he became aware that he had come from the human realm. Second, he wondered, ‘Where am I now born?’ Immediately he became aware that he was in the Northern Prison of Black Sand. Third, he wondered, ‘By what karmic conditions have I come here?’ Immediately he became aware that it was due to slandering the *Yuanyang Sutra*, not believing in causes and conditions, and being killed by the king that he had come to be born here. Having realized this, he generated reverence for the *Yuanyang Sutra*. Soon after, his life ended, and he was born in a world of bliss and sovereignty, where he obtained a complete lifespan.

Good son, for these reasons, in a past kalpa I merely shared a lifespan with this person—how can this be called killing?

Good son, if a good person digs the earth, cuts grass, chops trees, severs a corpse, or utters curses and imprecations—by these causes and conditions, do they fall into hell?"

Perfected One of Wondrous Joy said to the Heavenly Worthy, "As I understand the meaning of the sagely teaching, they should fall into hell. Why? As the Heavenly Worthy once preached to those of heterodox views, ‘You, my disciples, must not harm grasses and trees without malice. Why? It leads to the evil destinies.’"

Then the Heavenly Worthy praised the Perfected One of Wondrous Joy: "Excellent! Excellent! As you have said, it should be well received and upheld.

Good son, if one falls into evil destinies due to malice, then Perfected Ones at that time were truly without malice. Why? Perfected Ones and Daoists, regarding all ordinary beings—even insects and ants—all generate minds of compassion and benefit. Why is this? Because they skillfully understand causes, conditions, and all expedient means. By the power of expedient means, they wish to lead all ordinary beings to perform meritorious deeds.

Good son, for these reasons, at that time, though I took his life, it was through skillful means and not out of malice.

Good son, if one kills insects and ants by the hundreds of millions, there is but slight karmic retribution. Tigers, wolves, poisonous snakes, mosquitoes, fleas, lice, bears, and wildcats—anything that harms all ordinary beings—if one severs their lives, there is but slight karmic retribution. If one kills a violent and harmful evil person, there is karmic retribution. If, after killing, one does not repent, one falls into the three evil destinies. If one can repent and confess openly, fasting for three days, the transgression is immediately extinguished, leaving no residue.

If one harms a good person, a virtuous and practicing Daoist, one’s parents, a woman, or a cow, one falls into hell for immeasurable kalpas."

Good son, the Realized Ones and I recognize three kinds of killing. What are these three? They are: the low, the middle, and the high.

The low refers to ants and all other animals, excepting only those in whom a Realized One manifests a birth. When a Realized One or Daoist, by the power of their vow, manifests as an animal, this is called low killing. Through the cause of low killing, one falls into the three evil destinies of hell, where all sufferings are fully endured. Why is this? Because these animals possess subtle roots of goodness, and thus the killer fully receives the karmic retribution. This is called low killing.

Middle killing refers to ordinary beings up to those in the initial stages of learning. This is called middle killing. Through this karmic cause, one falls into the three evils, fully enduring middle sufferings. This is called middle killing.

High killing refers to plotting against the ruler of a state, one’s parents, respected elders, Realized Ones, or good people. This is called high killing. Through this cause, one falls into the evil destinies of the three paths of hell, fully enduring the highest sufferings. This is called high killing.

If one kills those who commit the ten evils or the five heinous crimes, one does not fall into these three kinds of evil destinies. Good son, all such violent people are foolish, like digging the earth, cutting grass, chopping trees, scolding, or whipping—there is no karmic retribution. Killing a single violent and heinous person is likewise without karmic retribution. Why is this? Such violent and heinous ones lack faith and the like, and bring no benefit to beings. Thus, though one kills them, there is no karmic retribution.

Good son, you should not have asked why the Heavenly Worthy cursed and called the karma-receiving great adept a fool who eats spittle. Why is this? The words uttered by the Heavenly Worthy cannot be likened to anything.

Good son, there are those whose words are true and loved by others, yet spoken at the wrong time and contrary to the Dharma, bringing no benefit—such speech I ultimately do not believe. Good son, there are also those who utter harsh, perverse, flattering, or deceitful words, spoken at the wrong time and contrary to the Dharma, which are disliked by listeners and bring no benefit—I likewise do not believe them. Good son, if there are sounds, though harsh, that are true and without error, spoken at the right time and in accord with the Dharma, capable of benefiting all ordinary beings, even if they are not believed when heard, I must still speak them. Why is this? The Heavenly Worthy’s divine penetrations and wisdom power pervade all skillful means.

Good son, as I once traveled through mountains and forests, villages and towns, beneath a tree there was a great ghost named Jingchang, who fed solely on flesh and blood, killing many beings, and in his gathering, devoured one person each day. Good son, at that time, I expounded the marks of the Dharma to that great ghost, yet in his ignorance, he refused to accept the teachings. I then transformed my body into a mighty spirit, toppled his palace, and made it uninhabitable. The ghost, at that moment, led his retinue out of his palace, intending to resist and strike. When the great ghost saw me, he was seized by terror and confusion, collapsing to the ground like a dead man. With a mind of compassion, I stroked his body with my hand, and he immediately rose and sat up, saying: “Great indeed! Fortunate am I to have my life restored. This is the power of a great spirit, endowed with majestic dignity, a mind of mercy that pardons my offenses.” He then generated reverence and faith before me. I then resumed the form of the Heavenly Worthy and further expounded the true essential Dharma, causing that ghost and his spirits to receive the precept against killing. On that very day, in the village or town, there was an elder named Falong who was next to die, and his family had already delivered him to the ghost. The ghost, having received him, offered him to me. After accepting him, I gave the elder a new name, calling him Rushou.

At that time, the ghost addressed me, saying: “Now this retinue of mine relies solely on blood and flesh to sustain their lives. Having received the Dharma, how shall we provide for the Heavenly Worthy?” I replied: “From this day forward, have all perfected ones and Daoists, wherever they practice their methods and conduct their affairs, universally offer them food and drink.” Good son, for this reason, such a rule was established for all immortals and Daoists. From now on, you must always offer food to that ghost, Jingchang. If there are places where this is not done, know that those are not my disciples—they are companions of the heavenly demons.

Good son, the Heavenly Worthy demonstrates such skillful means to tame and subdue all ordinary beings, not intending to instill fear in them. Good son, I have struck guardian ghosts with wood, and at another time, pushed a great ghost’s body from a mountaintop, causing him to fall below, and also pierced the body of the Jianmao ghost with needles. Though I acted thus, I did not cause those ghosts and spirits to be destroyed; I merely wished to establish them in the true Dharma, demonstrating such skillful means.

Good son, in the past, I have never reviled those of perverse views or doubts with abusive words; nor have I been foolish, consuming others’ nasal mucus and spittle; nor have I been born in the evil destinies, the three woeful realms of hell, enduring manifold sufferings; nor have I slandered Daoists or learners of the Way; nor have I violated the four covenantal transgressions, slandering the primordial Yang true Dharma, the esoteric scriptures, nor am I one of those latecomers to learning; nor am I of the lesser immortals. Good son, the lesser immortals and late learners are not within the realm of perverse views or demonic influences—only the sages fully comprehend this.

Good son, therefore, you should not have asked why the Heavenly Worthy became angry and reproached the late-learning immortals. You should not harbor such doubts regarding the realms of all the heavens.

The Perfected One of Wondrous Joy addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “It is like sugarcane—when chewed in the mouth, one obtains its sweetness. Likewise, from the assembly of sages, hearing the scriptures, I have gained the flavors of the Dharma: the flavor of the Dao, the flavor of the Dharma, the flavor of wisdom, the flavor of thorough understanding.”

“The Heavenly Worthy is like true gold: the more it is smelted and refined, the more its brilliance increases, becoming malleable and soft, its luster pure and fair, its value immeasurable—only then does it become a treasure for humans and gods. The Heavenly Worthy, the sage, is also thus: through earnest inquiry, one comes to understand the profound and subtle meanings, enabling one to receive and uphold them, awakening to the boundless.”

“When ordinary beings generate the natural intention of the Dao, they then become revered by all humans and gods.”

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy praised the Perfected One of Wondrous Joy, saying: “Excellent, excellent! Perfected ones and Daoists, for the sake of benefiting all ordinary beings, have thus inquired of the Heavenly Worthy regarding such wondrous Dharma. Good son, for this reason, in accordance with your wishes, I expound this primordial Yang, great vehicle, subtle and wondrous scripture—one that is compassionate, like the love for an only child.”

The Perfected One of Wondrous Joy addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “If perfected ones and Daoists cultivate the minds of kindness, compassion, joy, and obtain the state of an only child, when they cultivate the mind of equanimity, what state do they then attain?”

The Heavenly Worthy said: “Good son, you know well the proper time, and when I have something to say, you then inquire. When perfected ones and Daoists cultivate the mind of equanimity, they abide in the Dharma-ground of the empty and equal. Good son, when perfected ones and Daoists abide in this empty and equal Dharma-ground, they do not perceive the six kinds of relatives or the center of enmity and hatred. Good son, just as empty space has no six kinds of relatives, nor even enmity and hatred, all dharmas are likewise without relatives. All the outflows—when perfected ones and Daoists see all dharmas—their minds are equal, like empty space.”

“Why is this so? Because they are skillfully able to contemplate and transcend all the Dharma-gates of emptiness.”

The Wondrous Joy Perfected One again addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “What is called emptiness?”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Good son, this emptiness is what is called internal emptiness, external emptiness, emptiness of the unconditioned, emptiness of the conditioned, and all dharmas are entirely empty.

Good son, what is meant by contemplating internal emptiness? When perfected ones and Daoists contemplate the emptiness of internal dharmas, this emptiness of internal dharmas is without relatives or the center of enmity and hatred. The true and constant joy of the Heavenly Worthy’s Dharma-disciples, and all their possessions, exist within these internal dharmas. Though they possess the Dao-nature, this Dao-nature is neither internal nor external. Why is this so? The Dao-nature abides constantly, without change or movement. This is called the perfected ones and Daoists’ contemplation of internal emptiness. What is called external emptiness is likewise so. There being no internal dharmas, the emptiness of both internal and external is likewise so.

Good son, only the Heavenly Worthy’s Dharma-disciples’ Dao-nature does not reside within the two emptinesses of internal and external. Why is this so? Such dharmas as true and constant joy are the reason the Dao-Dharma is not called empty. This is called the emptiness of both internal and external.

Good son, what is the emptiness of the conditioned? All conditioned dharmas are entirely empty, namely the internal emptiness and external emptiness. Internal emptiness is true and constant joy. The Heavenly Worthy’s Dharma-disciples’ supreme emptiness of the ultimate meaning is the Middle Way-nature, not a conditioned dharma. Therefore, the Dao-nature is not the emptiness of conditioned dharmas.

Good son, how do perfected ones and Daoists contemplate the emptiness of the unconditioned? All unconditioned dharmas are entirely empty, namely impermanence, suffering, joy, non-self, the aggregates, realms, and entrances, the marks of sentient beings, and the outflows of the conditioned. Within internal dharmas, external dharmas, and unconditioned dharmas, there is one dharma that is equal, neither conditioned nor unconditioned, neither possessing the nature of the conditioned nor the nature of the unconditioned. This is called the constant abiding. Neither internal nor external, this is called the perfected ones’ contemplation of the emptiness of the unconditioned.

How do perfected ones and Daoists contemplate beginningless emptiness? These perfected ones and Daoists see that arising and ceasing are without beginning and are entirely empty and quiescent. What is called emptiness—true and constant joy—is entirely empty and quiescent, without change. The marks of sentient beings’ lives, the Dharma-nature of the Three Treasures, and the unconditioned dharmas—this is called the perfected ones’ contemplation of beginningless emptiness.

How do perfected ones contemplate the emptiness of dharmas? These perfected ones and Daoists contemplate all dharmas as empty in their original nature, namely the aggregates, realms, and entrances as constant or inconstant, suffering or non-suffering, joyful or non-joyful, pure or impure. Contemplating all such dharmas, they do not perceive their original nature. This is called the perfected ones and Daoists’ contemplation of the emptiness of nature.

How do perfected ones and Daoists contemplate the emptiness of non-possession? Just as a person without a child says their dwelling is empty, when they thoroughly contemplate emptiness, there is no attachment to love. Foolish people say the ten directions are all empty, and impoverished people say everything is empty. Such calculations may be empty or not empty. When perfected ones contemplate, like impoverished people, everything is empty. This is called the perfected ones and Daoists’ contemplation of the emptiness of non-possession.

How do perfected ones and Daoists contemplate all as empty within the supreme Dharma? Good son, when perfected ones and Daoists contemplate the supreme state, it arises from the eye, but from where does it come? And when it ceases, where does it go? Formerly non-existent, now existent; originally existent, now non-existent. Examining its true nature, there is no eye, no master. All dharmas are likewise so.

What is called the supreme meaning? Dharmas have karma and retribution, yet no agent is seen. Such empty dharmas are called the emptiness of the supreme Dharma. This is called the perfected ones and Daoists’ contemplation of the supreme Dharma’s emptiness.

How do perfected ones and Daoists contemplate the emptiness of emptiness? Emptiness within emptiness is where lesser immortals and disciples become deluded and lost. Good son, being and non-being—this is called emptiness; emptiness being affirmation and negation—this is called the emptiness of emptiness. Good son, even the perfected ones of the three times only partially comprehend this, like a mote of dust. Good son, such emptiness of dharmas is also not the same as the emptiness of emptiness attained by lesser immortals and disciples. This is called the perfected ones and Daoists’ contemplation of the Dharma of the emptiness of emptiness.

Good son, how do perfected ones and Daoists contemplate great emptiness? Good son, this great emptiness refers to the wisdom of the heavenly eye. This is called great emptiness. Good son, when perfected ones and Daoists attain such wondrous emptiness, they abide in the Dharma-ground of the empty and equal.

Now, as I broadly expound the meanings of all emptiness in this great assembly, there are measureless and boundless perfected ones and Daoists who immediately attain abiding in the Dharma-ground of the empty and equal. Good son, when perfected ones and Daoists abide in this ground, they are without obstruction, bondage, or attachment in all dharmas, and their minds are without confusion or distress. For this reason, it is called the Dharma-ground of emptiness.

Good son, just as empty space does not generate attachment in regard to lovable forms, nor joy or anger in regard to unloved forms, so too do perfected ones and Daoists abiding in this ground remain without attachment in regard to beautiful forms.

Good son, just as empty space is vast and can contain all things, so too do perfected ones and Daoists abiding in this ground. The vast empty space can contain all dharmas. For this reason, it is also called the Dharma-ground of emptiness.

Good son, when perfected ones and Daoists abide in this vast Dharma-ground of emptiness, they see and know all wondrous dharmas—whether practices or conditions, natures or marks, causes or effects, the minds of ordinary beings, roots or origins, good-knowing advisors, good conditions, good Dharma-precepts, good acts of giving, good regulations, and all such dharmas—they know and see them all.”

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists abiding in this ground know but do not see. What is meant by *knowing*? They know of self-mortifying practices—casting oneself into water or fire, falling into deep pits, standing on one leg for long periods, enduring the five fires or covering oneself with ashes, dwelling in filth among thorns, trees, noxious grasses, or cow dung, wearing coarse cloth, eating only vegetables and grasses, begging for food and limiting themselves to one household, departing if the host says there is none, and never turning back even if called again; they know of abstaining from meat and the five worldly flavors, and of all such practices that are entirely renounced. Yet there is no instance where these can become the cause of supreme liberation—this is called *knowing*. What is meant by *not seeing*? Perfected ones and Daoists do not see anyone who practices such methods attaining true liberation—this is called *not seeing*.

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists also know what constitutes *seeing*: they see that all ordinary beings who practice such perverse methods will surely fall into hell—this is called *seeing*. What is meant by *knowing*? They know that when ordinary beings are reborn from hell into the human realm, if they cultivate the practice of giving and fulfill all the diligent practices, they will certainly enter true liberation—this is called *knowing*.

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists also both see and know. What is meant by *seeing*? They see what is constant and what is inconstant, what is suffering and what is not, what is bliss and what is not, what is pure and what is not, what is self and what is not—this is called *seeing*. What is meant by *knowing*? They know that the realization of the noble ones is never ultimately extinguished; they know that the bodies of the noble ones are indestructible like vajra, not formed by defilements, nor are they foul, decaying bodies. They also know that all beings possess the nature of the Dao—this is called *knowing*.

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists also both know and see. What is meant by *knowing*? They know which beings seek the wondrous Dharma, who is flowing with the current, who is flowing against it, and who abides in the correct place; they know which beings have reached the other shore. Those flowing with the current are ordinary people. Those flowing against it range from those who have attained non-action to all the immortals. Those who abide correctly are perfected ones and Daoists who have reached the other shore—namely, the divine penetrations and wisdom-eye of the Heavenly Worthy, the Thus-Come One of universal knowledge—this is called *knowing*. What is meant by *seeing*? Perfected ones and Daoists, abiding in the Primordial Yang world and cultivating the wondrous practices of the Great Vehicle, with the pure heavenly eye of their wondrous practice, see all ordinary beings creating unwholesome karma through body, speech, and mind, and due to these three unvirtuous acts, falling into the dark prisons of hell; they see beings who cultivate wholesome karma, who at the end of life will be reborn in the heavens or among humans; they see ordinary beings moving from darkness to darkness, from darkness to light, from light to darkness, and from light to light—this is called *knowing and seeing*.

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists also both know and see. They know that when ordinary beings cultivate bodily discipline, practice, Dharma, precepts, concentration, and wisdom, if in this life their evil karma is mature, whether due to greed, hatred, or delusion, such karma will inevitably lead to retribution in the three evil destinies. Yet through cultivating bodily discipline, practice, Dharma, precepts, concentration, and wisdom, these beings experience only minor suffering in this life and do not fall into the three evil destinies. How can such karma be met with karmic retribution in accordance with principle? By openly confessing and repenting all past karma, and after repentance, never daring to repeat it, establishing shame and remorse, making offerings to the Three Treasures, and constantly reproaching oneself—due to these causes and conditions, they do not fall into the three evil destinies but instead experience retribution in this life. Such retribution includes various illnesses, ailments, encounters with deadly misfortunes, hunger and hardship, bodily pain and suffering—these are the minor retributions experienced in this life. This is called *knowing*. What is meant by *seeing*? Perfected ones and Daoists see that those who fail to cultivate bodily discipline, Dharma, precepts, concentration, and wisdom, and commit even minor evil, due to this karmic cause, will face karmic retribution; if such a person does not repent, does not reflect or reproach themselves, feels no shame or fear, their evil karma will increase, and they will suffer retribution in the dark prisons—this is called *seeing*.

There are also cases of knowing but not seeing. What is meant by *knowing but not seeing*? They know that all ordinary beings possess the Dharma-nature, yet it is obscured by defilements and cannot be seen—this is called *knowing but not seeing*. There are also cases of knowing but seeing little. Perfected ones and Daoists know that all ordinary beings possess the Dharma-nature, yet their vision is unclear, like seeing indistinctly in the dark of night.

There are also cases of both seeing and knowing. The heavenly sages both see and know. There are also cases of both seeing and knowing, yet not seeing and not knowing. What is meant by *both seeing and knowing*? This refers to worldly matters such as written language, clothing, bedding, mats, screens, food and the five flavors, worldly treasures, and the signs of living beings—this is called *both seeing and knowing*. What is meant by *not seeing and not knowing*? The profound and wondrous meanings possessed by the sages, which are free from notions of male and female, and even gardens—this is called *not seeing and not knowing*.

There are also cases of knowing but not seeing. They know what has been given, what has been offered, who the recipients are, and the karmic fruits of cause and effect—this is called *knowing*. What is meant by *not seeing*? They do not see the acts of giving, offering, the recipients, or their karmic fruits—this is called *not seeing*.

Perfected ones and Daoists possess eight kinds of knowledge, which are known through the divine penetrations and wisdom-eye of the Primordial Heavenly Worthy. Miao Le the Perfected One addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "What benefits do perfected ones and Daoists gain from knowing in this way?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Good son, perfected ones and Daoists who know in this way attain the four unimpeded powers: unimpeded dharma, unimpeded meaning, unimpeded wisdom, and unimpeded insight.

Unimpeded dharma means knowing all dharmas and their names. Unimpeded meaning means knowing all meanings inherent in the dharmas and being able to assign meanings to the names established for each dharma. Unimpeded wisdom means being able to analyze the profound principles found in sutras and treatises. Unimpeded insight means that whenever perfected ones and Daoists expound upon matters about which immortals have doubts, there are no obstructions, and they can clarify all dharma characteristics.

Good son, this is what it means for perfected ones to know and see in this way, thereby attaining these four unimpeded dharmas.

Good son, unimpeded dharma means that perfected ones and Daoists comprehensively know the profound dharmas of the wondrous sutras of divine immortals and great beings. Unimpeded meaning means that although there are the Three Vehicles, they know they all return to the One, and there are ultimately no differences or distinctions. Unimpeded wisdom means that perfected ones and Daoists can express a single dharma in myriad names, expounding upon it through infinite kalpas across heaven and earth without exhaustion—lesser immortals and disciples cannot do this. Unimpeded insight means that perfected ones and Daoists, over infinite kalpas, expound upon the dharmas to all ordinary beings and sentient beings, whether in names or meanings, employing skillful means and varied explanations that cannot be exhausted.

Good son, unimpeded dharma means that although perfected ones and Daoists know all dharmas, they do not cling to them. Unimpeded meaning means that although they know all meanings, they do not cling to them. Unimpeded wisdom means that although they know names, they do not cling to them. Unimpeded insight means that although they know such supreme insight, they do not cling to it. Why is this? If they were to cling, they would not be called perfected ones."

Miao Le the Perfected One again addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "If they do not cling, then they do not know the dharma; if they know the dharma, then they are clinging. If they do not know clinging, then they know nothing—how then can the Heavenly Worthy say they know the dharma yet do not cling?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Clinging is not called unimpeded; only without clinging is it called unimpeded. Good son, all perfected ones who cling are not unimpeded. Those without unimpededness are not called perfected ones—they should be known as foolish. Why is clinging called foolish? All foolish beings cling to form, and even cling to consciousness because of their clinging to form. Thus, they generate greed. Because they generate greed, they are struck and defiled by form, and even by consciousness. Because they are struck and defiled, they cannot escape birth, old age, sickness, death, sorrow, affliction, great suffering, and all afflictions. Therefore, clinging is called foolish. For this reason, all foolish beings lack the four unimpeded dharmas.

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists have known and seen the characteristics of dharmas for as many kalpas as the sands of the Ganges. Because they know and see, they understand their meanings. Because they see the characteristics of dharmas and know their meanings, they do not generate clinging to form, and it is likewise with consciousness. Because they are undefiled, perfected ones do not generate clinging to form, nor do they generate clinging to consciousness. Because they are without clinging, they are not struck or defiled by form, nor are they defiled by consciousness. Thus, they can escape birth, old age, sickness, death, sorrow, great suffering, and all karmic afflictions. For this reason, all perfected ones attain unimpeded dharma.

Good son, for this reason, in the *Yuanyang Sutra* I taught my disciples that being struck and defiled is called perverse attachment, while being undefiled means liberation from perverse attachment. It is like a guilty ordinary person being bound by officials, while an innocent person cannot be seized. Perfected ones and Daoists are likewise: those with clinging and defilement are seized by perversity, while those without defilement cannot be seized by perversity. For this reason, perfected ones and Daoists are without defilement.

Good son, unimpeded dharma means that perfected ones and Daoists skillfully know expedient means without false loss. What are expedient means? They are like earth, like mountains, like eyes, like clouds, like people, like mothers—all dharmas are likewise.

Unimpeded meaning means that although perfected ones know the names of all dharmas, they do not know their meanings but attain unimpeded meaning and can understand their intent. How do they know meaning? It is like the earth, which can give rise to all grasses and trees—ordinary beings, for this reason, are called like earth.

Good son, as for being like mountains: perfected ones and Daoists cultivate and study the Dao and its dharmas, contemplating their meanings to ensure they are unshakable—for this reason, they are called like mountains. As for being like eyes: they possess various lights that illuminate and reveal all meanings—for this reason, they are called like eyes. As for being like clouds: they can provide shade and moisture to benefit all things—for this reason, they are called like clouds. As for being like people: they uphold all the wondrous meanings of the dharmas and serve as good physicians for the world, healing all illnesses—for this reason, they are called like people. As for being like mothers: they lovingly nurture their elder brothers' children with an impartial heart—for this reason, they are called like mothers.

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists know the profound meanings of all dharmas, and they are likewise.

Unimpeded expression means that perfected ones and Daoists, using the wondrous terms of the great vehicle from the *Yuanyang Sutra*, can expound upon a single phrase without doubt or difficulty, and without any fixed meaning—just as all dwellings, grasses, and trees have names.

Good son, why is there no fixed meaning? Such meanings belong to the realm of perfected ones, Daoists, and the sagely beings of heaven."

Expressions belong to the realm of ordinary beings, for they know their meanings—this is why it is called "unimpeded expression."

Unimpeded wisdom means that perfected ones and Daoists, knowing the meanings of the dharmas, can expound upon their savor for as many kalpas as the grains of sand in the Ganges, yet their principle remains inexhaustible—this is called "unimpeded wisdom."

Good son, perfected ones and Daoists cultivated the supreme-meaning dharma for kalpas long past, thus attaining the unimpeded meaning. They also cultivated the *Lingbao Dadong Zhenjing* for kalpas long past, thus attaining the unimpeded dharma. They likewise cultivated the wondrous Three Clarities for kalpas long past, gaining wisdom without doubt or difficulty.

Good son, it is impossible for any of the immortals' disciples to possess these four unimpeded powers. As I have stated in this *Yuanyang Sutra*, though the immortals' disciples are said to possess the four unimpeded powers, in truth they do not. For this reason, perfected ones and Daoists possess these four unimpeded powers to deliver ordinary beings. The immortals' disciples practice the lesser arts of immortality, aspiring to the ranks of immortals but not yet ascending to the wondrous fruit—this is why the immortals' disciples are said to possess the four unimpeded powers.

Then Miaole the Perfected and others rose from their seats, knelt with hands clasped, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Today we have heard the proclamation and fully understood the source of the Dao." At that time, all the assembled deities bowed their heads in reverence and returned to their seats.

Thus concludes *The Wondrous Yuanyang Sutra of the Numinous Treasure*, Scroll Three.

*The Wondrous Yuanyang Sutra of the Numinous Treasure*, Scroll Four
"Questions on Practice"

The disciples then rose and addressed their Master, saying: "All beings possess their respective karmic capacities, as do the various great bodhisattvas, male and female officials. As we, your disciples, reflect: though the present Sage is not the Sage-Teacher of the past, he expounds the sequential teachings, unfolding the Great Dharma of Primordial Yang’s Ascension to Immortality and elucidating the Sutra of Profound Meaning. All dharma-assemblies of holy ones—male and female officials, those bound by external affinity and those by internal affinity—we, among the male and female immortals of the past, attained great adornment, divine penetrations, and luminous clarity. We once beheld this auspicious sign, this radiant illumination, and thus the Great Dharma was proclaimed. Therefore, we now recognize that the Master manifests transformations and broadly expounds the teachings—this is the second [aspect] of divine penetration. All dharmas are likewise; thus do we disciples come to hear and know of them. For those in the world who find it difficult to believe, this auspicious sign is manifested.

Among the male and female officials, in a past kalpa—boundless, immeasurable, and inconceivable—there was a king named Great Form-Lamp, the Pure Dharma King, who transformed and manifested eighty-four thousand lands. Those lands were level and joyous, abundant with people, free of mountains, rivers, sands, stones, ravines, or pits. Their cities, with earthen mounds and hills, were walled in gold, with pools of mercury, chambers of true pearls, and sleeping quarters adorned with agate. Extending over four hundred *li*, the people were kind and virtuous.

There was a disciple named Great Dharma Grove, widely learned in all dharmas, possessed of perfect wisdom and intelligence. He transcended and ascended to the supreme state, transforming and guiding gods and humans. His teachings were unadulterated, his voice exquisite and wondrous, fully clear and complete, endowed with the marks of the five penetrations. Expounding the Dharma for benefit, he liberated and delivered beings, realizing the emptiness of all dharmas. He became a Perfected One, and together with the Six Spirit Kings, he next attained the Dao, becoming a Second-Rank Perfected One of Primordial Yang’s Upper Grade, capable of perfecting all Dao-wisdom.

Next, there was another disciple named Constant Progress and Conduct, a great bodhisattva known as Luminous and Everlasting Form. This person had been born twenty-two times in the Palace of Literary Brilliance, owing to the roots of virtue planted in past lives. His numinous wisdom was celestial, inheriting the mysterious wind of transformation. Feasting on the teachings of the wondrous Dharma, he accumulated blessings and fulfilled all merits, attaining the fruit of the Nine Heavens. Rejoicing in the blessings to come, he received the shade of the Grand Clarity, concentrating his spirit in the Celestial Palace. His merit was vast, and the numinous peaks of the true palaces bestowed their favor. The immortals’ officials extended their hands to him. Among his studies and delights was the *Purple Yang Immortal Duke’s Diagram of the Grand Clarity*, and he was designated the Seventh.

Before leaving the household life, there was a great bodhisattva, fully endowed with wisdom, whose ancestral teachings followed Purple Yang as his master. He diligently studied the Primordial Yang of divine immortals, aspiring to the ranks of immortals in the celestial charts. He could discern the initial, middle, and lesser immortals; the initial, middle, and later virtues. His understanding was profound and far-reaching in the end.

Before the immortal Perfected One left the household life, he had eight attendant disciples: the first named Radiant Grove, the second named Treasure Grove, the third named Intent Grove, the fourth named Manifest Grove, the fifth named Good Grove, the sixth named Joyful Grove, the seventh named Jeweled Grove, and the eighth named Doubt-Dispelling Grove. These individuals were renowned in the Celestial Palace as Upper-Grade Perfected Ones of Primordial Yang, fully endowed with wisdom and conduct, possessing the five divine penetrations, majestic virtue, and self-mastery, each leading gods and humans.

When he first left the household life, he meditated beneath a tree, relinquishing his high station and arousing the mind of great compassion. Resolutely, he departed. Constantly cultivating the true practice, he became an immortal elder. After ten thousand years, all the virtues he had planted came to fruition. At midnight, during the *zi* hour, he observed the Northern Dipper’s handle and the Purple Tenuity of Literary Brilliance within the Dipper’s bowl. Suddenly, it opened, and he beheld the Most High Lord Lao descending upon a blue-green dragon—below, it was a blue-green horse. He addressed the person, saying: "Who is this true worthy?"

At that time, Lord Lao replied: "I am the Little Lad Li Yuan, a Perfected One of the Eastern Sea. At the celestial assembly’s celebration, I was sent down to transform you, Grove Bodhisattva. Later, you will expound the *Sutra of Boundless Meaning*, unfolding the second [teaching] of Primordial Yang’s divine immortals. Heavenly flowers rained upon him, universally transforming the world with manifold tremors."

At that time, among the assembly was a Perfected One, twelve years of age, who rose and addressed the Master, saying: "As for our great assembly, we have never before seen such joy and delight. Kneeling with focused mind, we behold the teachings expounded by the Master—excellent words, exquisite and wondrous, skillful in analogy and expedient means. Radiant illumination shines universally, illuminating all, enabling this assembly to awaken and become enlightened. The cause and condition of this illumination reveal the Upper Grade of Primordial Yang, the Great Rank of Immortals and Sages, the realm of gods and humans. That land is pure, never before seen. Thus, for hundreds of thousands of years, beings will forever abide in great blessings."

Perfected One Serene Grove of the Dharma said: "Since my Master expounded the Upper Grade of Primordial Yang, sixty minor kalpas have passed without his rising from his seat. Now, he wishes to gather responses and return to his origin. On the seventh day of the first month, he will return to the Celestial Palace to celebrate with the gods and humans. If, after my departure, there are one or two, or even ten among you who can propagate the wondrous Dharma and exhort beings, all shall be reborn in the ranks of Primordial Yang. Do not grow weary or indolent. For sixty minor kalpas, gods and humans shall share the same rank, receiving the prediction with one mind."

He then addressed the great bodhisattvas, saying: "Having received the words of Perfected One Serene Grove of the Dharma, we shall now celebrate with the gods and humans." After his departure, Wondrous Grove of Primordial Yang and Radiant Grove of Light attained the five penetrations and the wisdom of a divine immortal with vast knowledge. Skillful and sharp in scriptural predictions, they gained pure wisdom, awakened beings, and were named Pure Wisdom. When Perfected One Deliverance bestowed the prediction, on the seventh day of the first month in the *renchen* year, he suddenly departed.

Perfected One Grove of Primordial Yang’s Pure Wisdom was born in the palace of the Profound and Wondrous King. His ancestors had accumulated practices, diligently cultivating reverent mindfulness, delighting in the study of true scriptures, and constantly practicing the records of immortals. His ancestral teachings followed the Primordial One’s Celestial Palace. He studied the *Eight Hundred Scrolls of the Primordial One’s Immortal Canon*, which broadly expounded the teachings and transformed and delivered beings."

Mystic Grove expounded the *Eight Thousand Scrolls of the Immortal Records*, remaining seated without rising for eighty minor kalpas, discoursing for others. He had eight disciples: the first named Radiant Grove, the second named Mystic Grove, the third named Teaching Grove, the fourth named Unshakable Grove, the fifth named Lamp-Incense Grove, the sixth named Joyful Grove, the seventh named Deliverance Grove, and the eighth named Transformation Grove. These eight disciples all possessed luminous conduct and were the third-rank disciples of the Upper Grade of Primordial Yang. They dwelled beneath terraces, pavilions, gardens, fields, vast groves, and trees.

Among those who attained the rank of immortality was one named Perfected One Ancestral Sovereign, who sought to remain at his side, reciting scriptures with fluency, broadly expounding the various sutras, and proclaiming the supreme ranks. In the past, amidst a great assembly spanning sixty minor kalpas, his followers revered and respected him as he expounded the teachings to deliver countless beings, guiding them into the Upper Grade of Primordial Yang.

When he first left the household life, he had three disciples who beheld the divine and greatly sagely ones, with all immortals following in attendance. They expounded the boundless varieties of meaning within this sutra. The immortals and devas of all heavens were to broadly distinguish them. At that moment when I spoke, I was seated in the void of the heavens above, observing from on high for eighty minor kalpas as you broadly discoursed, ascending into the boundless ranks.

Celestial incense and jeweled canopies, dragon immortals and deva-kings made offerings among humans. All the immortals of the world adorned and purified the land, which was smooth as fat, with many jeweled trees. It was named the Palace of the Lion and Elephant Kings. At that moment, the various celestial and human divine sounds shook Perfected One Deliverance of Pure Wisdom, who emitted the light of spiritual penetrations. He beheld all the rare and wondrous signs and saw all the people of that land.
