That land was pure, with mother-of-pearl for earth, yellow gold for its walls, white silver for its ramparts, lapis lazuli for its chambers, and yellow, azure, and crimson cords interwoven throughout. Agate bordered its sides, crystal formed its palaces, and white jade its towers. Everywhere were walking trees, gardens, groves, terraces, pavilions, and pure lotus ponds, with luxuriant flowers and fruits. All beings reveled in bliss within it. Extending continuously for over four thousand *li*, celestial light universally illumined it. Adorned with manifold treasures, lapis lazuli and glass were radiant within and without, not relying on the sun or moon.

The immortals prepared offerings of delicacies and food, with natural celestial kitchens and utensils. There, the foremost in purity among the devas emerged riding cloud chariots, drawn by dragon spirits and divine tigers, with soaring phoenixes singing. Bells hung on all four sides, and blessings were bestowed in the eight directions. Natural music arose, and their bodies shone with light like golden treasure mountains, majestic and wondrous as pure lapis lazuli, perfect within and without.

Next was a great being named Perfected One Discerning Wisdom Who Delivers from Calamity. All his disciples ascended to the heavens and the palaces of the Primordial One, delivering countless beings. Through my light, they flew with self-mastery, beholding all the immortals of the great assembly, the mountain-forest *mahāsattvas* of diligent progress, those who upheld the precepts in accord with the tally, and the wondrous numinous ranks of immortals, like bright pearls.

One disciple was named Serene Mystic Grove. He constantly cultivated practice in the mountains and forests, diligently upholding the precepts, with pure conduct, generosity, forbearance, and the immortal ranks of Primordial Yang. Another disciple was named Great Treasury of Wisdom, who entered the profound and wondrous samādhi, with body and mind quiescent and extinguished, possessing vast wisdom, samādhi, and insight.

The next disciple was named Mystic Brahma Grove, whose wisdom and dharma were profoundly vast and quiescent, with unmoving spiritual wisdom. Each discoursed on the supreme ranks in their respective lands. The next disciple was named Great Brahma Grove, who manifested great spiritual penetrations, his mind filled with joy. The four groups of disciples broadly expounded the teachings, each inquiring of one another about the immortal ranks of Primordial Yang.

The next disciple was named Contemplative Brahma Grove, who delighted in the supreme Dao and was revered by devas and humans, foremost in the three realms, able to praise all immortals as rare in the world. The next disciple was named True Mystic Sound, who broadly knew all things. Devas and humans turned toward him, taking refuge and placing trust in his great practices, able to uphold the supreme undertaking.

The next disciple was named Treasure Mystery Grove, whose mysterious wisdom was like empty space, illuminating the immortal records. He often praised yin and yang, broadly expounding the teachings, celebrating the assembly of devas and humans, and wondrously delivering the world. The next disciple was named Profound Wisdom, who possessed the five spiritual penetrations. After eighty minor kalpas, he could open the world’s teachings without rising from his seat. What he discoursed was of the supreme rank, subtle and unfathomable, and he was named Moonlight Supreme Immortal Master.

The next disciple was named Treasure Mystic Grove, who delighted both devas and humans. The true characteristics of all dharmas have already been expounded to you, including their length and brevity. On the fifth day of the tenth month, I shall return to the celestial palace. He addressed his disciples, saying: "You must single-mindedly cultivate diligent progress and ascend to the celestial palaces, where you shall be named the Heavenly People of Grand Purity."

All these disciples were of the immortal ranks of Primordial Yang, with unhindered spiritual penetrations. When Perfected One Deliverance of Pure Wisdom had finished speaking, he addressed his disciples, saying: "Since I and you have severed the immortal records, what barrier remains to the celestial palace of celebration?"

On the fifth day of the tenth month, I shall return to the celestial palace. The celestial command is most urgent, and this auspicious assembly is extraordinary. Thereupon, on the fifteenth day of this month at noon, the Perfected One, together with all the immortals, departed in cloud chariots and feathered canopies, attended by eighty million people, flying immortals, and celestial immortals—boundless holy multitudes—riding away.

The Heavenly People of Primordial Yang Deliverance of Grand Purity arose from the Palace of the Unattached King, traversing the three worlds in peace and tranquility. He addressed his disciples, saying: "I have received the profoundly deep wisdom of the Perfected Ones, boundless wisdom, and the gate of wisdom that sees arising. The five spirits are resplendent and bright, and the faculties are keen, benefiting all beings.

All the world finds it difficult to comprehend, difficult to fathom, and difficult to enter—something devas and humans cannot attain. Why is this so? I have personally drawn near to hundreds of thousands of myriads of billions of countless Perfected Ones and great beings, fully practicing the boundless great Dao, with courageous and diligent progress. My fame is universally heard, and my accomplishments are most profound. I have attained the rare dharma. The immortal officials of the Celestial Charts of Mount Ling bestowed the dharma, descending to transform the three realms, guiding and instructing as appropriate."

Since attaining the rank of Perfected One, through manifold causes and conditions, manifold analogies, I have broadly expounded the teachings in countless skillful means, guiding beings to depart from all attachments. Why is this so? My skillful means and insight are profound and far-reaching, all fully equipping the people of the world.

My Most High Former Master’s wisdom is vast, deep, and boundless, fearless and unobstructed. With a settled mind and liberation, he deeply entered the secret treasury, his insight without limit. He accomplished all unprecedented dharmas, ascending to the Celestial Palace as a Great Perfected One of the Supreme Primordial Yang, foremost among the sublime immortal charts. The precious scriptures, in manifold forms, distinguish and expound the dharmas with skillful speech, their words gentle and pleasing to the hearts of all. The people of the world, taking the essential teachings I have spoken, without limit, and upholding what I have taught, all attain accomplishment—unthinkable and inconceivable.

You need not speak further of this. Why? What I have accomplished is subtly wondrous and foremost, its meaning and purport difficult to comprehend. Only my supreme master can discern it. The profound mysteries of all dharmas cannot be fully fathomed.

I now possess such marks, such nature, such essence, such power, such activity, such conditions, such causes, such effects, such retributions, such origins and conclusions—all perfectly and ultimately realized.

At that time, the devas bestowed prediction upon faithful men and women of good conduct, causing all to hear and know, and all to awaken.

Then the youngest son of the Heavenly Elder, Mysterious Purity King, who first emerged from the Palace of Comforting Fields, took the Great Treasure as supreme in his ancestral teachings. What he cultivated were the eight thousand scrolls of the *Taiqing* scriptures. He could broadly expound the teachings for sixty minor kalpas without rising from his seat. Originally from countless [practices], he fulfilled all conduct—profound, wondrous, difficult to perceive, difficult to comprehend.

He had three chief disciples: the first named Mysterious Wonder Perfected One, the second named Proof of Fruit Perfected One, and the third named Luminous Wisdom Perfected One. These disciples possessed great sagely conduct and could expound the Primordial Yang immortal ranks for a thousand days and nights without rising from their seats.

Another disciple, named True Brahmā Grove, had keen faculties, profound subtlety, and practiced these ranks to attain fruition. I fully know such great fruition and the merits of Primordial Yang.

Another disciple, named Great Brahmā Grove, through manifold skillful means, could transform and instruct all beings of the ten directions, awakening those in darkness.

Another disciple, named True Purity Grove, possessed wisdom and unshakable faith. All these disciples, their afflictions exhausted, abided in their final state and ascended to the Celestial Palace of the Most High, each dwelling in their proper rank.

Thus concludes Scroll Four of the *Most High Numinous Treasure Primordial Yang Wondrous Scripture*.

---

**Scroll Five of the *Most High Numinous Treasure Primordial Yang Wondrous Scripture*: The Chapter on Contemplation and Practice (Part One)**

At that time, the Most August Heavenly Worthy of Jade Treasure of the Eastern Quarter, in the Pure Land of the Empty Song Realm, together with his divine immortals and retinue, flying celestial spirit-kings, perfected and greatly sagely hosts—eighty-four thousand companions in all—assembled amidst the fragrant groves and seven-jeweled trees. There he expounded the *Supreme Wondrous Scripture of Primordial Yang on Contemplation and Practice*, creating a vast field of merit for all future beings, dispelling deep doubts and enabling them to know the wondrous Dao.

“Good man, you should arouse the mind of aspiration and vow, and follow the four kinds of practices for cultivation.”

When these words were spoken, from among the assembly there arose a perfected one named Numinous Flower. Adjusting his robes and cap, he held a censer in hand and, kneeling at length, addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “By past causes, I have been fortunate to encounter your majestic radiance, and my joy surpasses all bounds—yet I am truly ashamed and awestruck. Now, having heard the profound and secret treasury of Primordial Yang expounded, its meaning runs so deep as to be inconceivable. How is this so?”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Good man, the four kinds of practices for cultivation are these: first, to follow a teacher and receive the scriptures of Primordial Yang; second, to seek out good spiritual friends to resolve deep doubts; third, to contemplate the profound meaning and attain the dharma of suffering and emptiness; fourth, to cultivate practice with diligence and aspire to realize the Dao.

“Good man, you should know that these four practices involve drawing near to an enlightened teacher, seeking out spiritual friends, requesting the explanation of profound meaning, and resolving doubts. Perfected One, you should understand these four kinds of practices for cultivation.

“Furthermore, good man, the actions of body, speech, and mind give rise to four kinds of delusion. What are these four? First, delusion of greed; second, delusion of ignorance; third, delusion of lust; fourth, delusion of deceit.

“Good man, those who study the Mahāyāna scriptures and seek the natural fruit should abandon these four kinds of delusive practices. What is the delusion of greed? It refers to coveting, beyond one’s proper share, worldly glory, fine clothing, rare treasures, and all manner of scheming and calculation—killing living beings, harming their lives, indulging one’s desires, and gluttonously devouring. Such things are called the delusion of greed.

“What is the delusion of ignorance? It refers to the transgressions of body, speech, and mind—failing to avoid the Three Luminaries (sun, moon, and stars), disrespecting the Three Treasures, and when encountering those who follow the Dao, hearing of their good deeds yet seeking to undermine them, spreading slander, scheming against elders and teachers, and when summoned, evading and refusing to comply. Such things are called the delusion of ignorance.

“What is the delusion of lust? It refers to delighting in feminine beauty without regard for kinship or propriety, seducing the wives and concubines of others, harboring secret schemes, covertly luring and enticing, separating people from their kin, and indulging without restraint. Such things are called the delusion of lust.

“What is the delusion of deceit? It refers to harboring false and flattering intentions, weaving countless deceptions, exploiting public office for private gain, covertly wielding power, posing as a renunciate while deceiving beings, seizing others’ wealth under the pretense of possessing the Dao, and lacking any true reality. Such things are called the delusion of deceit.

“Good man, if you earnestly seek the supreme natural fruit, Perfected One, you should know that these four evil delusions must all be severed.

“Furthermore, good man, there are two kinds of faith: first, faith of the utmost sincerity; second, faith lacking sincerity. Perfected One, you should know that sincere faith is good, while insincere faith is not called good.

“Moreover, faith has two aspects: first, constantly attending the Dharma seat; second, not attending the Dharma seat. Perfected One, you should know that those who constantly attend the Dharma seat are good, while those who do not are not called good.

“Among those who attend the Dharma seat, there are two kinds: first, those who pay homage; second, those who do not pay homage. Perfected One, you should know that those who pay homage are good, while those who do not are not called good.

“Among those who pay homage, there are two kinds: first, those who listen to the Dharma with utmost sincerity; second, those who do not listen with utmost sincerity. Perfected One, you should know that those who listen with utmost sincerity are good, while those who do not are not called good.

“Perfected One, you should know that among those who listen to the Dharma with utmost sincerity, there are two kinds: first, those who contemplate and seek its meaning; second, those who do not contemplate and seek its meaning. Perfected One, you should know that those who contemplate and seek its meaning are good, while those who do not are not called good.

“Among those who contemplate and seek its meaning, there are two kinds: first, those who practice as taught; second, those who do not practice as taught. Practicing as taught is good, while not practicing as taught is not called good.

“Among those who practice as taught, there are two kinds: first, those who possess great wisdom and can benefit all beings; second, those who possess great wisdom yet cannot benefit all beings. Those who can benefit all beings are good, while those who cannot are not called good.

“Perfected Youth, you should know that benefiting beings brings peace, joy, and the natural fruition of karmic reward.

“Good man, among all treasures, the luminous moon-pearl is the most sublime; among all flavors, the sweet dew nectar is the most sublime. Perfected One, if you can expound the meaning of the Primordial Yang scripture among humans and devas, benefiting all beings, this is the most sublime—beyond all comparison.

“Good man, this is called the Perfected Youth abiding in the nine dharmas of the Mahāyāna, the pure and unconditioned. Perfected Youth, abiding in these nine virtues, you will truly attain contemplation and practice.

“Furthermore, good man, the mind of contemplation and practice consists of the four immeasurables: kindness, compassion, joy, and equanimity.”

The Perfected One Numinous Flower knelt at length and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “If abundant kindness can sever anger, and cultivating compassion can also sever anger, why then speak of the four immeasurable minds? Logically, it should be three.”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Kindness has three conditions: first, conditioned by beings; second, conditioned by the Dharma; third, unconditioned.”

Compassion, joy, and equanimity are likewise the same. If one examines their intent, there should logically be only one, not four.

That which is conditioned by beings is conditioned by the five aggregates, wishing to bestow happiness upon them—this is called the Dharma conditioned by beings. The so-called conditioning here means providing all the necessities that beings require—this is called the Dharma-conditioned.

The unconditioned is conditioned by the Heavenly Worthy—this is called the unconditioned.

Kindness is often conditioned. For impoverished beings, the Heavenly Worthy, the Great Master, forever severs their poverty and grants them the foremost joy. If conditioned by beings, one does not condition by the Dao; the same applies to the Dharma. For this reason, that which is conditioned by the Heavenly Worthy is called the unconditioned Heavenly Worthy.

The objects of kindness are all beings, such as parents, siblings, spouses, and kin—hence it is called the being-conditioned. The Dharma-conditioned does not perceive parents, siblings, spouses, or kin, but sees all beings as arising from conditions—this is called the Dharma-conditioned. The unconditioned does not abide in the marks of Dharma or beings—this is called the unconditioned. Compassion, joy, and equanimity are likewise the same. Thus, there should be three, not four.

The Heavenly Worthy said: “People are of two kinds: those who act from insight and those who act from attachment. Those who act from insight often cultivate kindness and compassion; those who act from attachment often cultivate joy and equanimity. Thus, there should be two, not four.”

The Heavenly Worthy said: “The immeasurable is called boundless because its bounds cannot be reached. If it is called immeasurable, it should be one, not four. If there are four, how can it be immeasurable? Thus, it should be one, not four.”

The Heavenly Worthy addressed Perfected Youth Numinous Flower: “Good man, when the sages of the heavens expound the essential Dharma for beings, their words are profound and secret—only you may understand. Sometimes they speak of one condition, such as all conditioned dharmas. Good man, sometimes they speak of two: cause and effect; or three: afflictions, karma, and suffering; or four: ignorance, volitional formations, birth, and old age; or five: feeling, grasping, existence, birth, and so on; or six: the causes and effects of the three times; or seven: consciousness, name-and-form, the six sense bases, contact, feeling, craving, and grasping; or eight: origin, clarity, volition, birth, old age, death, and the other eight matters; or nine: birth, old age, sickness, and death.

“Good man, for the sake of beings, these causes and conditions are variously distinguished. The immeasurable minds are likewise the same. Good man, for this reason, you should not doubt the profound and secret practices of the Heavenly Worthies. Good man, the Heavenly Worthy possesses great skillful means, teaching and transforming beings with meticulous care, enabling all to deeply comprehend the nature of the Dharma, dispel doubts, speak of suffering where there is no suffering, speak of joy where there is no joy, speak of cause where there is no cause, speak of effect where there is no effect, speak of the real where there is no real, expound the Dharma where there is no Dharma, speak of immortals where there are no immortals, and discourse on the Dao where there is no Dao.

“Good man, does the Heavenly Worthy employ such boundless skillful means to tame and transform beings in vain? Good man, if there are beings attached to wealth and treasure, I manifest myself to them as a wealthy elder, supplying all their needs for countless eons before teaching and transforming them, enabling them to awaken to the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao. If there are beings attached to the five desires, for countless eons I fulfill their desires before exhorting them to abide in the unconditioned realm, awakening them to the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao. If there are beings who pride themselves on their nobility, for countless eons I serve as their attendant, running errands and waiting upon them until their hearts are won over, then exhorting them to abide in the unconditioned realm, illuminating the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao.

“If there are ordinary beings whose minds are cruel and who commit evil deeds, requiring admonishment, for countless eons I teach, admonish, and console them, pacifying their hearts before exhorting them to enter the pure realm, awakening their understanding of the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao. Good man, does the Heavenly Worthy employ such boundless skillful means over countless eons to guide beings into the pure realm and cultivate the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao in vain? Though the sages dwell in defilement, they remain unstained, like a bright pearl in the sand or a lotus in muddy water.

“Good man, you should understand that the meaning of the four immeasurables is the immeasurable mind. As you said, kindness severs anger, and compassion also severs anger. Why is this? Good man, suffering is of two kinds: one that takes life, and one that inflicts lashes. Cultivating kindness severs the former; cultivating compassion removes the latter. Good man, for this reason, is it not the severing of anger?

“Furthermore, anger is of two kinds: anger toward beings and anger toward non-beings. Cultivating kindness severs anger toward beings; cultivating compassion severs anger toward non-beings. Furthermore, anger is of two kinds: that with a cause and that without a cause. Cultivating kindness severs anger with a cause; cultivating compassion severs anger without a cause. Furthermore, anger is of two kinds: that accumulated long in the past and that newly accumulated in the present. Cultivating kindness severs the past; cultivating compassion severs the present.”

Furthermore, anger is of two kinds: anger toward sages and anger toward ordinary beings. Cultivating kindness severs anger toward sages; cultivating compassion severs anger toward ordinary beings. Furthermore, anger is of two kinds: that which is superior and that which is middling. Cultivating kindness severs the superior; cultivating compassion severs the middling. Good man, for this reason, it is called the Four. Why is it difficult to speak of? It should be three, not four—this is why. The Perfected One of Numinous Flower is of boundless mind, and by analogy and contrast, distinguishes them as four. Moreover, by the nature of the vessel, it should be called the Four. If there were only kindness, there could be no compassion, joy, or equanimity—thus, it must be four and not fewer.

Good man, by the distinction of practice, there should be four. When practicing kindness, there is no compassion, joy, or equanimity—this is why. Good man, by its boundlessness, it is also called the Four Immeasurables. The Four Immeasurables are of four kinds: boundless mind with an object but not mastery; boundless mind with mastery but not an object; boundless mind with both object and mastery; and boundless mind with neither object nor mastery.

What is the boundless mind with an object but not mastery? When one contemplates boundless, limitless beings but cannot attain mastery, though one may partially realize the true and be tainted by dharmas, one may or may not succeed. What is the boundless mind with mastery but not an object? Such as when one contemplates parents, siblings, sisters, wives, and children, desiring to bring them boundless happiness. What is the boundless mind with both object and mastery? It refers to the sages and deities. What is the boundless mind with neither object nor mastery? Late learners of the Dharma, unable to broadly contemplate boundless beings, also lack mastery.

Good man, for this reason, it is called the Four Immeasurables. This is not known by late learners of the Dharma but is the realm of sages and deities. Good man, in these four matters, though late learners of the Dharma may call them boundless, they are too few to speak of; only sages and deities can truly be called boundless and limitless.

The Perfected One of Numinous Flower addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "So it is, so it is. Truly, as the Sage has said, the realm of sages and deities is beyond the reach of late learners of the Dharma. Heavenly Venerable, are there Perfected Ones abiding in the *Great Vehicle Primordial Yang Sutra* who attain the mind of kindness and compassion but not the mind of great kindness and great compassion?"

The Heavenly Venerable replied: "There are. Good man, if a Perfected One among the multitude distinguishes three grades: first, the beloved; second, the hostile; and third, the neutral. Among the beloved, there are further three grades: superior, middling, and inferior—and the same for the hostile. The Perfected One, as a novice, grants the highest joy to the superior beloved, equal joy to the middling and inferior beloved, and the highest joy to the superior hostile. To the middling hostile, they grant middling joy; to the inferior hostile, they grant the highest joy.

The Perfected One thus transforms hostility, practicing to grant middling joy to the superior hostile and equal highest joy to the middling and inferior hostile. Further practicing, they grant the highest joy equally to the superior and middling. When they grant the highest joy to the superior hostile, they are then called 'kindness' and have attained the Perfected One’s accomplishment. At that time, their mind toward good parents and the superior hostile becomes equal, without distinction.

Good man, this is called attaining kindness and compassion—great kindness. Heavenly Venerable, why does the Perfected One attain such kindness yet still not merit the name of great kindness and great compassion?"

"Good man, because it is difficult to perfect, it is not called great kindness. Why? In the past, over countless eons, they accumulated afflictions and did not cultivate wholesome dharmas, so they cannot, in a single day, subdue their mind, attain steadfastness, and be free from slackening. Good man, the mind of affliction is stubborn and hard to remove; the mind of the true Dao is light and easily lost. Like a household dog that fears no one, or a wild deer in the mountains that flees in terror at the sight of humans: anger is hard to remove, like a guard dog; kindness is easily lost, like a wild deer. Thus, this mind is difficult to subdue. For this reason, it is not called great kindness.

Furthermore, good man, it is like painting on stone—its marks endure; painting on water vanishes instantly, impossible to retain. Anger is hard to remove, like painting on stone; wholesome roots are easily lost, like painting on water. Thus, this mind is difficult to subdue. Like a great fire that burns long and bright, while lightning’s brilliance is fleeting: the fire of anger endures, while kindness is like lightning. Thus, this mind is difficult to subdue. For this reason, it is not called great kindness.

Good man, when a Perfected One novice abides in the true ground, it is called great kindness. Why? Good man, the most extreme evil is called wrong view. When one first abides in the true ground and cultivates great kindness, even when entertaining wrong views, the mind remains undifferentiated, seeing no fault and generating no anger. For this reason, it is called great kindness. Good man, removing what is unbeneficial for the foolish multitude is called great kindness. Desiring to bring boundless benefit and happiness to the foolish multitude is called great compassion. Rejoicing in the hearts of the foolish multitude is called great joy. Being without attachment is called great equanimity. Seeing no distinction between self, dharmas, and others, perceiving all dharmas as equal and undivided—this is called great joy. Forsaking self and others, delighting in giving to others—this is called great joy and equanimity.

Good man, only the Four Immeasurables enable a Perfected One to grow, perfecting the four deportments; other practices cannot necessarily do so. Good man, a Perfected One novice first attains the Four Immeasurable Minds, then arouses the mind of the unsurpassed, correct, and true great Dao, and only then, in due order, attains the supramundane."

Good man, through the immeasurable of the world one attains the supramundane; because of this meaning, it is called the Great Immeasurable.

The Perfected One of Numinous Flower addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Apart from those who confer no benefit and those who confer benefit and happiness, there is truly nothing to be done. To contemplate thus is but an empty observation, devoid of true benefit.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like when a Daoist contemplates impurity: seeing the garments one wears as all being of skin, yet in truth not skin; seeing what one eats as all being of worms, yet in truth not worms. Observing fine and beautiful broth as excrement and filthy liquid, yet in truth not excrement; observing the milk and cheese one eats as marrow and brains, yet not marrow and brains; observing crushed grain as powder, yet in truth not powder.

The Four Immeasurable Minds are likewise. If they cannot truly benefit sentient beings and enable them to attain happiness, though one may speak of conferring happiness upon sentient beings, in truth they do not attain it. Is not such contemplation false and deceptive?

Heavenly Worthy, if it were not false and illusory, and truly conferred happiness, why then do all sentient beings not, by the power of the devas and sages, receive happiness in all things? If it is truly real yet they do not attain happiness, as the Heavenly Worthy has said: 'I recall in the past, having cultivated only the Sutra of the Mind of Compassion, this kalpa’s world has undergone a hundred cycles of formation and destruction, and I have not been reborn here. When the world is formed, I am born in the Dragon-Transformed Brahmā Heaven; when the world is destroyed, I am born in the Heaven of the Great Ultimate and Equal Nurturance.'

If there are sentient beings who can arouse the mind of the Dao toward me and cultivate only compassion, they too may attain such human and heavenly rewards. If this were not real, how could it accord with this meaning?"

The Heavenly Worthy said: "Excellent, excellent! Good man, you are truly courageous and fearless." Then, for the Perfected One of Numinous Flower, he spoke these verses:

"One who can clearly discern the marks of dharmas,
And does not arouse the mind of the three poisons,
Whose actions are equal and impartial—
Such a one can proclaim the wondrous sound.

All the men and women of the world
Should do so with a pure and divine mind.
This is called the Chapter on Contemplation and Practice,
Attaining the fruit and meeting in the Forest of Fragrance.

At dawn, all Daoists,
Proficient in the precepts and skilled in profound mysteries,
Gracefully ascend the Purple Tenuity,
The serene peaks of the Jade Capital.

If one can embody the true and real,
One must seek the profound meaning.
At the six hours, constantly recite,
At the eight festivals, ever chant and sing.

Common folk and sentient beings,
Should cease killing, stealing, and sexual misconduct.
When the karma of body, speech, and mind is exhausted,
Evil spirits cannot invade.

All good causes and effects
Arise from the reverence of vows.
I now speak these verses
To awaken those sunk in delusion.

The ambrosial flavor of the sages,
The wondrous nectar poured at will.
The immortal’s intent serves the Dharma-robe,
The jade maidens adorn the divine hairpin.

The esoteric verses of Primordial Yang,
Like the five-stringed lute in harmony.
If you can discern the essential,
Your body will be purified as yellow gold."

"Good man, those who cultivate great compassion do so not in vain imagination, for this is the true and real principle. If it is a lesser immortal or a beginner in learning, it is called false and illusory; the devas and sages are true and not false.

How is this known? Good man, when a Perfected One novice cultivates this Supreme Vehicle Sutra of Primordial Yang, observing earth as gold, gold as earth; earth as the appearance of water, water as the appearance of earth; water as the appearance of fire, fire as the appearance of water; earth as the appearance of wind, wind as the appearance of earth; the conditioned as the unconditioned, the true as the provisional; the real as emptiness—whatever the mind conceives is without falsehood.

Observing sentient beings as not being sentient beings, observing non-sentient beings as true sentient beings—whatever the mind conceives is without falsehood.

Good man, you should know that the Four Immeasurable Minds of a Perfected One novice are both true and real, and not true and real.

Furthermore, good man, what is called true and subtle contemplation? It means being able to sever the net of doubt and still all afflictions. Good man, one who cultivates the mind of compassion can sever craving; one who cultivates the mind of悲 can sever hatred; one who cultivates the mind of joy can sever discontent; one who cultivates the mind of equanimity can sever craving, hatred, and the marks of sentient beings. For this reason, it is called the true and real meaning.

Furthermore, good man, when a Perfected One cultivates the Four Immeasurable Minds, they become the root of all good qualities.

Good man, if a Perfected One novice does not see impoverished sentient beings, there is no cause to arouse compassion; without compassion, one cannot arouse the mind of generous giving. Through this cause and condition, one enables all ordinary beings to attain peace and happiness—such as food and drink, vehicles, clothing, incense and flowers, beds and seats, sleeping mats, various treasures and playthings, various sweet fruits, various patterned silks, and various brocades.

When giving thus, the mind is without regret or stinginess, without arising attachment, and one definitely dedicates it to the unsurpassed, correct, and true great Dao. At that time, the mind has no reliance, delusive thoughts are forever severed, and one does not act for fear, fame, profit, or the pleasures received in the human and heavenly realms. One does not give rise to arrogance, nor expect repayment. Not deceiving others, one practices giving; not seeking reward, when giving, one does not see a recipient.

Whether upholding or transgressing the Dharma, whether by this or not—this is a good spiritual friend. When giving thus, one does not select days or choose times, but gives with a straightforward mind, without regret or remorse. One does not consider whether the recipient is hungry or full, poor or prosperous, nor sees cause and effect. This is an ordinary being, this is not an ordinary being; this is merit, this is not merit.

Though one does not see the giver, the recipient, or the clothing and goods—even to the point of not seeing severance or karmic reward—one constantly practices giving without interruption.

Good man, if a Perfected One sees upholding or transgressing the Dharma, or even karmic reward, they will be unable to give. If one does not relinquish and let go, one will not perfect the natural fruit; if one does not perfect the natural fruit, one cannot accomplish the unsurpassed, correct, and true great Dao."

Good man, it is like a man struck by a poisoned arrow. His kin, wishing him well and to remove the poison, summon a skilled physician to extract the arrow. Yet the man says, "Wait, do not remove it. I must first observe from which direction this poisoned arrow came, who shot it, whether it was an enemy or a malevolent spirit, or if it arose naturally." Such a foolish man, unable to know these things, soon dies.

Good man, the Perfected One is likewise: if, when practicing giving, one discriminates the recipient—whether they uphold or transgress the Dharma, or even karmic reward—one will be unable to give. If one cannot give, one will not perfect the natural fruit; if one does not perfect the natural fruit, one cannot accomplish the unsurpassed, correct, and true great Dao.

Furthermore, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving and scattering, toward all ordinary beings, he maintains a mind of compassion and equality, regarding them as his own children. When giving, he arouses thoughts of loving-kindness toward all ordinary beings. Just as parents gaze upon their sick child, when he practices giving and scattering, his mind rejoices. Like parents seeing their child’s illness cured, after giving and scattering, his mind relinquishes. Like parents seeing their child grown and able to sustain himself, such is the mind of the Perfected One’s youth.

When practicing giving with a mind of compassion, offering food, he constantly thinks: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." For this reason, he enables all ordinary beings to obtain the food of great wisdom, diligently dedicating it to the unsurpassed Mahāyāna *Yuanyang Sublime Sutra*. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings, with a single thought of equality, obtain the food of good wisdom, not seeking to beg from the noble, wealthy, or prosperous. May all ordinary beings obtain my food, not seeking other food. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings attain natural food, all becoming satiated, unimpeded in their uptake, and increasing in good roots. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings comprehend the emptiness of characteristics, attain an unimpeded body like empty space. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings always be recipients, cherishing all, serving as fields of merit.

Good man, when the Perfected One’s youth cultivates a mind of compassion, for all food he gives, he should firmly generate such vows of the unsurpassed, correct, and true equality.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering drink, he constantly makes this vow: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." For this reason, he enables all ordinary beings to enter the river of the Mahāyāna, drink the eight kinds of flavored water, swiftly awaken to the unsurpassed, correct, and true Dao, leave behind all doubts and obstructions, sever afflictive karma, thirst for the flavor of the Dharma, delight in the Mahāyāna *Yuanyang* scriptures, perfect the Dharma-body, attain the treasury of all dharmas, and enter the profound ocean of wisdom. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings obtain the water of ambrosia, drink the flavor of sweet springs, and with the arising of the true Dao, all attain purity in such dharmas. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings perfect the immeasurable hundreds of thousands of Dharma-flavors; having perfected the Dharma-flavors, may they see the nature of the Dao; having seen the nature of the Dao, may they rain the rain of the Dharma; having rained the rain of the Dharma, may the Dao and Dharma pervade all, like empty space. May the remaining immeasurable sentient beings attain the single flavor of the Dharma—the Mahāyāna—not the flavors of heterodox views. The various kinds of sentient beings differ, not the flavor of goodness.

Good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering drink, he should firmly generate such natural vows.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering fine clothing, brocades, vehicles, and bedding, he constantly makes this vow: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." Through this cause and condition, may all ordinary beings accomplish, abide in, never retreat from, and remain unshaken in the fruit of the Mahāyāna *Yuanyang*. Good man, when practicing giving with a mind of compassion, offering fine clothing, brocades, vehicles, and bedding, he should always firmly generate such vows.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering clothing, he constantly makes this vow: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." Through this cause and condition, may all ordinary beings and all sentient beings obtain the clothing of shame and modesty, their bodies covered by the Dharma-realm, tearing apart heterodox views, their clothing leaving their bodies, attaining pure bodies. May all that they receive be purely good and unimpeded, their complexions warm and moist, their skin soft, perpetually radiant and without color. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings attain bodies without color, transcending all colored realms, and enter the secret treasury of the great Mahāyāna without color.

Good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering clothing, he should think thus and firmly generate such natural vows.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering fragrant incense of a hundred harmonies, he constantly makes this vow: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." Through this cause and condition, may all ordinary beings and all sentient beings, upon smelling its fragrance, all awaken to the Dao. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings become like the bright moon, all that they see being supremely subtle and wondrous. May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings attain all the myriad adornments of goodness.

May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings see whatever pleasing forms they desire.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings always encounter noble friends, obtain unobstructed fragrance, and be free from all foul odors.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings possess all virtuous deeds and the supreme, precious treasure.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings know harmony and joy, be free from sorrow and affliction, all awaken to the suffering and emptiness of existence, and have no attachments of love.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings uphold the unobstructed Dharma, their fragrance pure and pervasive, filling the entire world.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings attain the steadfast Dharma, the Dharma free from regret, all precepts of the Dharma, be free from all broken precepts, all attain the Dharma without attachment, the unprecedented Dharma, the Dharma without a teacher, the uncontrived Dharma, the unstained Dharma, the untainted Dharma, the ultimate Dharma, the ultimate Dharma, the Dharma of equality, transcending good and evil, equal and without partiality or attachment.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings attain the supreme Dharma, the Dharma of the Great Vehicle, not the Dharma of the Lesser Vehicle.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings fully realize the natural fruition of the Dao, just as the Perfected One did when first attaining the Dharma.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings all engage in giving, uphold the precepts, practice forbearance, diligence, and spiritual wonder, perfumed and cultivated by fragrant flowers.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings all accomplish the supreme, subtle, and wondrous treasure fragrance of primordial yang, its fragrance pervading empty space.
May all ordinary beings and all sentient beings partake purely of the supreme, Great Vehicle fragrance of primordial yang, like bees gathering from flowers, taking their fragrance and essence.

Good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering fragrant incense, he should constantly and firmly generate such natural vows.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering bedding and seats, he constantly makes this vow: "What I now give, I share with all sentient beings." Through this cause and condition, may all ordinary beings obtain the celestial beds on which they recline, gain great wisdom, sit in the four states of bliss, and rest upon the Perfected One’s bed, never lying upon the beds of demonic or unwholesome Dharma.
May all ordinary beings rest in peace, free from the bed of birth and death, and attain the natural lion’s bed of repose.
May all ordinary beings, having sat upon this bed, further manifest spiritual powers for the sake of countless other ordinary beings, possessing great wisdom and strength.
May all ordinary beings dwell in this palace of primordial yang and expound the Dharma for all ordinary beings.
May all ordinary beings sit upon the supreme bed, never subdued by worldly Dharma.
May all ordinary beings attain the bed of forbearance, free from birth and death, hunger, and hardship.
May all ordinary beings attain the bed of fearlessness, forever free from afflictions and all hostile foes.
May all ordinary beings attain the pure bed, devoted solely to the supreme, true, and correct Dao.
May all ordinary beings attain the bed of virtuous Dharma, always protected by good friends.
May all ordinary beings attain the bed of reclining on the left side, in accordance with the practices of the sages.

Good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering bedding and seats, he should constantly and firmly generate such vows.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering dwellings, he constantly makes this vow: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." Through this cause and condition, may all ordinary beings dwell in the Great Vehicle’s abode, cultivate the practices of good friends, the practice of great compassion, the practice of sublime liberation, and the practices of the celestial Perfected Ones—boundless and vast as empty space.
May all ordinary beings all attain right mindfulness, far removed from evil thoughts.
May all ordinary beings all dwell in peace, abiding in constant joy and purity, forever free from the four inclinations.
May all ordinary beings all uphold the subtle and wondrous scriptures.
May all ordinary beings all become the supreme abode of omniscience.
May all ordinary beings all enter the abode of the joyful Dharma of sweet dew.
May the minds of all ordinary beings, in the beginning, middle, and end, always enter the pure palace of primordial yang.
May all ordinary beings, in future lives, always dwell in the palaces where the Perfected Ones reside.

Good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering dwellings, he should constantly and firmly generate such vows.

Furthermore, good man, when the Perfected One’s youth practices giving with a mind of compassion, offering lamp-light, he should make this vow: "What I now give, I share with all ordinary beings." Through this cause and condition, may all ordinary beings attain boundless illumination and abide in the Dharma.
May all ordinary beings always be bright and clear.
May all ordinary beings attain radiant and lustrous forms, supremely subtle and wondrous.
May all ordinary beings have pure eyes, free from obstructions and veils.
May all ordinary beings attain the great torch of wisdom, fully understanding non-self, without the marks of ordinary beings, without person or life.
May all ordinary beings all clearly perceive the pure Dharma-nature, like empty space.
May the eyes of all ordinary beings be bright and clear, seeing afar the worlds of the ten directions like the Ganges’ sands.
May all ordinary beings attain the illumination of the Dharma, pervading the infinite lands of the ten directions.
May all ordinary beings attain unobstructed light, all clearly perceiving the pure Dharma-nature.
May all ordinary beings attain the great illumination of wisdom, dispelling all darkness and demonic influences.
May all ordinary beings attain boundless illumination, universally shining upon the infinite celestial worlds.
May all ordinary beings kindle the lamp of the Great Vehicle Dharma, free from the views of the Lesser Vehicle.
May the illumination attained by all ordinary beings extinguish the darkness of ignorance, surpassing the light of a thousand suns.
May all ordinary beings attain great illumination, pervading the three-thousandfold world, all hidden darkness fully dispelled.

May all ordinary beings attain the five eyes in full, awaken to the marks of the Dharma, and become supreme masters.

May all ordinary beings perceive no ignorance.

May all ordinary beings attain the primordial yang’s subtle and wondrous illumination of the Great Vehicle, revealing and awakening ordinary beings to the true nature of the Real Person and the true Dharma.

Good man, when the Real Person Youth offers lamp-light within the heart of compassion, he should always firmly generate such vows.

Good man, the celestial Real Person Youths take compassion as their root; cultivating the heart of compassion, they give rise to such boundless meritorious deeds—
what is called impurity, exhalation and inhalation, impermanence and arising-and-ceasing, the four noble fruits, the five kinds of virtuous deeds, the three attainments of insight, the eight kinds of merit, all entering emptiness, without form or appearance.
They know the wisdom of others and all the wisdom of spiritual penetrations, the wisdom of the primordial beginning, the wisdom of the immortals, the wisdom of the youth, the wisdom of the Real Person, the wisdom of the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, such Dharmas take compassion as their root.
For this reason, compassion is true and real, not false or delusive.

Good man, one who can act with goodness is called “true and subtle contemplation”; true and subtle contemplation is called compassion.
Compassion is the Heavenly Worthy; compassion is the Great Vehicle; the Great Vehicle is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the natural; compassion is the true Dao; the true Dao is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the immortal; the immortal is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion serves as father and mother to ordinary beings and all sentient beings; father and mother are compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the inconceivable realm of all Dharmas; the inconceivable realm of all Dharmas is compassion.
You should know that compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the Dharma-nature of ordinary beings; this Dharma-nature has long been obscured by afflictions, causing ordinary beings to be unable to perceive it.
Dharma-nature is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the great void; the great void is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is empty space; empty space is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the eternal; the eternal is the true; the true is the Dao; the Dao is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is joy; joy is the immortal; the immortal is the Dharma; the Dharma is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is purity; purity is clarity; clarity is the Dao; the Dao is the Dharma; the Dharma is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the self; the self is the Dao; the Dao is the Dharma; the Dharma is the noble one; the noble one is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the sweet dew; the sweet dew is compassion; compassion is Dharma-nature; Dharma-nature is the Dao; the Dao is the noble one; the noble one is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the supreme Dao of the Real Person; the Dao is compassion; compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, compassion is the boundless worlds of the celestial sages; the boundless worlds are compassion.
You should know that this compassion is the Heavenly Worthy.

Good man, if compassion were to have existence or non-existence, neither existence nor non-existence—there is no such compassion that inferior immortals or beginners could fathom.

Good man, if compassion is inconceivable, the Dharma is inconceivable, Dharma-nature is inconceivable, and the Heavenly Worthy is also inconceivable.

Good man, the Real Person Youth abiding in the wondrous garden of the Great Vehicle cultivates such compassion—though resting in sleep, he does not sleep, for he is diligent and vigorous.
Though ever clear, he is not clear, for he is without slumber.
In his sleep, though the celestials protect him, there is no protector, for he does not commit evil.
He does not dream evil dreams, nor does he have unwholesome thoughts, though he sleeps.
After the end of his life, though he is born in heaven, there is no birth, for he attains mastery.

Good man, cultivating compassion can accomplish such boundless and infinite merits.
Good man, this supreme and subtle scripture of the Primordial Yang can also accomplish such boundless and infinite merits; the celestial Real Persons also attain such boundless and infinite merits.

The Real Person of Numinous Flower addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “All the subtle contemplations of the Real Person Youths are true and real; those of inferior immortals and late learners are not true.”

“Why do all sentient beings not receive joy equal to the power of the Real Person Youths?
If sentient beings truly do not attain joy, then the compassion cultivated by the Real Persons would be without benefit.”

The Heavenly Worthy said: “Good man, the compassion of the Real Persons is not without benefit for sentient beings.
All ordinary beings either must suffer or may not suffer. If there are sentient beings who must suffer, then the compassion of the Real Persons would be without benefit.
But if ordinary beings may or may not suffer, then the compassion of the Real Persons becomes beneficial, enabling those sentient beings to all receive joy.

Good man, it is like a person who, seeing fierce beasts and poisonous creatures from afar, naturally feels dread and fear; walking at night and seeing ghosts, he also feels terror.
Good man, such people naturally experience fear.
Sentient beings, upon seeing one who cultivates compassion, naturally receive joy.

Good man, for this reason, the compassion cultivated by the Real Person is true and subtle contemplation, not without benefit for all sentient beings.
One should wholeheartedly make offerings, recite, and contemplate the *Supreme Subtle Scripture of Primordial Yang’s Contemplation and Practice*, deeply understanding the heart of compassion, joy, equanimity, and renunciation—all attaining liberation and ascending to the fruit of the supreme, natural, and great Dao.”

Good men, you must not slight or scorn, harbor doubts or perverse thoughts, disbelieve the scriptural teachings, or slander the sacred texts. If one’s heart gives rise to disbelief, one shall fall into the three evil destinies and receive the retribution of being reborn as an animal.

Thereupon, the numinous Radiant Flower Real Person, the divine immortals and their retinues, and the good men, having gained clarity and harboring no lingering doubts, all paid reverent homage, circumambulated three times to the left, prostrated, and departed.

The Fifth Scroll of the *Supreme Numinous Treasure Scripture of Primordial Yang* concludes.
*(Note: “议” should read “卷” [Scroll].)*

The Sixth Scroll of the *Supreme Numinous Treasure Scripture of Primordial Yang*
The Middle Chapter on Contemplation and Practice

At that time, the Primordial Yang Wondrous Joy Real Person, together with the great assemblies of the heavens, the divine immortals and their retinues, and eighty-four thousand youths, gathered in the Primordial Yang realm. They prepared a great high seat, adorned with incense, flowers, music, banners, canopies, and myriad treasures, filling the entire void of space.

All at once, they expounded the mysterious and subtle, the secret treasury of Primordial Yang, enabling those who would be reborn as men and women to universally hear the sacred teachings.

The Heavenly Worthy, moved by great compassion, manifested various radiant signs and expounded the profound and esoteric scriptures, awakening sentient beings: “What is known in the world, I too know; what is unknown in the world, I too fully know. What does this mean?

Good men, all in the world do not know, do not see, do not awaken to the nature of the Dao. If there are those who know, see, and awaken to the nature of the Dao, they are not called worldly beings but are named Real Persons. Worldly ordinary beings also do not know, do not see, do not awaken to the thirty-six revered scriptures, the thirty-six kinds of causes and conditions, or the meaning of the supreme-grade contemplation and practice of Primordial Yang. If one can know, see, and awaken to these, one is not called a worldly being but is named a Real Person.

Good men, this is what is meant by the world’s not knowing, not seeing, and not awakening.

What then is the world’s knowing, seeing, and awakening? It refers to the Lord of Creation’s dharmas, the beginning and end of the world, the two views of annihilation and permanence, and the discourse that begins with the initial mind and extends to the Neither-Perception-Nor-Non-Perception realm, calling this the true Dao.

Good men, this is what is meant by the world’s knowing, seeing, and awakening.

Real Persons and youths know, see, and awaken to such matters. If Real Persons, having thus known, seen, and awakened, claim not to know, not to see, and not to awaken, this is falsehood. The dharma of falsehood is sin, and because of this sin, one falls into hell.

Whether man or woman, if one declares there is no Dao, know that such persons are kin to external demons and are named slanderers of the Dao and its dharma. Those who slander the dharma slander the Heavenly Worthy. Such persons shall fall into the three evil destinies, become non-human kinds, and receive manifold苦 retributions.”

Thereupon, the Wondrous Joy Real Person and all the dharma assemblies, having heard these words, praised them in verse:

“Out of loving-kindness for sentient beings,
You expound Primordial Yang to me.
Skillfully extracting the poisoned arrows,
Thus You are called the Great Physician King.
The world’s physicians, though they heal,
Bring harm again once cured.
Those treated by the Heavenly Worthy
Ultimately attain freedom from calamity.”

The sagely ambrosial medicine is the wondrous nectar of all gods.
Once sentient beings partake of it,
They neither die nor perish.
Now the Heavenly Worthy expounds,
Dissecting the hidden and secret chapters.
Having heard this treasury of mysteries,
Beings ascend to the realm of self-mastery.

After the Wondrous Joy Real Person recited this verse, he addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “As You have said, in all the world, none know, see, or awaken to the Primordial Yang Youth. If the Primordial Yang Youth were of this world, You could not say that the world does not know, see, or awaken, while only the Primordial Yang Youth knows, sees, and awakens. If not of this world, what distinguishing marks does he bear?”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Good son, the true person youth is both of this world and not of this world. Those who do not know, see, or awaken are called ‘of this world’; those who know, see, and awaken are not called ‘of this world.’ You ask what distinguishes them—I shall now explain.

Good son, whether man or woman, if upon first hearing this *Supreme Contemplation of Primordial Yang Sublime Scripture*, one generates reverence and faith, and arouses the mind set on the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao, such a one is called a ‘youth of this world.’ All the world does not know, see, or awaken, and such a youth likewise does not know, see, or awaken. Yet having heard this scripture, the youth knows there is something the world does not know, see, or awaken to—this should be what the youth knows, sees, and awakens to. Knowing this, the youth reflects: ‘By what means shall I cultivate to attain knowing, seeing, and awakening?’ Again and again, he thinks: ‘Only by wholeheartedly upholding the dharma precepts.’

Good son and good daughter, for this reason, in future lives in every place, they will remain free from arrogance, perverse views, and the net of doubt. They will never speak of the Heavenly Worthy in vain, and will ultimately enter the profound and wondrous. This is called a true person. Having upheld the precepts and purified their conduct, they next cultivate the true dharma, so that wherever they are born, their right mindfulness never falters.

That is to say, all sentient beings possess the Dao-nature; the thirty-six divisions of the Heavenly Worthy’s scriptures, the Heavenly Worthies and true persons, constantly delight in the self and the pure—all true person youths see the Dao-nature. Remembering such matters without forgetfulness, through cultivating concentration they attain the twelve emptinesses. This is called a true person youth.

Having perfected the pure dharma precepts, they next cultivate pure wisdom. Through cultivating pure wisdom, the precepts they uphold become firm and unshakable. Good son, it is like Mount Jade Capital, which is not shaken by the four winds. The true person youth is likewise not swayed by the four inversions.

Good son, when the true person knows, sees, and awakens, the precepts they uphold remain unshaken. This is called the knowing, seeing, and awakening of the true person—not of this world. Good son, when the true person’s upheld precepts are firm and unshakable, their mind is free from regret. Being free from regret, their mind attains joy. Attaining joy, their mind attains delight. Attaining delight, their mind attains tranquility. Attaining tranquility, they attain the unshakable concentration. Attaining the unshakable concentration, they attain true knowing and seeing. Attaining true knowing and seeing, they become weary of birth and death. Becoming weary of birth and death, they attain self-mastery. Attaining self-mastery, they clearly perceive the Dao-nature. This is called the knowing, seeing, and awakening of the true person—not of this world.

Good son, this is what is meant by the world not knowing, seeing, or awakening, while the true person knows, sees, and awakens.”

The Wondrous Joy Real Person again asked: “How does the Primordial Yang Youth uphold the dharma precepts without regret, and ultimately clearly perceive the dharma-nature?”

The Heavenly Worthy replied: “Good son, the precepts of this world are not called pure. Why? The precepts of this world are for the sake of existence, their nature is unstable, they are not ultimate, and they cannot broadly benefit all sentient beings. For these reasons, they are called impure. Being impure, they give rise to regret. With regret, the mind lacks joy. Lacking joy, there is no delight. Lacking delight, there is no tranquility. Lacking tranquility, there is no unshakable concentration. Lacking unshakable concentration, there is no true knowing and seeing. Lacking true knowing and seeing, there is no weariness of birth and death. Lacking weariness, there is no liberation. Lacking liberation, the dharma-nature is not seen. Not seeing the dharma-nature, one ultimately cannot attain the fruit of the supreme Great Dao. This is called the impurity of the world’s dharma.

Good son, the pure dharma of the true person youth is not dharma for the sake of non-dharma, not for the sake of existence, its nature is stable and ultimate, and it is for the sake of sentient beings. This is called the purity of the true person’s dharma.

Good son, though the true person youth does not intend to generate a mind free from regret within the dharma precepts, such a mind arises naturally. Good son, it is like someone holding a bright mirror, not expecting to see their face, yet their reflection appears of itself. It is like a farmer sowing seeds in fertile soil, not expecting sprouts to grow, yet sprouts arise of themselves. It is like lighting a lamp, not expecting darkness to vanish, yet darkness vanishes of itself. Good son, when the true person youth upholds the dharma precepts, a mind free from regret arises naturally—it is likewise so.

Through the purity of the dharma, the mind attains joy. Good son, it is like a person of fine appearance seeing their own face and feeling joy. One who upholds the dharma precepts is likewise so. Good son, one who violates the dharma precepts, seeing the impurity of the precepts, feels no joy—like one with a crippled or ugly form seeing their own reflection and feeling no delight. One who violates the dharma precepts is likewise so.

Good son, it is like two cowherds, one carrying a jar of cream and the other a jar of whey, both going to market to sell their wares. On the way, they stumble, and both jars break. One feels joy, the other sorrow.”

Upholding the precepts and violating the dharma are likewise so. One who applies the mind with reverence to uphold the pure dharma precepts feels joy in the heart; because of this joy in the heart, one then contemplates that in the scriptures of the Heavenly Venerable, it is said that those who uphold the pure dharma precepts attain the true Dao. "I now cultivate such dharma precepts and should likewise attain it." Through this causal condition, the heart feels delight.

The Perfected of Primordial Yang again asked: "What is the difference between joy and delight?"
Good son, when one does not commit evil, this is called joy; when the mind upholds the dharma precepts, this is called delight. Good son, observing birth and death is called joy; seeing the marks of the dharma is called delight. The lower is called joy, the higher is called delight. Departing from the shared dharma is called joy; attaining the unshared dharma is called delight. Because your precepts are pure, your form and bearing become light and gentle, and your speech is free from coarse faults. Perfected Youth, at that time, whether seeing or hearing, all evil is absent; because evil is absent, the mind attains peace. Because of this peace, one attains stillness and concentration. Attaining stillness and concentration, one gains true knowledge and vision. Gaining true knowledge and vision, one becomes weary of birth and death. Becoming weary of birth and death, one attains freedom. Attaining freedom, one sees the dharma-nature. Seeing the dharma-nature, one attains the true Dao. This is called the Perfected Youth purely upholding the dharma precepts—precepts that are not of the worldly kind.

Why is this so? Good son, the pure dharma precepts one receives and upholds are assisted by five dharmas. What are the five assisting dharmas? First is faith, second is shame, third is remorse, fourth is good spiritual companions, and fifth is reverence for the true dharma. Because the five hindrances are departed from, what is seen is pure; because the five views are departed from, the mind is free from doubt and obstruction. What are the five doubts? First is doubt of the Dao, second is doubt of the dharma, third is doubt of the true, fourth is doubt of the precepts, and fifth is doubt of non-negligence.

At that time, the Perfected attains the five roots—namely, faith, mindfulness, vigor, concentration, and wisdom. Because of the five roots, one attains the five kinds of true dharma: form-freedom, and so on up to consciousness-freedom. This is called the Perfected Youth purely upholding the precepts—precepts that are not of the world. Good son, this is what the world does not know, see, or perceive, but what the Perfected knows, sees, and perceives.

Good son, if among my disciples there are those who receive, uphold, recite, or transcribe the *Upper Grade Scripture of Primordial Yang*, and there are those who break the precepts, others may reproach, belittle, disparage, or humiliate them, saying: "If the profound treasury of the *Mahāyāna Sūtra of Primordial Yang* possesses power, why do you now slander and violate the dharma precepts you have received? If one receives and upholds the wondrous scripture of Primordial Yang yet violates the precepts, know that this scripture is without power. If it is without power, though one recites it, there is no benefit. Because of such disparagement of the *Scripture of Primordial Yang*, countless beings will fall into hell. Those who receive and uphold this scripture yet violate the precepts are great evil companions to beings, not my disciples, but followers of demonic forces. Such persons, I do not permit to receive the subtle and wondrous scriptures, nor to receive, uphold, and cultivate them while slandering the dharma by violating the precepts."

Good sons and daughters, if among my disciples there are those who diligently receive, uphold, recite, transcribe, or expound the *Mahāyāna Treasury of the Profound Primordial Yang*, they should rectify body and mind, taking care not to engage in frivolity or restless movement. Frivolous speech is called restless movement of the mind; seeking existence is called restlessness, and bodily actions are called frivolity. If among my disciples there are those who seek existence and create karma, they should not receive and uphold the subtle and wondrous meanings of this *Scripture of Primordial Yang*. If those who receive and uphold the scripture seek existence and create karma, others may reproach them, saying: "If the profound treasury of the Heavenly Venerable’s *Mahāyāna* possesses power, why do you seek existence and create karma? If those who receive and uphold the scripture seek existence and create karma, know that this scripture is without power. If it is without power, though one receives and recites it, there is no benefit. Because of such disdain for the *Scripture of Primordial Yang*, countless beings will fall into the three evil destinies of hell. Those who receive, uphold, and recite this scripture while seeking existence and creating karma are great evil companions to beings, not my disciples, but kin to demonic forces."

Furthermore, good son, if among my disciples there are those who recite, transcribe, or expound the meaning of the *Mahāyāna* scriptures, they should not speak at improper times, nor speak contrary to the dharma, nor speak impurely, nor speak with a frivolous mind, nor speak in a way that extinguishes the Dao, nor speak with worldly dharma ablaze. Good son, if among my disciples there are those who receive and uphold this scripture yet speak at improper times, or up to speaking with worldly dharma ablaze, others may reproach them, saying: "If the *Mahāyāna Treasury of the Profound Primordial Yang* possesses power, why do you speak at improper times, or up to speaking with worldly dharma ablaze? If those who uphold the scripture speak in this way, know that this scripture is without power. If it is without power, though one recites it, there is no benefit. Because of such disdain for the *Mahāyāna* scripture, countless beings will fall into hell. Those who receive and uphold this scripture yet speak at improper times, or up to speaking with worldly dharma ablaze, are great evil companions to beings, not my disciples, but followers of demonic forces."

Good son, if one wishes to receive, uphold, and recite, or expound the *Great Scripture of Primordial Yang*, speak of the dharma-nature, expound the *Mahāyāna Profound Treasury*, speak of the scriptures of immortals, speak of the youth attaining the Dao, speak of freedom and liberation, or see the dharma-nature, one should first purify the body. Because it is pure, there will be no reproach; because there is no reproach, countless people will generate a pure mind toward the *Scripture of Primordial Yang*, reverently reciting, receiving, and upholding this scripture.

If one hears even a single verse, a single phrase, or a single character, sighs with admiration and rejoices, and expounds it to others to awaken beings, thereby attaining the mind of the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao, know that such a person is a true good companion to beings, my disciple, not a follower of external demonic forces, and is called a true person.

Good son, good daughter, this is what the world does not know, does not see, does not awaken to, yet the true person knows, sees, and awakens to.

Furthermore, good son, what is meant by "what the entire world does not know, see, or awaken to, yet the true person knows, sees, and awakens to"? It is the six recollections. What are the six? First, recollection of the Heavenly Venerable; second, recollection of the true person; third, recollection of the youth; fourth, recollection of the dharma precepts; fifth, recollection of the Daoist; sixth, recollection of compassion.

Good son, what is recollection of the Heavenly Venerable? The sage is one who is rightly and universally knowing, whose luminous conduct is complete, who is a goodly passage through the world, who understands the unsurpassed one, who tames and guides the teacher of gods and humans, who is eternally unchanging; fully possessed of majestic power, fearless in body, ultimately pure, having reached the other shore; without one who can surpass, without one who can topple, without fear or dread, unstartled and unafraid, without companion or teacher, self-awakened and swiftly knowing; of great wisdom, sharp wisdom, profound wisdom, liberating wisdom, having accomplished the king of humans, the tamer and guide of gods and humans, the great benefactor, the great dharma master. Because he knows the dharma, he is called the great dharma master. Because he knows the meaning, he is called the great dharma master. Because he knows the time, he is called the great dharma master. Because he knows contentment, he is called the great dharma master. Because he knows the self, he is called the great dharma master. Because he knows the various natures of beings, he is called the great dharma master. Because he knows the keen, dull, and middling faculties of all beings, he is called the great dharma master. Because he expounds the wondrous Dao of Primordial Yang, he is called the great dharma master.

Furthermore, the Wondrous Joy True Person addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: What is meant by "one who responds"? The Heavenly Venerable replied: The dharmas of the world are all called enemies, for the dharma responds by harming, hence it is called "responding." The four demons are such. Good son, when the Heavenly Venerable was a good son, he was able to destroy the four demons with wisdom, hence he is called "one who responds." Furthermore, "responding" means to be far removed. When he was a good son, he was to be far removed from countless afflictions, hence he is called "one who responds." Furthermore, "responding" means joy. In the past, when the Heavenly Venerable was a good son, though he endured countless afflictions for the sake of beings over immeasurable kalpas, he was never without joy, but always rejoiced. The Heavenly Venerable is also thus, hence he is called "one who responds." Moreover, "responding" means that all humans and gods should make offerings of various fragrant flowers, music, and entertainments to him, hence he is called "one who responds."

What is "rightly and universally knowing"? "Right" means not inverted; "universally knowing" means being thoroughly penetrating amid inversion. Moreover, "right" means ascetic practice; "universally knowing" means knowing that through ascetic practice, there is certainly a bitter fruit. Moreover, "right" means within the world; "universally knowing" means definitively knowing that through cultivating the Middle Way, one attains the fruit of the supreme, correct, and true. Moreover, "right" means that which can be counted and measured; "universally knowing" means that which cannot be counted or measured. Therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is called "rightly and universally knowing." Good son, even if one of the true vehicle were to contemplate a single form for immeasurable kalpas without removing it, one could not exhaustively know it. For this reason, there is no universal knowing.

What is "whose luminous conduct is complete"? "Luminous" means attaining immeasurable good fruits; "conduct" means the foot; "complete" means the good fruit of the supreme, correct, and true Dao. Therefore, it is called "whose luminous conduct is complete." Moreover, "luminous" means incantation; "conduct" means auspicious; "complete" means, good son, the meaning in the world. "Incantation" means liberation; "auspicious" means the fruit of the supreme, correct, and true. Therefore, it is called "whose luminous conduct is complete." Moreover, "luminous" means light; "conduct" means karma; "complete" means, good son, the meaning in the world. "Light" means non-negligence; "karma" means attaining the fruit of self-mastery. Moreover, "luminous" means the three luminosities. What are the three luminosities? First, the luminosity of the true person; second, the luminosity of the Heavenly Venerable; third, the luminosity of ignorance. The luminosity of the true person is the natural fruit. The luminosity of the Heavenly Venerable is the wisdom eye. The luminosity of ignorance is ultimate emptiness. "Conduct" means cultivating various good karmas for the sake of beings over immeasurable kalpas. "Complete" means clearly seeing the dharma-nature. For this reason, it is called "whose luminous conduct is complete."

What is "a goodly passage"? "Good" means lofty; "passage" means not lofty. Good son, this is the meaning in the world. "Lofty" means the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao; "not lofty" means the mind of the Heavenly Venerable. Good son, if the mind were lofty, it would not be called the Heavenly Venerable. Therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is called "a goodly passage." Moreover, "good" means a good companion. Good son, this is the meaning in the world of a good companion. A good companion is the initial arousal of the mind, and its fruit is the Heavenly Venerable of the highest grade of Primordial Yang. Not abandoning the initial arousal of the mind, one attains the great wondrous scripture. Therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is called "a goodly passage." Good son, this meaning in the world is called seeing the dharma-nature and attaining the profound wondrous principle. Good son, the true nature of the Dao is truly not existent, but the Heavenly Venerable, because of the world, speaks of it as existent. Good son, it is like someone who in truth has no one, in truth has no child, yet falsely claims to have someone; in truth has no virtue or Dao, yet falsely speaks of having virtue and Dao.

The true Dharma is likewise: because of the world, it is falsely spoken of as existent. The Perfected One accomplishes the supreme Dao, hence is called the "Goodly Passage." What is meant by "Supreme Man"? The term "superior man" denotes severance. One who severs nothing is called the "Supreme Man." The Heavenly Venerable, the Perfected One, is without afflictions, hence has nothing to sever—therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is titled the "Supreme Man." Moreover, the "superior man" is named for contention; the "Supreme Man" is without contention. The Sage is without contention—thus, the Heavenly Venerable is titled the "Supreme Man." Furthermore, the "superior man" is named for speech that may be refuted; the "Supreme Man" has speech that cannot be refuted.
