The words of the Heavenly Venerable cannot be refuted by any being—therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is titled the "Supreme Man." Also, the "superior man" is named for a high seat; the "Supreme Man" is without a superior seat. No Sage of the three times surpasses him—therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is titled the "Supreme Man."

At that time, the Wondrous Joy Perfected One, his mind still harboring doubt, inquired of the Heavenly Venerable: "What is meant by 'Tamer and Guide, Great Man, Teacher of Gods and Humans'?" The Heavenly Venerable replied: "All Perfected Ones and youths who cultivate four dharmas are called 'Great Men, Teachers of Gods and Humans.' What are the four? First, relying on good companions, they cultivate and study the true Dharma. Second, their minds are able to listen to the Dharma and fathom its wondrous meaning. Third, they contemplate the profound principle without doubt or difficulty. Fourth, they uphold the precepts of the Dharma and conduct that subdues beings. Good son, possessing these four dharmas, one is called a 'Great Man'; without them, one is not called a 'Great Man.' Why? Though the body may be that of a great man, if the mind harbors deceit and crookedness, and the intent is tainted with depravity, one cannot be called a 'Great Man.' The majestic power of the Heavenly Venerable tames and subdues beings, enabling them to know the true Dharma—thus, he is titled 'Tamer and Guide, Great Man, Teacher of Gods and Humans.'"

Again, the good son inquired of the Heavenly Master: "What is meant by 'Tamer and Guide, Teacher of Gods and Humans'?" The Heavenly Venerable said: "There are two kinds of teachers: one who teaches good, and one who teaches evil. I now teach all beings with the good Dharma. What is the good Dharma? It is the goodness of body, speech, and mind. I now teach all beings to speak thus: 'Good son, you should distance yourself from unwholesome bodily deeds. Why? Because unwholesome bodily deeds can be distanced from, and one thereby attains freedom. Therefore, I teach you this Dharma. If these unwholesome deeds could not be distanced from to attain freedom, I would never teach you to distance yourself from them. If beings distance themselves from unwholesome deeds, there is no possibility of falling into the three evil destinies. By distancing oneself, one accomplishes the fruit of supreme, correct, and true enlightenment—thus, I constantly teach this Dharma to transform beings. The same applies to speech and mind—therefore, I am called the Teacher of Gods and Humans.'"

Moreover, before attaining the Dao, one was deluded; now, having awakened, one expounds the Dao attained to beings. From the beginning, one had not cultivated good conduct; now, having completed the cultivation, one teaches what was cultivated to beings. Having shattered one’s own ignorance, one shatters the ignorance of beings. Having attained the pure eye, one shatters the blindness of beings, enabling them to attain the pure eye. Knowing the two wisdoms, one expounds the two wisdoms. Having oneself awakened, one expounds the Dharma of awakening to beings. Having crossed the boundless, limitless sea of birth and death, one enables all beings to cross over. Having attained fearlessness, one teaches beings to be without dread. Having attained the supreme, correct, and true Dao, one expounds the supreme, correct, and true Dao to beings—therefore, the Heavenly Venerable is titled the "Tamer and Guide, Teacher of Gods and Humans."

Again, the good son’s mind harbored further doubt, and he ventured to inquire: "What is meant by 'Heavenly'?" The reply: "'Heavenly' means day—day is long, night is short—hence it is called 'Heavenly.' Moreover, 'Heavenly' means without sorrow or affliction, constantly receiving joy—hence it is called 'Heavenly.' Also, 'Heavenly' means lamp and light, able to shatter darkness and become great illumination—hence it is called 'Heavenly.' It also shatters the darkness of unwholesome deeds, attains wholesome deeds, and is born in heaven—hence it is called 'Heavenly.' Furthermore, 'Heavenly' means auspicious—because of auspicious omens, it is named 'Heavenly.' Also, 'Heavenly' is named for the sun—the sun has light—hence the sun is called 'Heavenly.' For these reasons, it is called 'Heavenly.'"

"'Human' means capable, abundant in kindness and righteousness. Moreover, 'human' means the body and speech are pure and fragrant. Also, 'human' means having arrogance. Furthermore, 'human' means able to shatter arrogance. Good son, though I am now the supreme Tamer and Guide for all beings, the scripture calls me the 'Teacher of Gods and Humans.' Why? Good son, among all beings, only gods and humans can arouse the natural intent for the Dao, cultivate the ten good deeds, and attain the fruit of the supreme, correct, and true great Dao—therefore, I am titled the 'Teacher of Gods and Humans.'"

Again, the good son inquired of the Heavenly Venerable: "My doubts are not yet exhausted; I have further questions. What is meant by the 'Great Dao'?" The Heavenly Venerable replied: "The Dao is called 'pervasive'—it pervades and understands itself and enables others to pervade. Good son, it is like someone who, knowing there are thieves, renders the thieves powerless. The Perfected One and youth can pervade all boundless afflictions; having pervaded them, they render afflictions powerless—hence the Dao is called 'pervasive.' Because of this pervasiveness, one is not born, does not age, does not fall ill, does not die—this is the true Dao. Good son, you should know that within my Dharma, there are great officials and soldiers, heavenly escorts, armored troops, and heavenly warriors who can capture demonic and evil spirits, and all afflictions are completely subdued. They can also accomplish all good dharmas, possess great majestic power that pervades the ten directions, and can perform various great acts of generosity. Moreover, they remain uncorrupted through boundless kalpas—hence it is called the 'Great Dao.'"

"Good son, whether man or woman, if one can thus contemplate the Dao—whether walking or standing, sitting or lying, by day or night, in light or darkness—one will constantly remain inseparable, beholding all true Dao.

Good son, why is it called the 'True Dao, the Properly Enlightened One Who Pervades All Knowledge,' and why does the Perfected One and youth possess such boundless meritorious virtues and great renown? Good son, in countless kalpas past, the Perfected One revered parents and teachers, constantly practiced generosity for the sake of all beings, firmly upheld precepts, cultivated forbearance, diligently practiced vigor, true concentration, and wisdom, and embodied great compassion. Thus, today, he attains the seventy-two marks, eighty excellences, and a body like true gold.

Moreover, in countless kalpas past, the Perfected One and youth cultivated faith and resolve, advanced the roots of concentration and wisdom, made offerings and paid homage to all teachers, and always acted for the benefit of the Dharma, never for harm. If the Perfected One and youth uphold, read, recite, expound, or teach the thirty-six revered sutras, they constantly enable beings to attain freedom, liberation, and unconditioned peace, secure and joyful, never acting for themselves. Why? The Perfected One constantly cultivates a supramundane mind, a mind without grasping or rejecting, without bondage, without birth or death, without doubt, without greed, without anger, without delusion, without arrogance. Having cultivated such a mind, all becomes pure; one deeply comprehends the source of the Dao, free from defilement, free from affliction, free from suffering, boundless, vast, empty, and void, without worldly intent, constantly at ease, constantly liberated, without retribution, without ill will, with good will, without verbal intent, with gentle intent, without abiding, without regression, without impermanence, with upright intent, without crookedness, with pure and good intent. Having such intent, one attains fearlessness, constant joy, self-mastery, and purity. Thus, one cultivates the mind of the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao—this is the fruit of the Perfected One and youth.

How does the Perfected One and youth contemplate the Dharma? Good son, one reflects on all dharmas, the most sublime and supreme teachings. Through this Dharma, beings can attain the present fruit. Only this true Dharma is timeless, seen by heavenly illumination, not by the fleshly eye, yet it cannot be likened to any analogy. It is unborn and unproduced, unabiding and unceasing, without beginning or end, without going or coming, unmoving and unturning, neither long nor short. It eternally severs all pleasures yet abides in secure joy, ultimately subtle. It is not form yet severs form while also being form; up to not consciousness yet severs consciousness while also being consciousness; not karma yet severs karma while also being karma; not fetters yet severs fetters while also being fetters; not realms yet severs realms while also being realms; not existence yet severs existence while also being existence; not emergence yet severs emergence while also being emergence; not entry yet severs entry while also being entry; not cause yet severs cause while also being cause; not fruit yet severs fruit while also being fruit; not truth yet severs truth while also being truth. Through such contemplation and practice, one directly realizes suffering and emptiness, accomplishing the sublime Dao.

Furthermore, it is neither false nor real, severing all reality while also being real; neither arising nor ceasing, eternally severing arising and ceasing while also being cessation; neither marked nor unmarked, severing all marks while also being the one mark; neither teaching nor non-teaching yet also being teaching; neither fear nor fearlessness, severing all fear while also being fear; neither forbearance nor non-forbearance, eternally severing all forbearance while also being forbearance. All such dharmas eternally remove all afflictions, eternally pacify, are pure and markless, eternally sever all marks. Countless beings ultimately abide therein, able to sever all birth and death. It is the radiant abode where the Heavenly Venerable dwells, constantly unchanging. This is the contemplation of the Dharma by the Perfected One and youth.

How does one contemplate the Dharma? All heavenly Perfected Ones abide in the Dharma, unbreakable, unassailable, inconceivable. For all beings, they are bridges and fields of merit. Though fields of merit, they receive nothing, pure and undefiled, without ill intent, harmonious and equanimous, single-minded without duality, constantly unchanging, without disturbance. This is contemplation of the Dharma.

How does one contemplate the precepts? The Perfected One and youth reflect on the precepts as unbroken, unviolated, uncorrupted, and unmixed. Though without form or color, they can be upheld; though without contact, through skillful practice, they can be perfected without fault. The Perfected One and youth praise them, and all attain boundless, sublime causes. Good son, if one can cultivate and uphold the pure realm, all thieves and robbers dare not disturb, fire cannot burn, water cannot sweep away. If one cultivates these precepts, one attains the natural fruit, the mind of the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao. One should broadly expound the sublime Dharma for all beings as their refuge and protection. This is the Perfected One’s contemplation of the precepts.

How does one contemplate generosity? The Perfected One deeply observes that generosity is the cause of the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao. Good sons, if one draws near and cultivates such generosity, I too draw near and cultivate it. Without bestowing alms, one cannot adorn and make offerings to the fourfold assembly. Though generosity cannot ultimately sever fetters, it can remove present afflictions. Through the causes of generosity, one is constantly praised by beings in the ten directions, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges in countless worlds. Good son, to give beings food is to give them life. Through this karmic retribution, when attaining the Dao, one remains constantly unchanging."

Through the causes of joyful giving, when attaining the Dao, one obtains bliss. When a youth gives alms, seeking in accordance with the Dharma without encroaching upon one offering for another, thus attaining the Dao, one obtains the fruit of purity. When a Perfected One gives alms, enabling all beings to gain without seeking, thus attaining the Dao, one obtains the natural fruit. Through the causes of giving, I empower others, thus attaining the Dao and obtaining the twofold karmic conditions of generosity. Enabling others to gain speech, thus attaining the Dao, one obtains the threefold roots of goodness. Perfected Ones and youths who cultivate this generosity do so as the supreme cause. I too cultivate generosity as the true and good cause. This is the contemplation of generosity.

How does one contemplate the heavens? There are nine heavens where divine immortals dwell, extending even to the realm of neither perception nor non-perception. Through learning, generosity, and wisdom, one attains the nine heavens of divine immortals, even reaching the realm of neither perception nor non-perception. I too have a share in this, yet it is not my desire. Why? The nine heavens of divine immortals, even the realm of neither perception nor non-perception, are all impermanent. Due to impermanence, there arise birth, aging, sickness, and death. For this reason, it is not my desire. It is like an illusion deceiving the foolish; the wise are not deluded by it. The nine heavens of divine immortals, even the realm of neither perception nor non-perception, are like illusions. The foolish are all ordinary beings; I am not like these foolish ordinary beings. I have heard of the Heaven of the Supreme Meaning, where Perfected Ones and youths remain constantly unchanging. Due to their purity and eternal abiding, they are neither born nor perish, neither age nor sicken nor die. For the sake of beings, I diligently aspire to seek the Heaven of the Supreme Meaning. Why? The Heaven of the Supreme Meaning can enable beings to sever afflictions, like a wish-fulfilling tree. If I have faith, even wisdom, I can attain this Heaven of the Supreme Meaning. This is the Perfected One’s contemplation of the heavens.

Good sons, this is the Perfected One’s transcendence of the worldly. It is unknown and unseen by the worldly, yet known and seen by the Perfected One. Good sons, if my disciples are said to uphold, recite, transcribe, expound, and elucidate the *Supreme Yang’s Exalted, Subtle, and Secret Treasury Sutra*, or to uphold, recite, transcribe, propagate, explain, and expound the Mahayana teachings without distinction, this is not so. Why? Good sons, the *Supreme Yang Sutra* is the profound and secret treasury of all heavenly Perfected Ones and divine immortals. This profound and secret treasury of the heavenly Perfected Ones is supreme. Good sons, for this reason, the *Supreme Yang’s Wondrous Sutra* is most rare and subtle, beyond thought and conception.

The Wondrous Joy Perfected One addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: "I now also know that the *Supreme Yang’s Wondrous Sutra* is most rare and subtle, beyond thought and conception. The Dao’s Dharma is lofty and exalted, beyond thought and conception. The Perfected Ones and youths are also beyond thought and conception." For what reason is it said again that the Perfected One is beyond thought and conception? Good sons, without a teacher, one can spontaneously arouse the unsurpassed mind for the Dao. Having aroused this mind, one diligently cultivates and advances, even if a great fire burns one’s body and head, never seeking rescue, never abandoning the mind intent on the Dharma. Why? The Perfected One and youth constantly reflect: "In countless kalpas, I have been in the three wretched destinies—hells, animal realms—heaven and human realms, burned by the fires of kalpas. I have never once attained a decisive Dharma. This decisive Dharma is the cause of the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao. I never guarded or cherished body, mind, or life. Now, for the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao, even if my body is shattered like dust motes, I will never abandon diligent cultivation and advancement. Why? The mind of diligent advancement is the cause of the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao."

Good sons, such a Perfected One, having not yet seen the unsurpassed, proper, and true Great Dao, can already be so ungrudging of body and life. How much more so after having seen it? This Perfected One is beyond thought and conception. Furthermore, the Perfected One and youth see that the sufferings of birth and death are boundless and limitless, with countless evil faults, beyond the reach of all demonic forces. Though knowing the boundless and limitless sufferings and evil faults of birth and death, for the sake of beings, they endure suffering within it without generating weariness or aversion. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception. The Perfected One and youth, for the sake of beings, though enduring all sufferings in hell, manifest traces like ordinary beings. Thus, they are called enduring suffering beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, it is like a elder whose house catches fire. Seeing this, the elder escapes from the house, but the children remain inside, not yet free from the fire’s peril. The elder, knowing the danger of the fire, returns to rescue the children, undeterred by the peril. The Perfected One and youth, in saving and protecting beings, are likewise. Though knowing the many faults of birth and death, for the sake of beings, they abide within it without weariness. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, when countless and boundless beings spontaneously arouse the mind for the Dao, seeing the many faults in birth and death, their minds retreat in regret. They restrain the six senses, sever the five desires, cultivate the wondrous Dao, and contemplate the true sutras. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, if someone claims, "I can float and cross the great sea," is such a statement beyond thought and conception or not? The Heavenly Venerable said: Such a statement may be thought and conceived or beyond thought and conception. Why? If one truly crosses, it is beyond thought and conception. If one falsely claims to cross, it is thought and conceived. Good sons, what I now speak is true and accurate, without falsehood or error.

The Heavenly Venerable said: Among humans, there are those who may be thought and conceived, and those who are beyond thought and conception.

The Heavenly Venerable said: Humans are of two kinds—first, the sagely; second, the ordinary. The ordinary person is beyond thought and conception; the worthy and sagely person may be thought and conceived.

Good sons, I speak of the ordinary person, not the sage.

The Heavenly Venerable said: If the ordinary person is truly beyond thought and conception—good sons, the ordinary person truly cannot cross the great sea of water, yet the true person truly can cross the great sea of birth and death. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, if someone claims they can drag a lotus fiber to suspend Mount Jade Capital, is this thought and conceived or not?

The Heavenly Venerable said: Good sons, in a single thought-moment, they can weigh all of birth and death. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, through countless kalpas, I have always observed the impermanence, suffering, and impurity of birth and death, yet for the sake of beings, I distinguish and expound the eternal, blissful, self, and pure. Though I speak thus, it is not a false view. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, like one who enters water yet is not drowned, or enters raging fire yet is not burned—such matters are beyond thought and conception. The true person and immortal youth are likewise: though dwelling in birth and death, they are not afflicted by birth and death. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, humans are of three grades: upper, middle, and lower.

What are the upper, middle, and lower?

The lower-grade person, upon first entering the womb, thinks: "I am now in a privy, where all filth gathers, among corpses, in a thicket of thorns, in profound darkness." When first emerging from the womb, they again think: "I now exit the privy, the place of filth and evil, even emerging from profound darkness."

The middle-grade person thinks: "I now enter a grove of fruit trees, a pure river, a secluded palace." When emerging, it is likewise.

The upper-grade person thinks: "I ascend a palace hall, dwell among kalpa trees, ride a fine steed, and climb a lofty mountain." When emerging, it is likewise.

The true person and immortal youth, when first entering and dwelling in the womb, know their dwelling; when emerging, they know their emergence. They do not arouse minds of greed, anger, or delusion, yet have not attained the first dwelling-ground. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, the supreme secret treasury of primordial yang is truly beyond thought and conception—it cannot be compared by analogy.

Good sons, the mind also cannot be compared or measured by analogy.

The true person and immortal youth, though without teachers or masters to receive and study from, can attain the profound meaning of this supreme primordial yang. Having obtained this Dharma, their minds are free from stinginess and constantly expound it for beings. Thus, they are called beyond thought and conception.

Good sons, some depart through the body, not the mouth; some depart through the mouth, not the body; some depart neither through body nor mouth.

Departing through the body refers to killing, stealing, and lust—this is called departing through the body, not the mouth.

Departing through the mouth refers to refraining from false speech, slanderous talk of sutras and treatises, harsh words, divisive speech, flattery, and slander—this is called departing through the mouth, not the body.

Neither body nor mouth yet able to depart refers to departing from greed, jealousy, malice, anger, and false views.

Good sons, this is called departing neither through body nor mouth.

Good sons, not seeing any dharma as body or karma, yet able to depart from all faults—these are all evil karmas—thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception. The mouth is likewise.

Good sons, departing from the body through the body, from the mouth through the mouth, from evil through evil, from karma through karma—neither body nor mouth yet able to purify all—this is called departing.

Good sons, there is no dharma that can destroy or create. The nature of conditioned dharmas is to arise and perish differently. Thus, this wisdom cannot depart.

Good sons, wisdom cannot be broken, fire cannot burn it, water cannot drown it, wind cannot move it, earth cannot bear it, birth cannot give rise to it, aging cannot age it, dwelling cannot dwell in it, destruction cannot destroy it, greed cannot greed it, anger cannot anger it, delusion cannot delude it. Because the nature of conditioned dharmas is to arise and perish easily, the true person and immortal youth never think: "I use this wisdom to destroy afflictions." Though they say, "I destroy afflictions," it is not false. Thus, they are again called beyond thought and conception.

Wondrous Joy True Person addressed the Heavenly Venerable: Now I first understand that the true person and immortal youth deeply comprehend the treasury of Dharma, which is beyond thought and conception. The subtle and wondrous Dao Dharma, the treasury of primordial yang, and those who receive and uphold it, who analyze and elucidate its principles—such meritorious virtues are profound and weighty, beyond thought and conception.

The Heavenly Venerable said: The supreme Dao dwells near humanity—how long until it perishes?

Good sons, the supreme secret essentials of primordial yang have four kinds of contemplative practices. What are the four?

First, contemplating the body as eternally pure, unstained by filth or evil.

Second, contemplating the mind as eternally settled, without deviant thoughts.

Third, contemplating that among all dharmas, there is no self.

Fourth, contemplating all phenomena with a single, equal perception.

These are the four contemplative practices.

If my disciples can receive, uphold, read, recite, transcribe, and expound their meaning, and are revered, honored, and praised by all beings, receiving various offerings—know then that the conditions for the Dao have not perished.

Good sons, when the scriptures of primordial yang are fully circulated, at that time, many of my disciples will violate precepts, commit numerous transgressions, and fail to respect and believe in such subtle and wondrous scriptures. Due to their lack of faith, they will be unable to receive, uphold, read, recite, transcribe, or explain their meaning, nor will they be revered by others or receive offerings.

Those who see others upholding these teachings yet scorn, slander, and revile them commit the sin of arrogance toward the Dharma and are not my disciples. Know that such persons will soon face annihilation.

Miaole the Perfected again addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "I personally received these scriptural teachings from the Sage. How can it be that merely slandering the Dao and its Dharma through arrogance leads to immediate destruction?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Sages conceal their forms and entrust their traces, appearing and vanishing without fixed manner. How could mere arrogance toward the Dharma destroy them? Would they perish for such a reason? If this were the principle, how could it be justified? If they did not exist, how could one speak of the Sages as having passed away?"

"Good sons, I shall now expound this meaning again. Listen carefully with single-minded attention. There are two kinds of Dharma. What are these two? The first is worldly Dharma, and the second is the Dharma of the Supreme Meaning. Worldly Dharma may be sought, but the Dharma of the Supreme Meaning cannot be sought.

"Furthermore, there are two kinds. What are these two? The first is impermanent, without self, without joy, and without purity; the second is permanent, joyful, with self, and pure. The impermanent, without self, without joy, and without purity may manifest or conceal; the permanent, joyful, with self, and pure has no manifestation or concealment.

"Furthermore, there are two kinds of Dharma. What are these two? The first is external, and the second is internal. External Dharma may be manifested, but internal Dharma cannot be manifested.

"Furthermore, there are two kinds. What are these two? The first is conditioned, and the second is unconditioned. Conditioned Dharma may be attained, but unconditioned Dharma cannot be attained.

"Furthermore, there are two kinds. What are these two called? The first is attainable, and the second is unattainable. Attainable Dharma has a beginning and an end; unattainable Dharma has no beginning or end.

"Good sons, if my disciples receive, uphold, read, recite, transcribe, and expound the Primordial Yang scriptures, reverently make offerings, honor and praise them, worship morning and evening, and contemplate the immortals, know then that the Dao and its Dharma will flourish without end.

"Good sons, have you heard that the Perfected Youth among the Realized Ones possesses this scripture?

"Good sons, the Primordial Yang scriptures are the secret treasury of all Sages. Why is this? Although the Heavenly Worthy expounds such scriptures, he does not speak of the nature of Dharma, nor does he speak of the Heavenly Worthy’s permanence, joy, self, and purity. All Perfected Ones have not fully fathomed the subtleties of the Dao. Therefore, these scriptures are called the *Thirty-Six Revered Scriptures of the Primordial Yang’s Secret Treasury*. Because they are not expounded, they are called a treasury, just as a person’s seven treasures are not used externally and are thus called a treasury.

"Good sons, people accumulate and store treasures for future contingencies. What are these future contingencies? They include storing grain for famine years, preparing for bandits invading the borders, encountering evil leaders, ransoming lives, and alleviating hardships on difficult roads. When the time comes, they distribute their wealth to provide relief.

"Good sons, the secret treasury of the Heavenly Worthies is likewise. In future ages, when evil Daoists accumulate impure things and teach the four assemblies that the Heavenly Worthy is ultimately impermanent and that offerings are in vain, when they disrespect the scriptures—when such evils appear in the world—the Heavenly Worthy, wishing to eradicate these evils and lead beings far from perverse views, will expound these scriptures for those who make offerings to the Heavenly Worthy. When the secret treasury of these scriptures is revealed without exception, the Dao and its Dharma will flourish.

"Good sons, the Primordial Yang scriptures are eternally unchanging. Why is this difficult to comprehend? Did these scriptures exist at the time of the Primordial Beginning?

"Good sons, at the time of the Primordial Beginning, all people were pure and good, abundant in wisdom. Though their natures had not yet awakened to the true Dao, their bodies and minds were pure, gentle, and easily transformed. They possessed great virtue and unshakable retention.

"Good sons, the beings of this present age are burdened with heavy greed and desire, beset by manifold afflictions. They are foolish, forgetful, lacking in wisdom, entangled in doubts, and their roots of faith are not established. The world is impure. All beings claim that the Sages are impermanent and subject to change, ultimately entering the true Dao. Therefore, the Heavenly Worthy expounds these scriptures.

"Good sons, the Dharma of the Sages is truly inexhaustible. Why is this? Because it is eternally unchanging."

"Good sons, if there are beings who perceive a self where there is no self, and perceive no self where there is a self; who perceive permanence where there is impermanence, and impermanence where there is permanence; who perceive joy where there is no joy, and no joy where there is joy; who perceive purity where there is impurity, and impurity where there is purity; who perceive truth where there is no truth, and no truth where there is truth; who perceive the Dao where there is no Dao, and no Dao where there is Dao; who perceive arising where there is no arising, and no arising where there is arising; who perceive cessation where there is no cessation, and no cessation where there is cessation—such deluded speech about the Dao is called demonic speech. Those who take such demonic speech to be true speech, with all its cunning and manifold deceptions, should know that such people will fall into the three evil destinies, never beholding good causes, submerged for ten thousand kalpas without hope of rebirth.

"Good sons, it would be better to say that one could bind the fierce wind with a rope than to dare say that the true Dao is obscured; better to say that great lotuses bloom in the midst of a raging fire than to dare say that the true Dao is obscured; better to say that the moon can be made hot and the sun made cold than to dare say that the true Dao is obscured.

"Good sons, when a true person first emerges and attains the fruit of the primordial yang’s subtle, wondrous, supreme, and perfectly true great Dao, yet has no disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, though the sage may conceal his form and transform his appearance, know that this Dharma will long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first attains the fruit of the great Dao and already has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, though the sage may transform his appearance, know that this Dharma will long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first emerges and attains the fruit of the great Dao, though he has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, yet there are no steadfast laypeople of pure faith who revere the Dao and its Dharma, the sage will pass away—know that this Dharma will long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first emerges and attains the fruit of the Dao, and already has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and there are many steadfast laypeople who revere the Dao and its Dharma, the sage will pass away—know that the true Dao will long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first emerges and attains the fruit of the great Dao, and already has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and though there are steadfast laypeople who revere the Dao and its Dharma, when those disciples expound the scriptures, they do so out of greed for profit—though this is so, they will ultimately pass away, and know that this Dharma will long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first emerges and attains the fruit of the great Dao, and already has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and there are faithful laypeople who revere the Dao and its Dharma, and those disciples, in all their teachings, are not greedy for profit but deliver beings and guide them to the true Dharma—though this is so, they will ultimately serve as guides, and know that this Dharma will long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first attains the fruit of the Dao, though he has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and there are faithful laypeople of pure faith who revere the immortals and contemplate the Dao in their hearts, yet those disciples often engage in disputes, mutually faulting one another, the sage will pass away—know that such people will not long abide in the world.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first emerges and attains the wondrous fruit, and has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and there are reverent laypeople who honor the Dao and its Dharma, and those disciples cultivate harmony and respect, never faulting one another but mutually cherishing and honoring each other, though the sage may pass away, know that this Dharma will long and unceasingly abide.

"Furthermore, good sons, when a true person first attains the fruit of the Dao, though he has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and there are reverent laypeople who honor the wondrous Dharma, and those disciples, in expounding the primordial yang’s wondrous Dharma for all beings, mutually respect one another and never engage in disputes, yet they cast aside all impure things and boast, saying, ‘I am certain to attain the fruit of the Dao’—though the sage may pass away, know that this Dharma will always abide in the world.

"Good sons, when a true person first attains the fruit of the perfectly true Dao, and already has disciples who comprehend its profound meaning, and there are moderately faithful laypeople who cherish the Dao and its Dharma, and those disciples can expound the primordial yang’s secret and profound scriptural Dharma, skillfully cultivating harmony and mutual respect, never casting aside all impure things, nor claiming that they must attain the wondrous fruit—though the sage may pass away, know that this Dharma will long abide in the world.

"Good sons, you should know: all dharmas have no fixed form, they cannot be measured or fathomed. Why is this?"

"According to the sharpness or dullness of beings’ inherent natures, the roots of their karma, and the faculties of their consciousness, some are coarse, some are subtle.

"Good sons, I now compassionately regard all beings without partiality or favoritism toward high or low, without attachment to self or others. Therefore, I now abide in the equality of the one mark, without duality or division.

"Good sons, it is like a skilled physician who administers medicine according to the root of the illness, prescribing remedies suited to the disease. The Heavenly Venerable observes the roots of beings’ afflictions and teaches them expediently, enabling them to know the scriptures and precepts and cultivate the true Dharma.

"I now save and deliver beings, removing their karmic afflictions, so that they may attain purity without remainder.

"You should now know: the sage’s abiding long in the world is not a passing away, nor does it ever cease.

"At that time, in the Primordial Yang world, the divine immortals and their retinues all attained clarity, without doubt or obstruction.

"Having attained the *dhāraṇī* of total retention and deeply comprehended the wondrous principle, the Wondrous Joy Perfected One rejoiced, praised, and reverently bowed in worship. Circumambulating seven times to the left, he spoke these verses:

The great Dao’s essence is mysterious and wondrous,
Its supreme principle most profound and subtle.
It lodges in the mark of true reality,
Adapting to the times to manifest its radiance.

Liberating all beings,
It is called the Teacher of Heaven and Humankind.
It alone compounds the wondrous medicine,
Serving as the world’s skilled physician.

Expounding the Primordial Yang’s teaching,
Its secret truth is truly worthy of reflection.
Eighty thousand disciples
All partake of its luminous majesty.

The three evil destinies are all liberated,
The five sufferings forever cease their sorrow.
Sinful spirits all return,
Hungry ghosts are fully sated.

Divine immortals now intermingle,
Jewels and jades naturally shine upon one another.
Spurring the phoenix, they journey to the Dark Capital,
Riding the simurgh, they ascend to the Purple Tenuity.

Beings, now awakened,
May hope to trust in non-action.
Today, having received this grace and love,
Their blessed fortune endures, lofty and majestic.

All the heavens rejoice in unison,
Bowing their heads in reverence before departing."

Thus concludes *The Wondrous Scripture of the Primordial Yang of the Numinous Treasure*, Scroll Six.

---

*The Wondrous Scripture of the Primordial Yang of the Numinous Treasure*, Scroll Seven
"Contemplation and Practice, Part Two"

At that time, the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning was amidst the Jeweled Canopy Grove of the Primordial Yang Realm, about to withdraw from the world. He saw a king named Good Seed lying senseless upon the ground and addressed the great assembly: "I shall now remain in the world for this king, enduring countless kalpas without entering the true Dao."

Thereupon, the Third Perfected One of Primordial Yang, named Following Karma, bowed his head and respectfully addressed the Celestial Venerable: "If you remain in the world for the sake of all beings and do not enter the true Dao, why do so solely for King Good Seed?"

The Celestial Venerable replied: "Good son, among this great assembly, not one believes I shall surely enter the true Dao. King Good Seed alone is certain that I shall ultimately and eternally perish, and thus he flails and throws himself to the ground in despair. Good son, as I have declared, I remain in the world for King Good Seed and do not enter the true Dao—such is the profound and subtle meaning you have yet to comprehend. Why is this so? When I speak of remaining, it is for all ordinary beings who commit the five heinous transgressions, and again, it is for all conditioned beings. I shall never remain in the world for the sake of unconditioned beings. Why? Because the unconditioned are not beings."

King Good Seed is one replete with afflictions. Moreover, I remain in the world for those who do not perceive the nature of the Dao. Were they to perceive the nature of the Dao, I would never remain long in the world. Why is this so? Those who perceive the nature of the Dao are no longer ordinary beings. King Good Seed has yet to arouse the mind set upon the supreme, correct, and true great Dao. Furthermore, I remain for those called the nature of the Dao; King Good Seed is called the unborn, and thus does not perceive the nature of the Dao. Because he is unborn of afflictions, he perceives the nature of the Dao; by perceiving the nature of the Dao, he abides in the correct and true Dao—this is called the unborn.

Good son, the esoteric words of the Celestial Venerable are inconceivable; the mysterious and wondrous Dharma of the Dao is inconceivable; the purity of the Perfected is inconceivable; the Primordial Yang scriptures are inconceivable.

At that time, the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning emitted the radiance of his body, adorned with eighty excellences and seventy-two marks, his light universally illuminating the realm, rendering the land cool and serene. The Primordial Yang Perfected and the great assembly of divine immortals and their retinues said to one another: "We are base and coarse, our impurities not yet exhausted—by what karmic cause do we encounter such an auspicious sign? The light emitted by the Celestial Venerable is fundamentally without origin, yet how does it suddenly arise? It is neither form nor formless, neither mark nor markless, neither non-existent nor not non-existent, neither existent nor not existent, neither white nor black, neither blue nor yellow. It is not for the sake of delivering beings that this auspicious sign appears, making visible what has form, what can be spoken of as hot or cold, blue or yellow, red or white. Though this light is thus, it truly cannot be described—by what cause does he emit this radiance?"

Then, among the assembly, a fourth Perfected named Immovable Grove replied: "This auspicious sign portends that King Good Seed’s body suffers from grave illness. He declares that in this world there are no skilled physicians to heal his body and mind, and thus the light is emitted first to heal the king’s body, then his mind."

The king said: "Perfected, does the Celestial Venerable also show partiality?"

The Perfected replied: "It is like a man with seven sons. Among these seven, one falls ill. The parents’ hearts are not unequal, yet toward the sick child, their love becomes partial. Great King, the Celestial Venerable is likewise: toward all beings, his heart is not unequal, yet toward the sinful, his love becomes partial; toward those who wander astray, he generates compassionate thoughts, while those who do not wander astray, his heart releases. Who are those who do not wander astray? They are the Celestial Venerable, the Perfected, the divine immortals, and their retinues. Among all beings, he does not regard their lineage as lowly or servile, nor their persons as base—he only regards whether beings possess a good heart. If they have a good heart, then he generates compassionate thoughts.

Great King, you should know that such an auspicious sign is the manifestation of the Celestial Venerable’s majestic virtue, which can remove the heat of afflictions from beings. Great King, you should know that the sweet dew of the Dharma is likewise. The true Dao beloved by all beings is called the sweet dew of the Dharma. It washes body and mind, enabling realization of the true Dao—this is called the skilled physician."

King Good Seed asked the fourth Perfected, Primordial Yang: "I have heard that the Celestial Venerable does not share the same abode, sit, rise, speak, laugh, or converse with evil persons, just as the great sea does not harbor corpses, and as the azure simurgh and crimson phoenix do not perch upon common trees. I observe that the Celestial Venerable is likewise. How then may we approach and see him? If we were to see him, would our bodies not sink into the earth? I observe that the Celestial Venerable would sooner draw near to tigers, wolves, lions, fierce beasts, or places of dreadful fire than approach those who commit the four or five heinous transgressions. Thus, what thoughts should I arouse in my mind to go and see the Celestial Venerable?"

The fourth Perfected, Immovable Grove, replied: "Great King, it is like one who, hungry and thirsty, seeks food and drink; like one who, ill, seeks a skilled physician; like one who, afflicted, seeks deliverance. Great King, in your quest for the fruit of the Dao, you should be likewise. Great King, the Celestial Venerable expounds the esoteric treasury of Primordial Yang even for those of perverse doubt—how much more so for you, who are not of perverse doubt, that he would not compassionately deliver you?"

The king said: "Perfected, I once heard that there are those of perverse doubt who neither believe nor listen, who cannot contemplate or grasp the meaning—why does the Celestial Venerable expound the Dharma for them?"

The Perfected replied: "Great King, it is like one who suffers from grave illness. In the night, this person dreams that his teeth and hair fall out, that he lies naked and exposed in filth, that he walks, stands, sits, and rises with the dead, hand in hand, eating and drinking, and that he passes through a road filled with venomous snakes. Upon awakening from the dream, his heart is afflicted, and because of this affliction, his bodily illness worsens. Due to the worsening illness, his family sends a messenger to summon a physician. Being poor and destitute, with no one to send, his body is stunted, his six senses incomplete, and he tells the skilled physician: 'Hurry, follow me.'

At that time, the skilled physician thinks to himself: 'Seeing this messenger, his appearance is inauspicious—I know this patient will be difficult to cure.' He further thinks: 'Though the messenger is inauspicious, I should divine whether the illness can be treated.' Thus, he observes the day, the stars, and the constellations—all are inauspicious, and so the patient will be difficult to cure. He further thinks: 'Though the day, stars, and constellations are inauspicious, I should observe the season—autumn, winter, sunset, or midnight—all are inauspicious. I know this illness will be difficult to cure.' Having thought thus, and seeing that all signs are inauspicious, though they may be uncertain, he considers the patient: if the patient has good fortune, he can be cured; if he lacks good fortune, even if the signs are auspicious, he cannot be treated. Having reflected on these matters, he immediately sets out with the messenger.

He further thinks: 'If that patient has the marks of long life, then he can be cured; if he lacks the marks of long life, then he cannot be treated.'"

Having thought thus, along the way he encountered two boys quarreling and cursing, their heads and faces streaming with blood. He saw someone carrying a great torch that suddenly extinguished itself. He saw men felling trees, or tigers and wolves and other fierce beasts. Having witnessed these things, he thought again: "All the signs I have seen are inauspicious. I know the patient will be difficult to save."

He further thought: "If I do not go, I am no true physician. Yet if I go, I cannot save him." Then he thought again: "Though all these signs are inauspicious, I am a good physician and must go to save him." Having resolved this, he heard ahead on the road the sound of wailing—people beating their breasts and striking the earth—along with the howling of dogs, the cries of birds, the roars of wild beasts, and all manner of clamorous noises shaking the land. Having heard these things, he thought again: "I know the patient will be difficult to cure."

Upon arriving at the patient’s home, he examined the illness: now cold, now hot, the head and face swollen, the body foul and putrid, the bowels and bladder obstructed, the voice gasping and labored, sleep restless. Seeing this, the physician asked the attendants: "How was the patient’s breath yesterday?" They replied: "Great master, this person was once devout and unwavering in reverence for the Three Treasures. Now, his devotion has faltered. He was once generous, but now he hoards. He once ate sparingly, but now he overindulges. He was once gentle, but now he is cruel. He was once filial and loving toward his parents, but now he shows them no respect." Hearing this, the physician knew that all signs were inauspicious and determined without doubt that the patient would die.

He said to the attendants: "I shall return for now. Tomorrow I will come again. Provide whatever the patient needs without restraint." The next day, he sent a messenger ahead, but then delayed, saying: "My affairs are not yet settled, and I have not prepared the medicine." The wise should know that such a patient will surely die.

Great King, the Heavenly Honored One is likewise: though one harbors perverse doubt, he discerns the nature of their roots and preaches the Dharma. Why? If he did not preach, all ordinary beings would say the Heavenly Honored One lacks great compassion. One with compassion is called wise. If he lacked compassion, how could he be called omniscient? The Heavenly Honored One preaches the wondrous Dharma for the sake of one perverse doubter. Great King, you should know that the Heavenly Honored One, seeing all who are ill, constantly offers wondrous medicine. If the patient does not take it, it is not that the Heavenly Honored One lacks kindness and love.

Great King, you should know that those with perverse doubt are of two kinds: those who attain good roots in the present life, and those who attain them in future lives. The Heavenly Honored One, knowing one harbors perverse doubt, preaches the Dharma for those who can attain good roots in the present, and also for those who will attain them in the future. Though it may bring no benefit now, it plants the cause for the future.

Thus, the Heavenly Honored One expounds the *Primal Yang Wondrous Sutra* for one perverse doubter, and there are two kinds: those of sharp faculties and those of middling faculties. Those of sharp faculties can attain good roots in the present life. Those of middling faculties will attain them in future lives when they encounter the Dharma.

Great King, it is like a man who has fallen into a filthy cesspit—how can he escape? A good man sees him and takes pity, seizing him by the hair and pulling him out, thus purifying him through the good man’s aid. The Heavenly Honored One’s grace and salvation are likewise: all beings have fallen into the Three Evil Paths, and he skillfully saves them, enabling them to escape the Three Evil Paths. Thus, the Heavenly Honored One expounds the *Primal Yang Treasure Repository* for one perverse doubter in the same way.

Then King Good-Seed asked the Fourth Perfected One, Impartial Grove: "If the Heavenly Honored One is truly thus, then one should choose an auspicious time and day before going." The Perfected One replied to the King: "Within the Dao’s teachings, there is no choosing of auspicious times and days. Great King, consider a gravely ill person: they do not select auspicious days or times, good or ill—they only seek a good physician. Now that your illness is grave, you seek the Heavenly Honored One, the good physician. You should not choose an auspicious time or day.

Great King, you should know that fire within wood and fire within bamboo both burn the same, with no difference. Auspicious days and inauspicious days are likewise. If one contemplates the Dao and reflects on truth, both can dissolve all karmic offenses. I only wish that you, Great King, would go swiftly today."

Then the Great King commanded a minister named Auspicious Blessing, saying: "Great minister, know that I now wish to go to the Heavenly Honored One in the Primal Yang realm. Quickly prepare all the offerings and necessities, ensuring everything is complete." The minister replied: "Great King, you wish to go to the Primal Yang realm to consult the true Dao—excellent, excellent! All the offerings and necessities are ready."

Thereupon, King Good-Seed, together with his retinue, ministers, and high officials, each adorned in pure and clean garments and with various offerings—golden-saddled steeds, all manner of carriages, banners and canopies, incense and flowers, music and entertainment, and all kinds of precious objects, nothing lacking—led a procession of tens of thousands of mounted attendants to the abode of the Heavenly Honored One in the Primal Yang realm, seeking the true Dao and wondrous medicine.

Then the Heavenly Honored One addressed the great assembly: "All ordinary beings who seek the supreme, correct, and true great Dao have no causes and conditions, nor prior good friends. Why? If King Good-Seed does not follow the Perfected One’s teachings, he will surely die within the coming month and fall into the Three Evil Paths. Therefore, to eliminate the illnesses of body and mind, nothing is better than good friends, a good physician, and wondrous medicine, which can eradicate the heavy karmic afflictions of illness."

"Great King, you should know that the *Supreme Wondrous Sutra of Primal Yang* is the excellent medicine and marvelous art for all beings. You must revere it with devotion, bow in worship, and recite it morning and evening without ceasing for years—then you shall surely attain the fruit of spontaneity."

Then the Heavenly Honored One of Primordial Beginning addressed the great assembly: "King Good-Seed still harbors doubt; I shall now resolve his mind."

At that time, among the assembly, the Sixth Perfected One of Primal Yang, named Pure Virtue, said to the Heavenly Honored One: "As previously stated, all dharmas are without fixed form—so-called form has no fixed form, so-called emptiness has no fixed form, so-called dharma has no fixed form, so-called truth has no fixed form, even the great Dao of the Unbounded has no fixed form. Why then does the Heavenly Honored One now speak of resolving King Good-Seed’s mind?"

The Heavenly Honored One replied: "Excellent, excellent! Good son, I now firmly resolve King Good-Seed’s mind. Why? If the king’s doubt can be shattered, know that all dharmas are without fixed form. Therefore, I resolve his mind—know that this mind is fixed. Good son, if the king’s mind is resolved, how can his transgressions be undone? Since there is no fixed form, his offenses may be shattered. Thus, I resolve King Good-Seed’s mind."

Then King Good-Seed proceeded to the fragrant grove beneath the towering *qian* trees and approached the Heavenly Honored One, gazing upon his majestic radiance and wondrous marks. Thereupon, the Heavenly Honored One emitted eight kinds of voices and addressed the king.

King Good-Seed looked to his left and right, asking the assembly: "Who among you is the great king? I, burdened by transgressions and devoid of merit, should not be called a king by the Heavenly Honored One."

Then the Heavenly Honored One again called out: "King Good-Seed." Upon hearing this, the king’s heart swelled with joy, and he declared: "Today, the Heavenly Honored One, out of compassion for all beings, bestows great mercy and boundless compassion, equal and without distinction."

King Good-Seed then stepped forward and said to the Heavenly Honored One: "My former doubts are now dispelled. I firmly know that the Heavenly Honored One is the supreme teacher of all beings."

At that time, the Sixth Perfected One of Primal Yang, Pure Virtue, said to the assembly: "The Heavenly Honored One has resolved King Good-Seed’s mind, allowing him to attain the natural karmic reward. His deep doubts are awakened, and his long-standing obstructions are cleared." Then, with the banners, canopies, incense, flowers, music, and offerings he held, he bowed his head in reverence, circumambulated three times to the left, and withdrew to one side.

Then the Heavenly Honored One of Primordial Beginning addressed King Good-Seed: "I shall now expound for you the wondrous method of contemplation and practice from the *Supreme Sutra of Primal Yang*, its subtle and profound meaning. You must collect your thoughts and listen attentively as I proclaim it.

All ordinary beings should constantly observe and examine their conduct in twenty matters:
First, this body and mind of mine are hollow and empty, never full.
Second, devoid of good roots, they cannot be awakened.
Third, this cycle of birth and death has not yet attained harmony."

Fourth, I have fallen into a deep pit, with no place free from fear.
Fifth, by what expedient means may I behold the true Dao?
Sixth, how should I cultivate concentration to behold the Heavenly Honored One?
Seventh, birth and death are ever suffering; there is no constancy, no self, no purity.
Eighth, the eight difficulties are hard to escape.
Ninth, I am constantly pursued by enemies.
Tenth, there is not a single good deed that can shield me from all evils.
Eleventh, I have not yet liberated myself from the three evil destinies.
Twelfth, I am replete with all manner of wicked and perverse views.
Thirteenth, I have not yet established the means to cross the ford of the five heinous transgressions.
Fourteenth, the cycle of birth and death is boundless; I have not yet attained the true path.
Fifteenth, if I do not perform deeds, I will not receive their retribution.
Sixteenth, if there is no self that acts, others will bear the fruit.
Seventeenth, without planting good causes, there will ultimately be no good effects.
Eighteenth, if one commits deeds, their fruit will never be lost.
Nineteenth, birth arises from ignorance, and death likewise follows from it.
Twentieth, in past, future, and present, I constantly act with reckless abandon.

Great King, though you are foremost among men, you should always contemplate these twenty matters regarding this body. Having made such contemplations, body and mind become pure, free from defilement, and one attains right observation. Progressing through these contemplations, observe the marks of arising, abiding, and ceasing. Likewise, observe the mind’s marks of arising, abiding, and ceasing. With mind settled, wisdom advances, and the precepts are likewise upheld. Having observed arising, abiding, and ceasing, you will know the marks of the mind and even the marks of the precepts, and will never commit evils, nor fear death or the three evil destinies.

If one does not contemplate these twenty matters with focused mind, the mind becomes reckless, and no evil remains uncommited.

King Good-Seed said: "As I understand the meaning expounded by the Heavenly Honored One, I have never before contemplated these twenty matters. Thus, I have committed many evils. Having committed evils, I now fear death and the three evil destinies. If I were to contemplate them, I would surely fall into the three wretched destinies."

The Heavenly Honored One addressed King Good-Seed: "All dharmas are by nature impermanent in their characteristics; nothing is fixed or certain. How then can you say you will surely fall into the three wretched destinies?"

King Good-Seed bowed his head and said to the Heavenly Honored One: "If all dharmas are without fixed characteristics, then my sin of killing should also be unfixed. If killing were fixed, then all dharmas would not be unfixed."

The Heavenly Honored One said: "Excellent, excellent! All true ones say that all dharmas are without fixed characteristics, and you too have understood that killing is likewise unfixed. Therefore, know that killing has no fixed characteristic.

Great King, as you have said, your father was wrongfully harmed without cause. But what is this 'father'? It is merely a provisional name for the five aggregates of sentient beings, falsely conceived as a father within the twelve dhatus and eighteen realms. What then is the father? If form is the father, the other four aggregates should not be. If the other four are the father, then form should also be. If form and the other four together constitute the father, this is impossible. Why? Because form and the non-form aggregates are by nature uncombined.

Great King, ordinary beings falsely conceive of form as a father. Yet even this form should not be harmed. Why? Form has ten aspects. Among these ten, only one aspect of form is visible and tangible, measurable, movable, and bindable. Though it may be seen and bound, its nature does not abide. Because it does not abide, it cannot be seen, grasped, measured, moved, or bound. If form is thus, how can it be killed? If form were killable, and one incurred karmic retribution for it, the other nine aspects should not be. If the other nine are not, then there should be no sin.

Great King, know that form has three phases: past, future, and present. Past and future forms cannot be harmed. Why? Because they perish in each instant. Thus, a single form may be killable or unkillable. With killing and non-killing, form is not fixed. If form is not fixed, killing is not fixed. If killing is not fixed, its retribution is not fixed. How then can you say you are destined for hell?

Great King, know that all the sins committed by sentient beings are of two kinds: light and heavy. If committed by mind and speech, they are light. If committed by body, mind, and speech, they are heavy. Great King, your thoughts and words did not involve bodily action; thus, the retribution you incur is light. In the past, you did not command killing with your words; you merely spoke of cutting off a foot without true intent. Moreover, you did not issue an edict—how then could you be fully culpable? Even the true ones should be culpable. Why? Great King, your noble birth arises from the good roots you planted in the past, born imbued with the qi of the Dao. Thus, you now occupy the royal throne. If you had not been born from good karma, you would not be a king. If you were not a king, you could not have brought harm to the kingdom. If your killing of the king-father incurs sin, then these true ones should also incur sin. If the true ones are without sin, how then can you alone be guilty?

Great King, in the past, you harbored an evil mind while hunting in the mountains. You roamed the vast wilderness but caught nothing. You saw only a perfected one, endowed with the five supernatural powers. Upon seeing him, you grew angry and resentful, thinking, 'I have hunted in vain because of this man. Drive him away!' You then ordered your attendants to kill him. As he faced death, he generated a mind of anger and hatred, lost his supernatural powers, and made this vow: 'I am innocent, yet you have wantonly slaughtered me with mind and speech. In a future life, I shall likewise harm your life with mind and speech.' Upon hearing this, you generated remorse and made offerings to his corpse."

Great King, even in such a case as this, one may incur only light retribution and not fall into hell—how much less should you, who are not like this, suffer hellish karmic consequences? The deed was first done by you, and the retribution is borne by you alone. How then can you alone incur the sin of killing?

As you say, your father the king was innocent—how then can you claim he was without fault? If one has transgressions, there is karmic retribution; if one has no evil deeds, there is no karmic retribution. If your father the former king had no transgressions, how could there be retribution? Even in the present life, Great King, you have experienced both good and evil fruits. Thus, the former king’s fate was likewise uncertain. Because it was uncertain, the act of killing was also uncertain. Since the killing was uncertain, how can you speak with certainty of falling into hell?

Great King, you should know that beings in delusion manifest four kinds of madness: first, the madness of greed, coveting all wealth and possessions; second, the madness of desire, seeking sensual pleasures to gratify the body; third, the madness of curses, harboring resentment and suspicion; fourth, the madness of karmic conditions, greedily pursuing wealth and possessions.

Great King, you should know that among my disciples are those afflicted with these four kinds of madness. Though they commit many evils, I never pronounce their fate. If one breaks the precepts under such madness, the transgression is not counted against them. If they later regain their senses, they are not said to have committed an offense.

You, Great King, were originally covetous of the kingdom and thus instigated this treasonous harm. How can such an act, born of the madness of greed, incur sin?

Great King, it is like a man who, drunk with wine, harms his own mother. Once sober, he feels remorse and regret. Know that such an act does not incur karmic retribution. You, Great King, were drunk with greed and acted against your true nature. If it was not your true nature, how can it incur sin?

It is like an illusionist at a crossroads who conjures various garments, ornaments, men and women, carriages and horses, necklaces, and robes. The foolish believe them to be real, while the wise know they are not truly existent. Killing is likewise: the common person believes it to be real, but the enlightened, with the eye of wisdom, know it is not.

Great King, you should know that it is like the echo in a mountain valley. The foolish believe it to be a real sound, while the wise know it is not. Killing is likewise: the common person believes it to be real, but the perfected ones know it is not.

Great King, it is like an enemy who feigns friendship. The foolish believe it to be genuine, while the wise discern its deceit. Killing is likewise: the common person believes it to be real, but the perfected ones know it is not.

Great King, it is like a man who sees his reflection in a mirror. The foolish believe it to be his true face, while the wise know it is not. Killing is likewise: the common person believes it to be real, but the perfected ones know it is not.

Great King, it is like a mirage in the heat. The foolish believe it to be water, while the wise know it is not. Killing is likewise: the common person believes it to be real, but the perfected ones know it is not.

Great King, it is like a city of treasures rising from the earth. The foolish believe it to be real, while the wise know it is not. Killing is likewise: the common person believes it to be real, but the perfected ones know it is not.

Great King, it is like a man who dreams of enjoying the five desires. The foolish believe it to be real, while the wise know it is not. Killing is likewise.

Great King, you should know that I fully comprehend the nature of killing, the karma of killing, its fruits, and liberation from it—thus, there is no sin. Though you know of killing, how can there be sin?

Great King, it is like a master of ceremonies who knows the properties of wine. Though he knows it, if he does not drink, he does not become drunk. Though he knows of fire, it does not burn him. You, Great King, are likewise: though you know of killing, how can there be sin?

Great King, there are beings who commit various sins when the sun rises, and when the moon rises, they engage in robbery. When the sun and moon do not rise, they commit no sins. Though the sun and moon cause them to commit sins, the sun and moon themselves incur no sin. Killing is likewise: though it arises through you, Great King, you yourself incur no sin.

Great King, you should know that in your palace, you regularly order the slaughter of sheep, yet your heart feels no fear. Why then do you feel such dread when it comes to your father, the former king? Though there is a distinction between humans and animals in status, their love of life and fear of death are no different. Why then do you treat the sheep with such lightness and indifference, while your father, the former king, fills you with deep sorrow and suffering?

Great King, the people of the world are enslaved by their attachments to servants and possessions. Driven by love, they commit acts of killing. If there is karmic retribution, it is the sin of attachment. You, Great King, are not free—how then can you be at fault?

Great King, it is like the *Sublime Scripture of Primordial Yang*: it is neither existent nor non-existent, yet it is also existent. Killing is likewise: though it is neither existent nor non-existent, it is also existent. For those with shame and remorse, it is as if non-existent; for those without shame and remorse, it is as if existent. Those who experience karmic retribution are said to be in the realm of existence.

For those with the view of emptiness, it is as if non-existent; for those with the view of existence, it is as if existent. Those with the view of existence are also said to be in the realm of existence. Why? Because those with the view of existence experience karmic consequences, while those without the view of existence do not. Those with the view of permanence are as if non-existent; those with the view of impermanence are as if existent. Those with the view of permanence cannot be said to be non-existent. Why? Because those with the view of permanence incur evil karmic retribution. Thus, those with the view of permanence cannot be said to be non-existent. For this reason, though killing is neither existent nor non-existent, it is also existent.

Great King, you should know that all beings are defined by the inhalation and exhalation of breath. To sever the inhalation and exhalation is called killing. The sages, following worldly convention, also speak of it as killing.

Great King, form is impermanent; the causes and conditions of form are also impermanent. Form arises from impermanent causes. How then can it be permanent? Even consciousness is impermanent. The causes and conditions of consciousness are also impermanent. Consciousness arises from impermanent causes.

How can the permanent arise from the impermanent, thus suffering, thus empty, thus marked by emptiness, thus devoid of self? If it is impermanent, suffering, empty, and devoid of self, then what is being killed? Through the impermanent, one attains the permanent; the sage kills suffering to obtain joy, kills emptiness to obtain reality, kills the formless to obtain the true form.

Great King, you should know that if one kills the impermanent, the suffering, the empty, and the formless, then one becomes identical with them. The act itself is like killing, yet it is impermanent, suffering, empty, and formless—thus one does not fall into hell. How then do you enter?

At that time, King Shanzhong said: As the Heavenly Venerable has expounded, contemplating form up to contemplating consciousness—having performed this contemplation, he addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: Now I have only just realized that form is impermanent, and that consciousness is impermanent. Had I been able to contemplate thus from the beginning, I would not have committed these transgressions.

He then bowed his head reverently and respectfully addressed the Heavenly Venerable: I once heard that sages always act as parents to all beings. Though I had heard these words, I did not fully comprehend them. Now I know with certainty that the Heavenly Venerable is truly the parent of all beings.

I also once heard that the Jade Capital Mountain is composed of four treasures—gold, silver, lapis lazuli, and agate—and that if there are many horses gathered there, they all take on the same color. Though I had heard this, I did not fully grasp its truth. Now that I have come to Jade Capital Mountain and seen that all things here share the same color, I have come to understand that the Dharma is impermanent, suffering, empty, and formless. Having performed this contemplation, I see that all dharmas are entirely impermanent. All dharmas are without root; I did not initially understand that being without root means not believing in the true Dao. Now, by good fortune, I have met the Heavenly Venerable, who has revealed profound mysteries and elucidated the true scripture. The merit thus attained can destroy the afflictions and evil minds of all beings.

The Heavenly Venerable said: Great King, excellent, excellent! Now I know that you will surely be able to dispel the evil minds of beings and break the bonds of their afflictions.

The Great King again addressed the Heavenly Venerable: If I can truly understand and destroy the evil minds of all beings, then even if I were to endure great suffering for immeasurable kalpas in the twenty-four hells of Mount Tai for the sake of all beings, I would not regard it as suffering.

At that time, there were countless worldly beings who did not believe in the true Dao and were constantly beset by perverse doubts. Upon hearing these words, foolish people all aroused the mind aspiring to the supreme, correct, and true Great Dao. Because of the boundless compassion of these innumerable people who aroused the great mind of loving-kindness, the grave transgressions of King Shanzhong were immediately diminished.

The king, his queen, and the ladies of the palace, seeing the king’s clear understanding of the marks of the Dharma and his purity of body and mind, all together aroused the mind aspiring to the supreme, natural Dao.

Then King Shanzhong addressed the Heavenly Venerable: Though I have not yet died, I have already gained deep understanding of the true essence. I have abandoned a short lifespan to attain longevity, and forsaken an impermanent body to obtain a truly permanent body. By inspiring all beings to arouse the mind aspiring to the supreme, correct, and true Dao, they attain a long lifespan and a truly permanent body, becoming true and eternal disciples of the Heavenly Venerable.

Having spoken these words, he offered the Heavenly Venerable various jeweled banners, canopies, incense, flowers, music, and all manner of exquisite treasures, garments, and adornments. He further praised the Heavenly Venerable in verse, saying:

The Heavenly Venerable’s body is profound and wondrous,
Virtue and power crown the Great Clarity.
Carefree, he strides through the Golden Gates,
At ease, he roams the Jade Capital.

Expounding the primal yang’s meaning,
The ultimate principle is most majestic.
This is called the nectar medicine,
Also named the Mahāyāna sutra.

Whether one believes or not,
Receiving and upholding it, sins naturally vanish.
Compassion saves from suffering,
Cherishing all beings with kindness.

If one can fathom its deep meaning,
One will meet in the Mystic Capital’s court.
The formless lodges in form,
The shapeless lodges in shape.

All good spiritual friends,
Must be utterly sincere.
Dwell on a single verse,
Gather the mind, sever worldly attachments.

Having parted from the bonds of affliction,
The Dao-nature naturally becomes clear.
Immortals will protect you,
Carefree, the body becomes light.

At that time, King Shanzhong, having received the Heavenly Venerable’s earnest instruction and enlightenment, together with his retinue, all awakened to the esoteric scripture of the primal yang. Deeply understanding cause and effect, they praised in verse and expressed gratitude to the Heavenly Venerable. Having paid their respects and circumambulated three times, they took their leave and returned each to their own kingdom.

Thus concludes *Scroll Seven of the Supreme Numinous Treasure Primal Yang Wondrous Scripture*.

*Scroll Eight of the Supreme Numinous Treasure Primal Yang Wondrous Scripture: The Chapter on Virtuous Conduct*

At that time, the Noble Perfected One of Supreme Virtuous Conduct of the Primal Yang, Yin Miaolin, together with his disciples and retinue—the foremost of the Eight Kinds of Wisdom—and an immeasurable assembly, gathered beneath the fragrant trees of the Qianshu Grove. Bowing their heads in reverence, they circumambulated three times, then knelt on one knee, holding tablets, and inquired of the Primordial Heavenly Venerable: "By fortune’s turn, we have encountered the Sagely Venerable. We dare to present the doubts that linger in our hearts, humbly beseeching your divine countenance to grant us instruction."

The Heavenly Venerable smiled and said, "Excellent, excellent! Profound indeed is your question. I shall resolve it as you ask."

Miaolin respectfully inquired: "Do ordinary beings who commit transgressions and grave offenses possess the Dao-nature? If such persons exist, why do they fall into hell? If they do possess the Dao-nature, why is it said there is no true and eternal bliss? If one who severs good roots is called an ordinary being, when good roots are severed, how is it that the Dao-nature is not also severed? If it is severed, why is it still said there is true and eternal bliss? If it is not severed, why is such a one called an ordinary being?"

The Heavenly Venerable replied: "Those who violate the Four Illuminated Precepts are called ‘indeterminate.’ Those who slander the *Primal Yang Sutra*, commit the Ten Evil Acts, or become ordinary beings are all termed ‘indeterminate.’ If such persons were determinate, by what cause and condition could they attain the supreme, correct, and spontaneous Great Dao, achieve the fruition of the Nine Immortals, or even become Enlightened Perfected Ones? They are also ‘indeterminate.’ If the fruition of the Nine Immortals or the state of Enlightened Perfected Ones were determinate, they would not attain the supreme, correct, and spontaneous Great Dao. If the Heavenly Venerable were to violate the Four Covenants and be ‘indeterminate,’ then the ranks of the Nine Immortals and the Enlightened Perfected Ones would also be ‘indeterminate.’ Thus, all heavenly and sagely beings would likewise be ‘indeterminate.’ If the Heavenly Venerable is ‘indeterminate,’ then the Dharma-nature of the Primal Yang—and indeed all dharmas—would also be ‘indeterminate.’ Why are they ‘indeterminate’? If an ordinary being, upon ceasing to be an ordinary being, attains the true Dao, then all heavenly and sagely beings should be the same. Having entered the ranks of the Primal Yang, they should also be able to depart from them. If this were so, the nature of the Primal Yang would be ‘indeterminate.’ Because it is ‘indeterminate,’ it should be understood that there is no true and eternal bliss. How then can it be said that ordinary beings may enter the ranks of immortals?"

At that time, the Formless Heavenly Venerable addressed the Noble Perfected One of Supreme Virtuous Conduct, Yin Miaolin: "Excellent, excellent! Good man, you ask this to benefit immeasurable ordinary beings and all sentient beings, that they may attain joy, and out of compassion and loving-kindness for all beings. You seek to nurture the spontaneous arising of the mind in all Perfected Ones and Daoists, and thus pose such questions. Good man, you have long drawn near to the Eight Kinds of Perfected Ones of the Primal Yang and have performed many meritorious deeds within the Dharma of the Heavenly Venerable. You have already attained the true Dao, and your virtues have subdued demonic adversaries, causing them to retreat. You have guided immeasurable beings to ascend to the ranks of Primal Yang immortals and comprehend the profound and wondrous scriptures of the Great Vehicle. You have inquired of the heavenly and sagely beings across as many kalpas as the sands of the Ganges. Such profound meanings I have never seen—neither in the world nor among gods or humans—even among beginning disciples who might question the Heavenly Venerable on these matters. Now, listen attentively, and I shall explain each point in detail.

"Good man, an ordinary being is also ‘indeterminate.’ If one were determinate, such an ordinary being would never attain the spontaneous Dao.
