Because they are ‘indeterminate,’ the Dao-nature is not severed, as you have said. How is it that an ordinary being severs good roots? Perfected One and Daoist, good roots are of two kinds: the inner Dao-nature and the outer Dao-nature. Neither inner nor outer, for this reason the Dao-nature is not severed. There are also two kinds: the defiled and the undefiled. The Dao-nature is neither defiled nor undefiled, and thus it is not severed. There are two kinds: the constant and the inconstant. The Dao-nature is neither constant nor inconstant, and thus it is not severed. If it were severed, it should be recoverable. If it cannot be recovered, it is not severed. If, once severed, it is recovered, one is called an ordinary being.

"Those who violate the Four Covenants are also ‘indeterminate.’ If they were determinate, violators of the Four Precepts would never attain the supreme, correct, and spontaneous Great Dao. Those who slander the Great Vehicle scriptures of the Primal Yang and the Three Radiant Dharma Masters are also ‘indeterminate.’ If they were determinate, slanderers of the true Dharma would never attain the wondrous spontaneous Dao. Those who commit the Ten Evil Acts are also ‘indeterminate.’ If they were determinate, evildoers would never attain the correct and true Dao.

"Form and appearance are both ‘indeterminate.’ Fragrance, taste, touch, birth, ignorance, the aggregates, sense-fields, and realms—all appearances are entirely ‘indeterminate.’

"Good man, it is like a master of illusions who, amidst a great assembly, conjures various transformations—mountains, forests, trees, cities, and villages. Among the crowd, some ordinary beings, lacking wisdom, see these and believe them to be real. The wise among them know them to be deceptive, mere illusions that delude the eyes. Good man, all ordinary beings, even the disciples of immortals and Enlightened Perfected Ones, perceive all dharmas as real in just this way. The Perfected Ones and Immortals do not see the true aspect of all dharmas.

"Good man, it is like a child in the scorching heat of summer seeing a mirage and calling it water. A wise person, seeing this heat, would never conceive of it as real water. It is but a deceptive illusion, not true water. All ordinary beings and disciples of immortals perceive dharmas in this way, believing them to be real."

The Perfected Ones of the heavens do not perceive the true aspect of all dharmas. Good man, it is like the echo in a mountain valley—ordinary beings hear it and believe it to be a real sound, while the wise understand there is no fixed reality, only the sound’s appearance deluding the ear’s perception. Good man, all ordinary beings and disciples of immortals perceive all dharmas in this way, seeing them as having true aspects. The Perfected Ones of the heavens clearly understand that all dharmas are without true aspect, perceiving the marks of impermanence, emptiness, and quiescence, without marks of arising or cessation. For this reason, the Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts see all dharmas as impermanent.

Good man, there is also a fixed aspect—what is this fixed aspect? The true and constant bliss—where does it reside? It is said to be within the primordial yang dharma. Good man, the natural fruit is also not fixed. Because it is not determined, after a hundred thousand kalpas, one attains the natural mind of the supreme great Dao. Yet even this Dao-fruit is not real, for it is not fixed in reality. After eighty thousand kalpas, one attains the natural mind of the true and perfect great Dao. The fruit of the Perfected One is also not real, for it is not fixed in reality; after sixty thousand kalpas, one attains the supreme mind of the Dao. The fruit of the immortal is also not real, for it is not fixed in reality; after forty thousand kalpas, one attains the supreme mind of the Dao. The fruit of the enlightened Perfected One is also not real, for it is not fixed in reality; after twenty thousand kalpas, one attains the supreme mind of the Dao.

Good man, the Heavenly Venerable now, beneath the azure forest trees of the Sweet Dew Great City, manifests awe-inspiring virtue, divine powers, and wisdom, causing the disciples of immortals and all ordinary beings to wholeheartedly uphold the dharma, sincerely submit to the truth, and recite the profound and mysterious meanings of the supreme Mahāyāna scriptures of primordial yang. Thus they attain the supreme, true, and natural great Dao, cultivate the sagely practices, and never regress.

Good man, ordinary beings who do not properly restrain the six senses will have leaks and be led by evil to unwholesome places. Good man, it is like a fierce and unruly horse that brings its rider to perilous places. Those who do not properly restrain the six senses through evil karma are likewise led far from the wondrous Dao of primordial yang to evil destinations. It is like an untamed mad elephant—if someone rides it, it will not go where intended, but instead strays far from good towns to dangerous places. Those who do not properly restrain the six senses through evil karma are likewise led far from the good towns of primordial yang into the perilous wilderness of birth and death.

Good man, it is like a treacherous minister who teaches the king to do evil—the six senses, like treacherous ministers, constantly lead beings to commit boundless evils. Good man, it is like a stubborn child who ignores the teachings of parents and teachers and commits all manner of evil. Those who do not discipline the six senses are likewise unwilling to accept the good instructions of parents and teachers, committing every kind of evil.

Good man, ordinary beings who do not restrain the six senses are constantly harmed by hell-dwellers, animals, and hungry ghosts, just as enemies and thieves harm the good. Ordinary beings who do not restrain the six senses gallop through the six dusts like a careless cowherd whose cattle trample others’ crops. Ordinary beings who do not guard the six senses constantly remain in the cycle of existence, suffering manifold afflictions.

Good man, when Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts cultivate the sagely practices of the supreme Mahāyāna of primordial yang, they constantly and skillfully discipline and guard the six senses, fearing greed, anger, jealousy, and arrogance, all for the sake of attaining all dharmas. Good man, if one can guard the six senses, one can guard the mind; if one can guard the mind, one guards the six senses. It is like someone who protects the king and defends the kingdom—guarding the kingdom means guarding the king. Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts are likewise: if they can hear the supreme Mahāyāna scriptures of primordial yang, they attain wisdom; having attained wisdom, they can then strictly guard the six senses.

Good man, it is like a good cowherd—if the cattle stray and eat others’ crops, he can stop them and prevent them from damaging things. Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts are likewise: through the causes and conditions of mindfulness and wisdom, they guard the six senses and do not allow them to run wild. Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts who possess mindfulness and wisdom do not perceive the mark of self, the mark of sentient beings, or the mark of what is enjoyed; they see all dharmas as sharing the same dharma-nature. They perceive the forms of mountains, grasses, trees, tiles, and pebbles as like houses—arising from causes and conditions, without fixed nature. Seeing all ordinary beings and sentient beings as constituted by the four great elements, they discern there is no fixed nature. Because there is no fixed nature, the Perfected Ones do not generate attachment. Ordinary beings, seeing sentient beings, thus give rise to afflictions. Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts who cultivate the scriptures of primordial yang, possessing mindfulness and wisdom, do not generate attachment to sentient beings.

Again, Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts who cultivate the scriptures of primordial yang do not cling to the marks of sentient beings or create various dharmas. Good man, it is like a painter who, using various colors, depicts cows, horses, men, and women—ordinary beings without wisdom see them and conceive the marks of men and women, but the painter knows there are no marks of men, women, cows, or horses. Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts are likewise: observing the different marks of dharmas as one mark, they never conceive the thought of sentient beings. Why? Because they possess mindfulness and wisdom.

Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts who cultivate the supreme Mahāyāna scriptures of primordial yang, when they sometimes behold beautiful women, never generate a mind of attachment. Why? Because they skillfully observe marks. Good man, Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts know the marks of the five desires—there is no joy in them, no lasting abiding. They are like a dog gnawing a dry bone, like a man carrying fire against the wind, like bubbles on water or drawings on its surface, like woven threads or paintings, like a prisoner going to the market, like borrowed power that cannot bring lasting joy. The desires are likewise, full of manifold faults.

Furthermore, Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts observe that all ordinary beings and sentient beings, on account of form, fragrance, flavor, and touch, have endured suffering and affliction for kalpas without measure. For each sentient being, the bones accumulated in a single kalpa would tower as high as Mount Sumeru; the milk they have drunk would equal the waters of the four seas; and the blood they have shed would be even greater. Among their six kinds of kin and relatives, when one dies and they weep, the tears they shed would surpass the four great seas. Even if all the grasses and trees on earth were made into counting rods, they could not tally the number of one’s parents. For kalpas uncountable, some have languished in the Three Wretched Realms or the dark prisons of hell, enduring sufferings beyond reckoning.

Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts, contemplating all sentient beings so profoundly, see that on account of desire they suffer boundlessly. Thus, in the cycle of birth and death, Perfected Ones practice goodness without losing mindfulness and wisdom. Good man, it is like a great assembly filling an area of thirty *li*, where a king named Majestic commands a minister named Wealthy Grove to carry a large basin of oil through the crowd without spilling a single drop, on pain of execution. He also dispatches another minister named Forest Governor to follow behind with drawn sword, keeping watch. The minister carrying the oil, having received the king’s command, holds it with utmost care. Though he passes through the crowd and sees beautiful women, he dares not look at them. His heart trembles with fear: if he were to grow lax and become attached to that perverse desire, he would drop what he carries and fail to preserve his life. Such is his terror that he does not dare spill even a single drop of oil.

Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts, firmly upholding the precepts, are likewise: in the cycle of birth and death, they do not lose mindfulness and wisdom. Because they do not lose this cause, though they see the five desires, their minds do not cling to them. When they see pure forms, they do not generate the mark of form; they only observe the mark of suffering. Likewise with the mark of perception and the other marks: they do not create the mark of arising, nor the mark of ceasing, nor the mark of cause, nor the mark of condition. They observe all dharmas as the mark of harmony.

At that time, because the six senses of Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts are pure, their precepts are complete. All ordinary beings, whose six senses are not at peace, cannot restrain and uphold them—they are called “leaky roots.” Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts forever sever all leaks, and thus are without leakage. The Heavenly Worthy pulls them out, forever removing the karmic roots of the senses, and they attain purity.

Then the Perfected One, Exquisite Grove, having heard this, rejoiced in his heart and spoke these verses:

Ordinary beings and all sentient beings,
Not knowing the purport of the Mahāyāna,
Sink in the river of birth and death,
Treading the steps of affliction again and again.
Thought after thought, they commit evils;
Mind after mind, they arouse doubt and awakening.
Māras and demons assail them with expedient means,
And adversaries bring forth litigation.
They receive retribution and descend to hell,
Imprisoned in dark cells, bound fast.
All their karmic offenses
Cannot be likened even with counting rods.
One should bear in mind the Primordial Yang Sutra,
Receive and uphold the precepts and the Dharma.
Transgressions may thus be dissolved,
And blessings and virtues pour down like rain.
Liberation is the gate of the Mahāyāna;
The path is pure and non-active.
Heavenly immortals constantly guide them,
And earth spirits ever protect them.
If one recites such verses day after day,
Through kalpas they will be free from sorrow,
And throughout the year, no decay or harm.
In perilous and difficult places,
They will have no fear.
Receive sincerely the verses of the Five Penetrations,
And firmly uphold the Six Perfections.
Today I speak this hymn,
Which may serve as a rhapsody of eternal joy.

The Perfected One, Exquisite Grove, having spoken these verses, continued:

Furthermore, good man, there are those who have departed from leakage—Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts who, for the sake of the unsurpassed ambrosial Dharma-realm, leave behind all evil leaks. For what reason is it called “departing”? If one can practice the supreme Mahāyāna scriptures of primordial yang, receive, uphold, read, and recite them, and contemplate their meaning, this is called “departing.” Why? Good man, I do not see among the thirty-six revered scriptures any that can remove evil leaks like this Mahāyāna sutra.

Good man, it is like a good teacher instructing disciples: among them, those who receive the teaching do not create transgressions. Perfected Ones and Daoist adepts who cultivate the supreme Mahāyāna scriptures of primordial yang are likewise—they do not create transgressions. Good man, it is like in the world there are spells and incantations: if there is a poisonous snake, it cannot harm them. All ordinary beings who read and recite this sutra, even until the end of their lives, will have no transgressions. Good man, this great Primordial Yang Sutra is likewise.

If there are sentient beings who hear even once such a sutra as this, they will not fall into evil destinies. If there are those who copy, praise, read, recite, explain, or analyze its subtle wonders, they will attain the unsurpassed, correct, and natural Great Dao, together with the Dharma-mark of its embodiment, just as the sages attain the ambrosial flavor of the Dharma. Good man, the majestic power of this great Primordial Yang—through cultivation, reading, and recitation—brings forth such fruition of the Way.

Good man, if there are faithful disciples who wholeheartedly copy, read, and recite this sutra, explain its meaning, and for others expound and teach it to transform sentient beings, know that such a person is truly my disciple. They know the Dharma-teaching well, instruct and admonish ordinary beings, and attain the Dharma of the Way. They are those I see, those I pity—such a person truly knows the Primordial Yang scriptures I speak.

Wherever such a person dwells—whether in mountains, forests, open wilderness, cities, villages, houses, or palaces—I too am there, constantly abiding without change. I always accept offerings from this person, sometimes appearing as a Daoist adept or a female Daoist. Good man, good woman, you should let such people know that the Heavenly Worthy accepts their offerings of wealth and treasure.

Good man, if such a person, while sleeping, dreams of the Heavenly Worthy’s sacred form, or sees the images of Perfected Ones, the form of a Wheel-Turning Sage King, or mountains, rivers, great seas, the sun, moon, and stars, or gold, silver, and precious jewels, clothing, and bedding, know then that it is the Heavenly Worthy accepting their offerings.

Upon awakening from such dreams, one attains great joy and bliss, soon obtaining all manner of needed things. No transgressions arise, and one’s aspirations remain truly good. The Primordial Yang fully accomplishes such boundless merits, inconceivable in their vastness.

Good man, you must now receive and uphold the subtle teachings of the Dharma: If any good man practices wholesome deeds, reveres me, aligns with the marks of the Dharma, and upholds its essentials—thereby shattering the evil demons of impermanence, suffering, non-self, and impurity—desiring the carefree joy of heaven or the human realm, then upon seeing one who receives, upholds, copies, recites, or explains the meaning of the Primordial Yang scriptures, you should draw near, reverently bow, praise and honor them, and provide for their needs, ensuring nothing is lacking. This scripture is profound and wondrous, beyond all comparison. You must serve it with wholehearted devotion, without retreat or weariness, and you shall attain the natural fruit of the Dao.

Good man, I recall in the past, across kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, there was a world called Pure Clarity. There lived a sage named Wenshi Heavenly One, whose divine powers and wisdom were unmatched, and whose celestial eye was supreme. He expounded the *Primordial Yang Upper Grade Mahāyāna Sūtra* to the great assembly. At that time, I followed him.

Good man, when I heard that this sage would reveal the supreme flavor of the unsurpassed meaning to the assembly, my heart rejoiced, and I wished to make an offering. Yet my family was poor, possessing nothing, so I resolved to sell myself. But I feared my strength would fail, and no one would buy me. In that moment, I encountered a man on the road and said to him, “I wish to sell myself. Would you buy me?” The man replied, “In my household, there is labor no one can perform. If you are capable, I shall buy you.” I then asked, “What labor is it that no one can perform?” He answered, “I suffer from a grave illness. A skilled physician prescribed medicine requiring two ounces of human flesh daily. If you can provide an ounce of your flesh each day, I shall pay you ten coins of gold.” Upon hearing this, my heart filled with joy. I said to him, “Grant me the coins, and after five days, when my affairs are settled, I will come to you.” He replied, “Five days is too long. Let it be one day.”

Good man, at that time, I took the coins and went to the Heavenly Worthy’s abode. I bowed in reverence and offered all my family’s possessions. Then, with wholehearted devotion, I listened to the recitation of the scripture. Though my mind was dull, upon hearing it, I vowed to uphold these verses:

*The Heavenly Worthy speaks the essential,*
*Called the Primordial Yang Sūtra.*
*It liberates from the karma of birth and death,*
*And illumines the depths of darkness.*
*Those with wholehearted devotion*
*Shall attain a radiant, enlightened mind.*
*Their hearts gain supreme bliss,*
*And they tread the courts of the Mystic Capital.*
*Carefree, they follow the path of feathered transcendence,*
*Ascending and descending through the clouded gates.*
*In the turning wheel, they meet emptiness and stillness,*
*And in an instant, behold the true form.*
*The Southern Elixir ascends to its celestial abode,*
*While the Northern Dipper dispels the star of death.*
*Knowing I am moved by the wondrous Dao,*
*Through kalpas, I shall not sink into obscurity.*

After receiving and upholding these verses, my heart gained understanding. I then returned to the sick man’s home. Good man, though I daily provided two ounces of my flesh, through reciting the verses, I felt no suffering. Good man, by this cause and condition, his illness was cured, and I, too, was restored—my body’s skin and flesh fully intact, without wounds, scars, or foulness. I then aroused the unsurpassed, correct, and natural mind of the Dao.

The power of these verses is thus mighty. How much more so, then, is the *Primordial Yang Mahāyāna Sūtra* expounded by the Heavenly Worthy, the Great Sage? One who fully receives and upholds it, reciting it with wholehearted devotion, shall gain such benefits. Witnessing the merits of this scripture, I resolved to redouble my recitation, vowing that in the past, future, and present, I would attain the natural fruit of the Dao.

Good man, by the cause and condition of these verses, I now proclaim the wondrous *Primordial Yang Sūtra* to all disciples in this assembly. Good man, by this cause and condition, the great Primordial Yang is inconceivable, accomplishing boundless true and wholesome conditions—it is the esoteric treasury of all heavenly sages. For this reason, those who receive, uphold, read, and recite it sever all evil defilements.

What are these evils? The mad elephant, the vicious horse, the fierce ox, the savage dog, perilous cliffs and treacherous valleys, poisonous insects and ferocious beasts, raging rivers and cascading torrents, and wicked companions. If such evils become the cause of defilement, the Perfected One departs from them at once. If they do not, then he does not distance himself. If defilements increase, he leaves them; if they do not, he remains. If evil deeds arise, he abandons them; if good deeds are done, he does not depart. He constantly protects himself with wisdom, cultivating wholesome deeds and forsaking evil.

The Perfected One and Daoist adept observe their own bodies, seeing them as a great mass of suffering, the root of all evil karma. Though the body is impure, the Perfected One still examines and regards it. Why? Not out of attachment to the body, but for the sake of wholesome dharmas, for the Primordial Yang, not for birth and death, for true and constant bliss, not for impermanence and non-self. For the sake of the pure and the Dao, not for the absence of the Dao; for the One Vehicle, not for the Three Vehicles.

Good man, the Perfected One and Daoist adept must always protect their bodies. Why? If the body is not protected, life is not preserved. If life is not preserved, one cannot read, recite, copy, uphold, or make offerings to the *Primordial Yang Upper Grade Mahāyāna Sūtra*, nor explain its meaning to others or contemplate its truths. Therefore, the Perfected One and Daoist adept must diligently protect their bodies. By this principle, the Perfected One is freed from all evil defilements.

Good man, just as one who wishes to cross water must carefully protect their boat, raft, or vessel, and just as a traveler on the road must carefully guard their mount, or as a farmer sowing seeds must mindfully tend to manure and filth—so too must the Perfected One and Daoist adept, though they see this body as replete with boundless impurities, refrain from slackness or weariness in wholesome deeds for the sake of upholding the *Primordial Yang Sūtra*.

The Perfected One and Daoist adept regard the mad elephant and the wicked person as no different—why? Because both destroy the body. Yet while the Perfected One feels no fear near the mad elephant, they cultivate dread and caution toward evil companions—why? The mad elephant can only harm the body, not the mind, whereas the wicked can destroy both. The mad elephant ruins but a single impure body, while the wicked ruin countless virtuous bodies and minds. The mad elephant harms only the defiled body, but the wicked shatter the pure body and pure mind. The mad elephant destroys the physical form, while the wicked break the Dharma-body. The slaying by a mad elephant does not lead to the three destinies, but the killing by the wicked assuredly does. Thus, the mad elephant is but an enemy to the body, while the wicked are foes to wholesome dharmas.

Therefore, the Perfected One must always shun all unwholesome companions and the wicked. Ordinary people, unable to distance themselves from mad elephants or the wicked, thus generate defilements; but the Perfected One and Daoist adept, by keeping far from them, do not.

If even the Perfected One remains free from defilements, how could the Primordial Heavenly Worthy, possessed of great majesty and numinous power, bear any? For what reason would one draw near to defilements? All ordinary beings, in seeking clothing, food, bedding, medicine, and fine flavors for the pleasure of body and mind, pursue such things and thereby commit transgressions. Unaware of the flavor of Dharma, they revolve through the three destinies—this is what constitutes defilement. The Perfected One and Daoist adept, perceiving such transgressions, thus keep far from them.

When they require clothing or food, they accept it not for the body’s sake but for the sake of Dharma. They do not grow arrogant or careless but maintain a gentle and humble mind, not for ostentation but for modesty. Though they partake of food and drink, their minds remain free from attachment, not for the body’s sake but always for the sake of the true Dharma. Not for the flesh but for sentient beings. Not out of arrogance but to sustain their strength. Not to cause harm but to remedy hunger and thirst. Even when they obtain the finest flavors, their hearts remain free from craving. The same applies to the acceptance of clothing.

They do not allow the fetters of greed and pride to dwell in their minds, seeking not longevity but the eternal life of Dharma. Good man, they reflect thus: *If I do not accept such offerings, my body will waste away and lack strength. Without strength, I cannot endure hardship; without endurance, I cannot cultivate the true Way. But if I endure hardship, I can cultivate the true Way and attain boundless virtue. If I cannot bear these sufferings, I will give rise to anger amid hardship, to craving amid pleasure, and to ignorance when pleasure is unobtainable. Thus do ordinary beings generate defilements from offerings.*

The Perfected One and Daoist adept, through profound contemplation, do not generate defilements—hence they are called "undefiled." For what reason would the Heavenly Worthy be called "defiled"? Therefore, the sage is not called "defiled."

Good man, though all ordinary beings may be said to protect body and mind, they still give rise to evil thoughts. For this reason, even if they sever afflictions and attain the state of neither perception nor non-perception, they ultimately fall into the three evil destinies. Good man, it is like one who, crossing a vast sea, seeks the far shore but drowns at the brink of arrival. So too do the foolish: on the verge of exhausting the three realms of existence, they fall back into hell. Why? Because they lack wholesome wisdom.

What is wholesome wisdom? It is what is called the six recollections. Ordinary beings possess a feeble and inferior good mind, while their unwholesome impulses rage fiercely. Because their good mind is feeble and inferior, their wisdom is slight and scant. And because their wisdom is scant, they increase all defilements.

The Perfected One and Daoist adept, with pure wisdom-eye, perceive all faults and harms—these manifest in manifold ways, ever opposing all ordinary beings as adversaries of the Three Vehicles. For this reason, they cause ordinary beings to fail in seeing the marks of the Dharma, and for kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, to generate inverted thoughts, claiming that the gods and sages possess no true constancy or bliss, that only purity exists, and that the Heavenly Worthy is ultimately void and empty.

All ordinary beings, being impermanent, devoid of bliss, impure, and without self, yet with inverted minds, assert the existence of true bliss. The Perfected One and Daoist adept should contemplate thus: all Perfected Ones, at times due to certain conditions, ought to arouse vigilance, just as a person of uprightness, purity, and cleanliness does not accept filth and defilement, like one who grasps an iron pellet—none would receive it.

Good man, those who wholeheartedly devote themselves to the Dao are likewise bound by such conditions. The Perfected One and Daoist adept reflect: all ordinary beings know me as a vast field of blessings. How then could I accept such evil? If I were to accept evil dharmas, I would be unworthy of serving as a field of blessings for all ordinary beings. Though I myself do not claim to be a good field of blessings, all ordinary beings, upon seeing my appearance, would say that I have generated such evil thoughts, thereby deceiving all ordinary beings. At the time of the Dharma, due to this deception, I would wander in the cycle of birth and death for kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, falling into hell.

If I harbor evil thoughts and accept offerings made in reliance upon me, all sages would bear witness to this. If I entertain evil thoughts and accept offerings made in reliance upon me, I may cause the donor’s karmic retribution to become meager or even nonexistent. If I am evil and accept offerings made in reliance upon me, I become a great enemy to the donor.

All ordinary beings constantly direct good thoughts and recollections toward me. How then could I deceive them and generate evil thoughts? For what reason? It may cause the donor to fail in accruing meritorious karma or to receive scant retribution. I constantly proclaim myself a Daoist adept. A Daoist adept ought not to generate evil; if one does, one is no Daoist adept. The essence of the Daoist adept lies in the harmony of body and speech. If they are not in harmony, one is no Daoist adept.

I have abandoned affection, family, companions, and kin to leave the household life and study the Dao, cultivating right mindfulness and gathering wholesome thoughts—this is not the time to gather unwholesome thoughts. It is like one who crosses the sea in search of treasure but forsakes the true pearl to take mere gold dust; or like one who abandons exquisite music to listen to harsh sounds.

As one who abandons the main chamber to love a mere concubine; as one who forsakes golden vessels to take clay bowls; as one who discards the sweet dew of the Dharma’s flavor to consume poisonous fare; as one who leaves good men to befriend evil companions; as one who rejects a skilled physician to trust in shamans and spirits; as one who abandons the sweet Dharma-food of the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning to partake of the varied bitter flavors of demonic enmity—

I have now encountered the pure and luminous Dharma-treasure of Primordial Yang, so rarely seen or heard, as a blind turtle chances upon a great floating log. Human life is perilous and fragile, like an autumn leaf; having attained deliverance today, how could I know when enlightenment will dawn?

How then could I indulge the six senses and commit evil deeds? Youth and vigor pass in but a moment. How could I allow arrogance to arise? Like a demon lying in wait for human faults, or the four great malevolent spirits shaking the sovereign of the body, so too do they ever seek my transgressions. How could I permit evil thoughts to arise?

Like a crumbling wall, my life too stands on the verge of collapse. How could I give rise to evil karma? I am called a Daoist adept, one who ought to comprehend all things—how then do I commit unwholesome deeds? How can I still be called a Daoist adept? I am called one who has left the household life; one who leaves the household life is called one who cultivates the good Dao—how then do I commit evil? How can I be called one who has left the household?

I am called a true person; the essence of a true person is to shatter afflictions—yet I do not shatter evil thoughts and afflictions. How then can I be called a true person? The world possesses six roots, which are difficult to perfect; I have now perfected them. How could I allow evil thoughts to dwell in my mind? What are these six?

The six are: first, the great Dao is difficult to encounter; second, the true Dharma is difficult to behold; third, the arising of a good mind is difficult; fourth, birth in the central land is difficult; fifth, encountering the human realm is difficult; sixth, the faculties of the body are difficult to complete. These six roots are difficult to perfect, yet I have perfected them—therefore, I ought not to give rise to evil thoughts.

When a true person cultivates the *Primordial Yang Sutra* in this manner, they must constantly observe all evil thoughts. Ordinary beings do not see the faults and harms of such evil thoughts and thus incur the defilements. The true person, having seen them, does not accept or become stained by them; therefore, the true person is free from defilements. How then could one say the Celestial Worthy is defiled? For this reason, all sages are not defiled.

Thereupon, the celestial perfected ones, immortals, and Daoist adepts, having heard this matter, rejoiced, paid homage, and with reverence spoke these verses:

We, this great assembly,
Have heard the subtle and profound meaning,
Each awakening to the nature of suffering and emptiness,
Deeply comprehending the wisdom of Primordial Yang.

Were we not scholars of the utmost learning,
How could we discern truth from falsehood?
We sever all afflictions,
Dispelling anger and hatred.

Men and ordinary beings,
Listen carefully to this true and good analogy,
Wash clean the illnesses of body and mind,
The filth, evil, and defilements.

All the divine immortals
Bow their heads in praise of this auspicious teaching.

Thus concludes *The Wondrous Sutra of the Numinous Treasure of Primordial Yang*, Scroll the Eighth.
*The Wondrous Sutra of the Numinous Treasure of Primordial Yang*, Scroll the Ninth.

At that time, the Most High Lord of the Primordial Beginning addressed the Perfected One of Primordial Yang, saying: "Good sons and good daughters, if there are those who cultivate and make offerings to *The Wondrous Sutra of the Numinous Treasure of Primordial Yang*, they shall attain ten kinds of virtue and power—unfathomable, astonishing to those who hear of them.

Neither hidden nor manifest, neither departing nor arriving, neither arising nor ceasing, neither difficult nor easy, neither form nor non-form, such are the characteristics of this Dharma. It has no shape or appearance, and is absent from the world.

What are the ten kinds of virtue and power? First, there are five. What are these five?

1. What was unheard before can now be heard.
2. Having heard the profound and wondrous, one can bring benefit.
3. One can sever all doubts and embody the ultimate principle.
4. The mind of wisdom is upright and without crookedness.
5. One deeply knows the secret treasury of Primordial Yang.

These are the five matters.

What is meant by 'what was unheard before can now be heard'? It refers to the most profound and wondrous meaning: all sentient beings possess the nature of the Dao, and all scriptures and Dharmas are without distinction. If good sons and good daughters, with sincere aspiration, dedicate themselves to the ultimate realization of the Dharma, they shall enter the supreme, correct, and true Dao—abiding without change, ever without retreat.

Neither conditioned nor unconditioned, neither defiled nor undefiled, neither form nor formless, neither empty nor non-empty, neither named nor unnamed, neither characterized nor uncharacterized, neither existent nor non-existent, neither cause nor non-cause, neither fruit nor non-fruit, neither luminous nor non-luminous, neither dark nor non-dark, neither emerging nor non-emerging, neither impermanent nor non-impermanent, neither severed nor non-severed, neither past nor non-past, neither future nor non-future, neither dependent origination nor non-dependent origination. Such Dharmas are most profound, most wondrous, most mysterious, most abstruse—what was unheard before is now heard, what was unseen before is now seen.

All scriptures, all methods, all arts and skills, all disciplines and precepts—such teachings, never heard before, are now fully comprehended through this sutra. Furthermore, the secret essentials of the Three Clarities and the divine charts of the Seven Divisions—such profound and abstruse meanings are now known through this sutra.

Good sons and good daughters, this is what is meant by 'what was unheard before can now be heard.' Having heard it, this is the great benefit. If one can recite, uphold, and embody the natural intent of the Dao, one will fully comprehend all methods and the profound meaning of the Mahayana scriptures.

It is like a person gazing into a bright mirror, seeing their reflection clearly without obstruction. The precious mirror of Primordial Yang is likewise: when the Perfected One holds it, they behold the profound and abstruse meaning of the Primordial Yang scriptures. It is also like a person in a dark room holding a great torch, seeing all things clearly. The torch of the Primordial Yang Dharma is likewise: when the Perfected One holds it, they behold the profound mysteries of Primordial Yang.

It is also like the sun rising from the Valley of Light, radiating great illumination, fully illuminating all, enabling one to see far into the empty sky. The pure sun of wisdom of the Great Primordial Yang is likewise: it illuminates the deepest and most obscure places, enabling all sentient beings to see the true Dao from afar. Why is this so? By listening to and receiving this supreme and wondrous sutra of Primordial Yang, all attain the supreme fruit of the Dao.

Good sons, if one wholeheartedly recites the subtle and wondrous scriptures of Primordial Yang, one will know the names of all Dharmas, penetrate their profound meanings, and expound them widely to others, awakening ordinary beings and enabling them to understand the ultimate principles of the Primordial Yang Dharmas. Good sons, those who listen may know the words of the Primordial Yang scriptures but not their profound meaning. If one copies, upholds, recites, and expounds them to others, guiding the deluded to understand their meaning, then one will know their meaning—this is the great benefit, increasing the bridge of the Dharma.

Furthermore, good sons, those who listen to this sutra may hear of the Dao and its methods but not yet see them. With sincere aspiration, they shall attain comprehension. By copying, reciting, and expounding it to others, contemplating its meaning, they shall come to see it. Those who listen to the Primordial Yang sutra may hear of divine powers but not yet see them. With aspiration and longing for immortality, after forming such thoughts, they shall know the Dharma, embody the intent of the Dao, and penetrate its source. In places feared by heavenly demons, evil spirits, tigers, wolves, and poisonous beasts, they shall be without fear. They shall elucidate and distinguish jade tablets and golden texts, cinnabar chapters and purple characters, expounding their meaning without error. Without hearing from others, they shall know for themselves the intent of the supreme, correct, and true Dao. This is what is meant by 'having heard the profound and wondrous, one can bring benefit.'

Furthermore, in severing doubts, there are two kinds: doubt regarding names and doubt regarding meanings. Those who listen to this sutra sever their doubting minds. Those who contemplate its meaning sever their doubt regarding its meaning.

Moreover, good sons, there are five kinds of doubt:
1. Doubt whether the Dao’s emptiness has a definite referent.
2. Doubt whether the Dao’s elusive nature is truly eternal.
3. Doubt whether the Dao’s secrecy is truly blissful.
4. Doubt whether the Dao’s profundity is truly pure.
5. Doubt whether the Dao’s manifestation or concealment is its true meaning.

Those who listen to this sutra shall forever sever their doubting minds. By copying, reciting, expounding it to others, and contemplating its meaning, the five doubts shall be forever severed.

Furthermore, good sons, there are three kinds of doubt:
1. Doubt whether the supreme, correct, and true Dao is conditioned or unconditioned.
2. Doubt whether the thirty-six revered scriptures are conditioned or unconditioned.
3. Doubt whether all wondrous Dharmas are conditioned or unconditioned."

Those who hear this sutra shall forever extinguish these three doubts without remainder. By copying, reciting, expounding it widely to others, and contemplating its meaning, they shall come to understand that all sentient beings possess the Dharma-nature.

Furthermore, good sons, if there are sentient beings who have not heard this *Primordial Yang* scripture, their doubts shall be manifold—doubting whether things are eternal or not eternal, blissful or not blissful, pure or not pure, possess a self or not, possess a lifespan or not, are ordinary beings or not, are ultimate or not ultimate, pertain to the future or not, exist or not, are suffering or not, are bliss or not, are the Dao or not, are cessation or not, are Dharma or not, are real or not. Those who hear this sutra shall sever all such delusions.

Furthermore, good sons, if there are those who have not heard this sutra, there are also various sentient beings beset by many doubts: Is form the self? Do sensation, perception, mental formations, and consciousness arise interdependently? Is form the self? Is the eye the seer, or am I the seer? ... Is consciousness the knower, or am I the knower? Does form receive retribution, or do I receive retribution? ... Does consciousness receive retribution, or do I? Does form reach other realms, or do I? ... And so too with consciousness. Does the cycle of birth and death have a beginning and an end, or is it beginningless and endless? Those who hear this sutra shall forever sever all such doubts.

There are also those who doubt: Do those who hold wrong views, violate the Four Pledges, commit the Five Heinous Crimes, or slander the Dao and its scriptures possess the Dharma-nature or not? Those who hear this sutra shall forever sever all such doubts.

There are also those who doubt: Does the world have boundaries or not? Does the ten-directional Dharma-realm exist or not? Those who hear this sutra shall also sever all such doubts. This is called severing the mind of doubt and delusion.

Furthermore, good sons, those with wisdom and upright minds free from perversity—if their minds harbor doubt, their vision shall not be correct. All sentient beings, if they do not hear this *Primordial Yang* supreme and wondrous scripture, shall perceive with perverse doubt, even the lowest immortals who awaken to the Dao shall still harbor perversity.

What is meant by the perverse views of all sentient beings? Seeing permanence, bliss, self, and purity within the defiled; seeing impermanence, suffering, impurity, and non-self in the Heavenly Worthy; seeing the lifespans of ordinary beings as long or short; seeing neither existence nor non-existence as the abode of the Primordial Yang’s palace; believing in the Eightfold Holy Dao as having existence or annihilation—such views are called perverse.

Good sons and good daughters, if they hear this Mahāyāna scripture and cultivate the holy Dao, they shall sever all such perversity. What is meant by all perversity? If one copies, recites, expounds it to others, and thoroughly understands its meaning, one shall attain uprightness, free from perverse views.

Good sons, those who cultivate this supreme *Primordial Yang* scripture, knowing its subtlety, shall from immeasurable kalpas past have cultivated it with sincere devotion, aspiring morning and night, and shall enter the supreme, correct, and true Dao.

Furthermore, good sons, those who understand the profound and esoteric meaning of this supreme *Primordial Yang* scripture and expound it to others, awakening sentient beings, shall enable all to know the Dao, eradicate the mind that slanders the Dharma, and exhaust all heinous transgressions—thereafter attaining the fruit of the supreme, correct, and true Dao. This is called the profound and secret meaning.

Furthermore, good sons, what is meant by the profound meaning? Though knowing that sentient beings truly have no self, they shall not lose the fruition of karma in the future. Though knowing that the six senses perish here, the karma of good and evil shall never perish. Though there are karmic roots, there is no doer. Though there are wondrous realms, there is no one who departs. Though there are attachments and fetters, there is no one bound.

Though there is the defilement of kalpas, it shall never perish—this is called the profound and secret meaning of the noble and exalted virtue of *Primordial Yang*.

At that time, the *Primordial Yang* Perfected One respectfully addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "As for the meaning of 'hearing what is not heard' just mentioned, this cannot be so. Why? If the Dao exists, it must exist definitively; if it does not exist, it must definitively not exist. The non-existent cannot give rise to the existent, nor can the existent be extinguished into the non-existent. As I have heard, what is heard is heard, and what is not heard is not heard—how then can one speak of 'hearing what is not heard'? If the Heavenly Worthy cannot be heard, this is not hearing; if one has already heard, then it is no longer hearing. Why? Because one has already heard the Dao. How then can one speak of 'hearing what has not been heard' or 'seeing what has not been seen'? It is like one who departs: upon arriving, they do not depart, and in departing, they do not arrive. It is also like being born: once born, one is no longer born. It is also like hearing: once heard, one no longer hears. If the Heavenly Worthy does not hear what is heard, then all sentient beings who have not yet awakened the mind of the Dao should possess it, those who have not attained liberation through *shijie* should attain it, and those who have not seen the *Dharma-nature* should see it. Why then do you say that though the Perfected One possesses the *Dharma-nature*, they have not yet attained clarity? If the Heavenly Worthy is not heard, from whom did the Perfected One of the past awaken and receive hearing? If you say they received hearing, why does the Perfected One now say before the Heavenly Worthy that they have not heard? If they have not heard, how has the Perfected One received the title of *Primordial Yang*? If this is so, would all sentient beings who do not hear the scriptures also receive the title of *Primordial Yang*? If the Perfected One, without hearing such scriptures, can see the supreme Dao, would all sentient beings who do not hear these scriptures also see the supreme, correct, and true Dao?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Form may be visible or invisible; sound is likewise—sometimes audible, sometimes inaudible. This great transformation is neither form nor sound—how then can one speak of seeing or hearing it?"

Thereupon, the *Primordial Yang* Perfected One suddenly awakened in astonishment, saying: "What has perished in the past cannot be heard; what has not yet arrived in the future also cannot be heard. At the moment of listening, it is not called hearing; once heard, the sound perishes and can no longer be heard. It is neither past, future, nor present. If it is not of the three times, it cannot be spoken of; if it cannot be spoken of, it cannot be heard. How then can one say that the Perfected One, cultivating this wondrous *Primordial Yang* scripture, hears what is not heard?"

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy rejoiced and praised the *Primordial Yang* Perfected One and the great assembly, saying: "Excellent! Excellent! You now deeply comprehend the wondrous principle and thoroughly penetrate the subtle and mysterious. All dharmas are like illusions, like transformations, like wind, like lightning, like bubbles, like foam, like the plantain tree—empty and without substance, neither life nor self, devoid of true form."

In that moment, a great radiance suddenly illuminated the entire realm, neither blue nor yellow, neither white nor black. When the great assembly encountered this light, their bodies and minds were filled with bliss, as if they had newly attained the fruit of the Dao.

Then the *Primordial Yang* Perfected One addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "From whence does this radiance arise?" The Heavenly Worthy remained silent and did not answer. The *Primordial Yang* Perfected One, trembling with awe, hesitated in unease, prostrated himself, and gazed upon the divine countenance, daring to inquire of the Heavenly Worthy: "By what cause and condition does this radiance illuminate the great assembly?" The Heavenly Worthy remained silent and did not answer.

At that time, the innumerable multitude of floating immortals in the void said to one another: "To whom does this radiance belong?" The Heavenly Worthy again remained silent. The *Minglü* Immortal and the assembly of *Dharani* masters again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "By what cause and condition does this brilliant light pervade the void without obstruction?" Thus, the great assembly questioned one another, yet none could comprehend.

Then the *Primordial Yang* Perfected One, with utmost sincerity and reverence, pressed his head to the ground, weeping and entreating with a trembling voice, humbling his heart and lowering his intent, gazing upon the Heavenly Worthy’s countenance and beseeching instruction to awaken future generations.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy smiled and addressed the *Primordial Yang* Perfected One, saying: "This radiance is called *wisdom*; wisdom is the true Dao. The Dharma of the true Dao does not arise from causes and conditions—how then can there be a question? By what cause and condition does this radiance arise? This radiance is called the wondrous Dharma of *Primordial Yang*; the wondrous Dharma of *Primordial Yang* is the true Dao. The Dharma of the true Dao does not arise from causes and conditions—why then do you, Immortal, question the cause and condition of this radiance? This radiance is the *primordial wisdom*; primordial wisdom is the Dharma of the true Dao. It does not arise from causes and conditions—why then do you, Daoist, question its cause and condition? This radiance is called *great compassion*; great compassion is the true Dao of *Primordial Yang*. The Dharma of the true Dao of *Primordial Yang* does not arise from causes and conditions—why then do you, Immortal, question its arising from causes and conditions? This radiance is the contemplation of the true and the mindfulness of the Dao; the contemplation of the true and the mindfulness of the Dao is the Dharma of the true Dao. It does not arise from causes and conditions—why then do you, Immortal, question its cause and condition? This radiance is the method by which all cultivators of the Dao swallow essence, imbibe qi, exhale and inhale, and practice ingestion—this is called the true Dao. The Dharma of the true Dao does not arise from causes and conditions—why then do you, Immortal, question its cause and condition? This radiance is the supreme lamp of the *Primordial Yang* Dharma."

The Heavenly Worthy said: "Perfected One, do not enter the coarse and defiled meaning of the dharmas. Now, in this eastern *Ganges* world called the *Immovable Realm*, the land is vast and level, without deserts or sands. The earth is adorned with the seven treasures, without ditches or pits. The trees are lush with flowers and fruits, ever-abundant. If sentient beings inhale their fragrance, their bodies and minds become pure, awakening to the *Great Vehicle*, like immortals attaining the fruit of the Dao."

There is also a great river whose waters are fragrant and sweet, possessing the eight flavors in full. If sentient beings bathe therein, they all become pure and clearly awaken to the Dao. The river abounds with manifold flowers and manifold fragrances; all sentient beings who inhale their scent attain clarity, awakening to the Dao with ease.

Moreover, there are countless tigers, wolves, lions, and all manner of fierce birds and beasts, yet when their gazes meet, they regard one another as tenderly as infants. In that world, no sentient being commits transgressions or betrayals, nor do they slander the Dao and Dharma or incur sins of evil and rebellion. The land is harmonious, free from pestilence, afflictions, greed, desire, jealousy, or envy. There is no sun or moon, no day or night, no seasons—it is as the era of *Dragon Han*. The people of that land are wise and upright, without arrogance or pride. All sentient beings awaken to the Dao, possessing great merit and virtue. Their minds all revere the true Dharma, cultivating the Great Vehicle, delighting in the Great Vehicle, contemplating the Great Vehicle, cherishing the Great Vehicle. Through the perfection of their practices, they attain the *Great Total Retention*, their hearts ever compassionate toward all sentient beings.

There is also the *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, deeply versed in the true teaching of *Primordial Yang*, the *Tamer and Teacher of Gods and Humans*. Wherever he goes, he proclaims the Dharma, and all sentient beings hear it without fail. For the assembly of the ten directions’ supreme and true great sages, he expounds such Great Vehicle sutras.

Good sons and their retinues, if they cultivate the *Wondrous Sutra of Primordial Yang of the Great Vehicle*, even what they have never heard before, they will come to hear the supreme essential Dao.

Twenty *Ganges*-sands of lands to the west lies a world called the *Great Hall Realm*, filled with mountains, hills, ridges, sands, and thorns, covering all. The people there constantly suffer hunger and thirst, enduring hardship in all four seasons, never knowing joy or peace. Through their ignorance, they fail to revere and seek the true Dao, clinging instead to unwholesome conditions. Within these unwholesome conditions, they practice perverse teachings, disbelieving in the true Dao. Their lifespans are short, and they constantly engage in deceit, governed by the king’s law. Though the king rules the land, he is never satisfied with what others possess, giving rise to greed and avarice. He raises armies to invade, causing many to die unjustly. As the king perpetuates such unwholesome acts, the gods and deities are displeased, sending down disasters of drought. The five grains fail to ripen, the people starve, and disease spreads. The land knows no peace.

The *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, the *Tamer and Teacher of Gods and Humans*, moved by compassion for sentient beings, traverses the worlds. In that land, he manifests a fragrant forest of the seven treasures, adorned with manifold splendor, manifold divine transformations, and manifold marvels. Together with the *Great Total Retention* sages and the *Peerless Immortals*, he expounds the *Wondrous Sutra of Primordial Yang of the Supreme Grade*, awakening sentient beings and enabling them to comprehend wisdom, so they may take refuge in the supreme, true, and perfect Dao.

Upon hearing this sutra, the people of that land are each astonished and doubtful, sighing in wonder: "By what cause and condition have we suddenly heard the subtle and wondrous scripture of a sage? From whence has it come? Now we rejoice, having encountered the true Dao."

Then the *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, together with seventy-four hundred *Perfected Immortals* of his retinue, bearing banners and canopies, flowers and incense, manifold music, and manifold adornments—all the implements of offering—arrived amidst the jeweled trees of the *Kan* grove in the *Land of Ultimate Bliss*. With the offerings they bore, they made offerings to the *Primordial Heavenly Worthy*, prostrating in reverence, circumambulating three times to the left. Having completed their homage, they withdrew to one side.

The Heavenly Worthy asked the *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, and all the good sons: "Have you come, or have you not come?"

The *Perfected One Radiant Wondrous Sound* addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "To come is not to come; not to come is also not to come. As I observe this principle, there is truly no coming at all."

The Heavenly Worthy said: "If all conditioned things are eternal, there is also no coming; if they are impermanent, there is also no coming. If one perceives the nature of sentient beings as real, then there is coming and not coming. But I do not see the fixed nature of sentient beings—how then can one speak of coming or not coming? Those who are arrogant perceive going and coming; those without arrogance perceive no going or coming. Those who grasp at actions perceive going and coming; those who do not grasp perceive no going or coming. If one sees the *Perfected One* as the ultimately supreme Dao, then there is going and coming; if one does not see the *Perfected One* as the ultimately supreme Dao, then there is no going or coming. Those who do not hear the nature of the Dao perceive going and coming; those who hear the nature of the Dao perceive no going or coming. If one sees the doubtful and inferior immortals, then there is going and coming; if one does not see the doubtful and inferior immortals, then there is no going or coming. If one sees the *Perfected One* as impermanent, blissful, self, and pure, then there is going and coming; if one sees the *Perfected One* as eternal, blissful, self, and pure, then there is no going or coming."

The Heavenly Worthy said: "Let us set this matter aside for now. If you have questions, I shall grant you leave to ask. May you receive my compassion and permission."

The Heavenly Worthy said: "Good son, ask as you will. Now is the proper time. I shall explain each point in order, resolving all your doubts one by one. Why is this so? The Dharma is difficult to perceive. Through a thousand kalpas of causes and conditions, one may encounter the sacred texts of the *Three Clarities* and the *Seven Divisions*—how rare is such a sight! You should diligently apply yourselves and listen with single-minded attention."

Then the *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, the *Perfected One of Primordial Yang*, and the others, having received permission and been admonished, addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "How is it that the *Perfected One* is able to cultivate the *Supreme Grade of Primordial Yang* and hear what they have never heard before?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Excellent, excellent! Good son, you now uphold the *Wondrous Sutra of Primordial Yang* and have also encountered me, who can expound it well. You have doubts—yet I am the *Great Physician King*, and I shall dissect and resolve your deep uncertainties. You have not yet fully understood the nature of the Dao, but I possess the lamp of the Dharma that can illuminate it for you."

"Now you wish to cross the great river of afflictions—I can be your boat and oars for you. Regard me as your father and mother, and I shall regard you with the heart of a loving parent. Your mind now clings to the treasure of the true Dharma. Listen carefully, listen carefully, and reflect well upon it. I shall unfold it for you step by step, leaving no doubts unresolved.

Perfected Ones, good sons, those who wish to hear the Dharma—now is the very time. If you hear the Dharma, you should cultivate reverence, recite it with utmost sincerity, and honor the true Dharma. In regard to the Dharma, do not seek its faults, nor entertain thoughts of greed, anger, or ignorance. Do not observe the Dharma-teacher and indulge in wicked conduct. Having heard the sutra, do not become arrogant or dismissive. Do not pursue fame, reputation, or material gain. Instead, regard it as the nectar-medicine of the Dharma for liberating the world. Do not give rise to aversion or attachment, nor harbor doubts.

After hearing the Dharma, first liberate yourself, then liberate others. First awaken yourself, then awaken others. First bring peace to yourself, then bring peace to others. Within the Dharma of the Dao, you should cultivate the thought of its constancy. Within the cycle of birth and death, you should cultivate the thought of its great suffering. Within the Dharma of the Dao, you should cultivate the thought of eternal bliss, true self, and purity. Strive for the Great Vehicle; do not cling to narrow views. In regard to all dharmas, you should abide in non-abiding and not fixate on the characteristics of any dharma. In all dharmas, do not give rise to thoughts of greed; instead, constantly cultivate the thought of knowing and perceiving the Dharma.

Good sons, you must diligently recite and study such scriptures, for then you will forever emerge from the苦海 of birth and death and ascend to the shore of compassion and goodness. You should follow these teachings and not give rise to doubts."

Then *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, the *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, bowed his head and respectfully asked the *Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Beginning*: "Regarding conditioned dharmas—if there is birth, is it permanent or impermanent? If birth is permanent, then conditioned dharmas would have no arising. If birth is impermanent, then conditioned dharmas would be permanent.

Heavenly Worthy, if birth arises from itself, then birth has no inherent nature. If it can give rise to others, then by what cause and condition does it not give rise to the unconditioned? Heavenly Worthy, if birth exists before it arises, then why is it called 'birth' now? If birth does not exist before it arises, then why not say that emptiness is birth?"

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the great assembly: "Excellent, excellent! Good son, you have profoundly penetrated the characteristics of dharmas and fully understood the source of the Dao. The unborn cannot be spoken of as birth, nor can birth be spoken of as birth, nor can the unborn be spoken of as unborn. Why is this? Because it is attained through cultivating the Dao.

Why can birth not be spoken of? Because birth does not exist. Why can the unborn not be spoken of? Because there is attainment. Why is there cause? Because there are causes and conditions. It can also be said that the ten causes and conditions serve as the cause of birth. For this reason, it can also be spoken of.

Good son, do not now enter the profound samādhi of emptiness. Why? Because the assembly is dull-witted. Good son, in conditioned dharmas, birth is also permanent, for abiding is impermanent; birth is also impermanent, for abiding is permanent. Because birth arises from birth, abiding is also impermanent. Because what originally did not exist now perishes, it is also impermanent.

Good son, by nature, all that arises is permanent, but because it perishes moment by moment, it cannot be called permanent. The true and correct Dao can extinguish it, hence it is called impermanent. Good son, in conditioned dharmas, before they arise, the nature of birth already exists, so birth can give rise to birth. In unconditioned dharmas, the nature of birth does not originally exist, so birth cannot give rise to birth.

It is like fire, which has an inherent nature and ignites when conditions meet. The eye has the nature to see, and through form, it becomes clear—thus it sees all sentient beings. Birth is also like this: because it has a nature, when conditions of karmic resonance meet, and parents unite, then birth occurs."

At that time, *Radiant Wondrous Sound*, the *Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding*, *Primordial Yang Perfected One*, and the assembly of seventy-four million, having heard this sutra, were filled with joy. With reverence and devotion, they bowed their heads, held jade tablets, and respectfully asked the *Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Beginning*: "Now that we have received your teachings and your clear exposition, the secret treasury of Primordial Yang has been revealed to us. We have heard what we had never heard before, and this assembly of seventy-four million has deeply understood the non-arising of all dharmas.

Heavenly Worthy, we have now resolved all our doubts. Among this assembly, there is a Perfected One named *True Radiant Light* who wishes to ask further questions. We humbly request your permission."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed *True Radiant Light*: "Good son, ask whatever you wish, and I shall explain and resolve it for you."

Then *True Radiant Light* and his retinue rose from their seats, adjusted their robes, knelt down, bowed their heads, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "What karmic deeds must the sentient beings of this world cultivate to be born in the *Immovable World*? How do the Perfected Ones of that land attain wisdom, become the most honored among humans, possess great virtue, perfect all practices, and swiftly comprehend upon hearing?"

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy spoke these verses:

All sentient beings
Contain the nature of the supreme Dao.
If they receive the wondrous sutra,
They will ascend to eternal bliss and purity.

Give generously and liberate beings,
Rescue the poor and the sick.
Cut off the mind of doubt,
And harmonize the mirror of consciousness.

Contemplate the *Sutra of Primordial Yang*,
Chant it day and night.
With ease, ascend the Nine Heavens,
And freely enter the Eightfold Right Path.

Good spirits will protect you,
Heavenly Perfected Ones will shine upon you.
Having escaped the Three Calamities,
You will also transcend the Nine Adversities.

Copy and uphold it,
And diligently practice.
Have compassion for good men and women,
Enabling them to fulfill their lifespans,
And through cyclic existence, become lofty Perfected Ones,
Meeting with sages through karmic conditions.

Today, attain the understanding of suffering and emptiness,
And forever cease all striving."

After the Heavenly Worthy spoke these verses, all in the assembly awakened fully, with no more doubts.

At that time, Perfected One Zhen Dingguang of Primordial Yang addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Now I have understood the karmic causes of my actions and have attained rebirth in that realm, the noble and exalted rank of Primordial Yang. I pity all sentient beings. As for the questions I have previously asked, the Heavenly Worthy has expounded this wondrous Dharma, which can bring benefit and peace to humans and gods."

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed Perfected One Primordial Yang, saying: "Excellent, excellent! Good man, you should now listen with utmost sincerity as I distinguish and explain each point in detail. There are causes and conditions for what has not yet come to be and does not come to be; there are causes and conditions for what does not come to be yet comes to be; and there are causes and conditions for what comes to be.

Good man, that which does not come to be yet comes to be is the noble and exalted rank of Primordial Yang. Ordinary beings do not attain it because they possess greed, hatred, and delusion; because their bodily, verbal, and mental actions are impure; because they accept all impure things; and because they commit the five grave offenses and slander the true and good Dharma. For these reasons, it is called what has not yet come to be and does not come to be.

Good man, that which does not come to be yet comes to be is free from greed, hatred, and delusion; free from evil in body, speech, and mind; does not accept all impure things; does not commit the four grave offenses; does not slander the supreme Dao; does not harbor perverse doubts; and does not commit the five grave offenses. For these causes and conditions, it is called what comes to be yet does not come to be.

Good man, for what causes and conditions is it called what comes to be yet does not come to be? That which comes to be is called the twenty-five states of existence. All sentient beings are constantly obscured by countless afflictions and fetters, ceaselessly transmigrating like a turning wheel—this is called coming to be. To save and deliver all sentient beings, one manifests in the present—this is also called coming to be.

Good man, for what causes and conditions is it called what comes to be and comes to be? That which comes to be is the twenty-five states of existence. Because of the causes and conditions of afflictions in all ordinary beings, it is called what comes to be and comes to be.

Good man, it is the same with what has not been heard. There is what has not been heard yet is heard; there is what has not been heard; and there is what has been heard and is heard. What is what has not been heard yet is heard? Good man, what has not been heard is the rank of Primordial Yang. Why has it not been heard? Because it is not conditioned, not of sound, and inexpressible. How then is it also heard? Because it is named as such—what is called *constant bliss, true self, and purity*. For this reason, it is called what has not been heard yet is heard."

At that time, Perfected One Primordial Yang and all in the assembly bowed their heads, knelt, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "As the Heavenly Worthy has said, the noble and secret meaning of Primordial Yang cannot be heard. How then can it be said that *constant bliss, true self, and purity* can be heard? Why is this?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "One who severs afflictions is called the noble rank of Primordial Yang. One who has not severed them is called one who does not attain it. For this reason, the noble rank of Primordial Yang is originally non-existent yet now exists. If worldly dharmas are originally non-existent yet now exist, they are called impermanent. For example, you all were originally non-existent, now exist, and will again become non-existent—thus they are called impermanent. If the noble rank of Primordial Yang is like this, how can it be said to be *constant bliss, true self, and purity*?

Furthermore, Heavenly Worthy, all that is accomplished through adornment is called impermanent. If the noble rank of Primordial Yang is like this, it should also be impermanent. What are the causes and conditions? The thirty-six revered scriptures, the Three Pure Ones’ secret treasury, the seven books of true teachings—all such Dharmas are the causes and conditions for accomplishing everything, and thus are called impermanent.

Furthermore, Heavenly Worthy, that which is named is impermanent. If the noble rank of Primordial Yang exists, it should also be impermanent. As the Heavenly Worthy once said before the Primordial Beginning, all wondrous scriptures undergo transformation. For this reason, they are called impermanent.

Furthermore, Heavenly Worthy, what is visible is called impermanent. As previously stated, the noble rank of Primordial Yang severs all afflictions.

Furthermore, Heavenly Worthy, for example, space is unhindered for all sentient beings and is thus called constant. If the noble rank of Primordial Yang is constant, why do some sentient beings attain it and others not? If the noble rank of Primordial Yang is unequal among sentient beings, it cannot be called constant.

Heavenly Worthy, for example, if a hundred people share a common enemy and that enemy is harmed, many will receive joy. If the noble rank of Primordial Yang is an equal Dharma, when one attains it, many should attain it; when one severs fetters, many should also sever them. If it is not like this, how can it be called constant?

For example, if someone reveres the Three Treasures, makes offerings to scriptures, respects and praises them, and does so diligently day and night, kings, princes, parents, and teachers will receive benefit and nourishment—this is not called constant. The noble rank of Primordial Yang is also like this and is not called constant. Why? As the Heavenly Worthy once said during the Primordial Beginning’s dispensation, expounding this scripture to Perfected One Primordial Yang: 'If someone can reverently recite this scripture, they will sever fetters and receive boundless joy.' For this reason, it is not called constant.

Heavenly Worthy, if within Primordial Yang there is what is called *constant bliss, true self, and purity*, it is not called constant. If it does not exist, how can it be spoken of?"

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed Perfected One Da Jie, saying: "The essence of Primordial Yang is not originally non-existent yet now exists. If the essence of Primordial Yang were originally non-existent yet now exists, it would not be the unconditioned, eternally abiding Dharma. Whether there is the Dao or not, its nature and characteristics are eternally abiding. Because sentient beings are obscured by afflictions and do not study the true Dao, they mistakenly believe Primordial Yang does not exist. When a perfected one diligently cultivates the mind with precepts, concentration, and wisdom, and severs afflictions, they then perceive it. You should know that the true Dao is the eternally abiding Dharma, not originally non-existent yet now exists—thus it is constant.

Good man, for example, in a dark room filled with various treasures, people know they exist but cannot see them because of the darkness."

Those of wisdom, knowing skillful means, kindle the great bright lamp and carry it to illuminate all, thereby perceiving the treasures—yet never do they conceive the thought that these treasures were originally non-existent and now exist. The true Dao is likewise: it has always existed, not beginning only now. Because of the darkness of afflictions, sentient beings do not see it. The greatly wise true person, employing skillful means, kindles the lamp of wisdom, enabling all to perceive the true Dao—constant, blissful, self, and pure. Therefore, the wise should not declare of this true Dao that it was originally non-existent and now exists.

Thus, great assembly, your claim that the true Dao becomes impermanent due to adornment is also incorrect. Why? Great assembly, the essence of the true Dao is neither born nor produced, neither substantial nor empty, neither generated by karmic action nor a conditioned, defiled dharma. It is neither heard nor seen, neither subject to birth-and-death nor possessing distinct or identical characteristics. It neither goes nor returns, neither cause nor effect. For these reasons, the true Dao is constant, eternally unchanging. Therefore, through cultivating wholesome dharmas over countless kalpas to adorn oneself, one comes to perceive it clearly.

Great assembly, for example, the earth contains waters of eight flavors, yet all sentient beings cannot obtain them. Those of wisdom apply effort to dig and drill, and thus obtain the water. The true Dao is likewise. Just as a blind person does not behold the sun and moon, yet a skilled physician restores their sight so they may see—so too the sun and moon are not newly existent. The true Dao is likewise: it has existed from of old, not only now.

Good man, it is like a person imprisoned for crimes, who after long confinement is released and returns home to see their six relations. The true Dao is likewise.

Thus, great assembly, your claim that the dharma of the true Dao is impermanent due to causes and conditions is also incorrect. Why? Good man, there are five kinds of causes. What are the five? First, the cause of arising; second, the cause of harmony; third, the cause of abiding; fourth, the cause of growth; and fifth, the distant cause.

What is the cause of arising? The cause of arising consists of various afflictions, various doubts, and the seeds of grasses and trees—this is called the cause of arising.

What is the cause of harmony? When wholesome minds harmonize with wholesomeness, unwholesome minds with unwholesomeness, and indeterminate minds with indeterminacy—this is called the cause of harmony.

What is the cause of abiding? Just as a house does not collapse when its foundation abides below, and mountains, rivers, and trees stand firm due to the great earth—so too the four great elements and boundless afflictions enable sentient beings to abide. This is called the cause of abiding.

What is the cause of growth? Through conditions such as clothing, ornaments, food, and other necessities, sentient beings grow. Just as seeds unburned by fire and uneaten by birds grow; as male and female disciples of the four assemblies, relying on true persons and those who nurture their abilities, grow; as children grow through their parents—this is called the cause of growth.

What is the distant cause? For example, when the Heavenly Venerable expounded this sutra in past kalpas, it became a great causal condition for future beings, washing away all doubts and obstructions—this is called the distant cause. Or, as the blood and qi of parents are a distant cause for sentient beings; or as seasons and the like are called distant causes.

Good man, the essence of the true Dao is not constituted by these five causes. How then can one claim it is an impermanent cause?

Furthermore, good man, there are two other causes: the cause of production and the cause of realization.

What is the cause of production? As the potter’s wheel and cord are the cause of production. What is the cause of realization? As a lamp illuminating objects in the dark is called the cause of realization.

Good man, the *Sublime Primordial Yang Scripture* does not arise from the cause of production but only from the cause of realization. The cause of realization is the clarification of the profound and subtle meanings of the supreme Primordial Yang, serving as a great vessel, a great bridge, a great causal condition, and a great field of merit for future beings, enabling all in this age to attain the fruit of the supreme, correct, and true Dao.

Then, the Radiant Voice of Primordial Yang, Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding, bowed his luminous head and respectfully addressed the Primordial Heavenly Venerable: "Having received your instruction, you have guided sentient beings with various skillful means, expounded in manifold ways, taught with meticulous care, and praised in exhaustive detail—my joy surpasses all measure. Yet, due to long-standing obstructions, doubts remain. Disdaining not my lowliness, I venture to touch your sacred countenance. Bowing my head, I humbly inquire further:

Heavenly Venerable, may I ask: what meritorious deeds must all sentient beings cultivate to escape sorrow and grief? What almsgiving brings wealth and abundance? What field of merit yields plenitude?"

What vows must one make to attain the true Dao?"

The Heavenly Venerable replied: "It is like a man planting a tree to gain shade, flowers, fruit, or timber. If one cultivates the Way with single-minded devotion, silently contemplating and profoundly reflecting, one naturally accumulates vast merit. By bestowing alms upon the destitute and impoverished, cherishing all beings with compassion, and loving all things without begrudging treasures, one’s endeavors align with the Dharma. Practicing thus, one deeply comprehends the wondrous Dharma, fulfills the true Dao, and severs the karmic obstructions of all beings.

Good man, it is like one who falls into the great ocean and clings to a corpse to cross to the other shore. When a perfected one cultivates the supreme Dao and practices almsgiving, it is likewise as that corpse.

Good man, it is like one imprisoned in a deep dungeon with doors and gates firmly secured, where only the privy hole offers passage to an unobstructed place. When a perfected one cultivates the supreme Dao and practices almsgiving, it is likewise so.
