Good man, it is like a noble in dire peril, with no refuge, who vows to recite the *Primordial Yang Sutra* and thereby attains peace and safety. When a perfected one cultivates the supreme Dao and practices almsgiving, it is likewise so.

Good man and all present assemblies, you should know that the secret treasury of Primordial Yang is none other than the supreme, correct, and true Dao. If one follows the sutra in cultivation, vowing and contemplating morning and evening, setting aside a pure chamber of one *zhang* square within the household to burn incense and make offerings, persisting year after year without retreat—through such sincerity, all shall naturally attain its fruit, and in this life be freed from sorrow, peril, and the afflictions of vexation."

Then, the Radiant Voice of Primordial Yang, Perfected One of Penetrating Understanding, along with the great assembly of divine immortals and their retinues—seventy-four million in all—simultaneously exclaimed in praise and recited these verses:

The true Dao’s essence is numinous and wondrous,
The supreme Dharma most profound and mysterious.
Its secret traces lie in the Purple Tenuity Palace,
Its radiant light illumines the Great Luo Heaven.
Scholars of the Dark Capital’s highest learning,
Ever pure and naturally so,
Guide the crane to roam the azure vastness,
Urge the phoenix to soar through blue mist.
At the Golden Portals, they worship the Great Sage,
At the Jade Gates, they gather the lofty and wise.
The four assemblies of Primordial Yang’s time
Encounter this great karmic condition.
The Three Clarities have unveiled their mysteries,
The Seven Divisions have been transmitted in turn.
Obstructions of doubt are dispelled and explored,
Past sorrows and vexations now understood.
All good men
Attain the field of pure body,
Roam the Four Correct Ways,
Wander freely atop the Nine Floral Peaks.
Flute notes rise beyond the clouds,
Brahma’s voice traverses the wind’s forefront.
By chance, they meet the era of the Primordial Beginning,
Unfading as the age of the Supreme Sovereign.
The Tamer, Teacher of Heaven and Humankind,
Severs the bonds of love and attachment,
Diminishes and cuts away the nets of doubt,
Anger and delusion are thus cast aside.
The four assemblies bow their heads in joy,
Taking leave of the great divine immortals.
Today, we receive your guidance and deliverance,
And pray you bestow your great compassion to the end.

Then, the Radiant Voice of Primordial Yang, Perfected One, and all present assemblies concluded their hymns of praise, bowed in reverence, and departed.

Here ends Scroll Nine of the *Supreme Pervasive Treasure Primordial Yang Wondrous Sutra*.
Scroll Ten of the *Supreme Pervasive Treasure Primordial Yang Wondrous Sutra* begins.

**The Ascent to Great Luo Chapter**

Thus have I heard. At one time, the Heavenly Worthy was in the land of Pulín, beneath the Fan Hua Tree, within the Palace of Primordial Yang, surrounded by a multitude of a million—great sagely perfected ones, great immortal Daoists, and male and female officials—all encircling him before and behind.

At that time, on the seventh day of the seventh month, the Heavenly Worthy ascended to the Upper Palace of Great Luo. Entering samādhi, he beheld his majestic divine power, emitting a great radiance of variegated hues—azure, yellow, red, and white—pervading the three thousand great thousand worlds and extending to the very edges of the ten directions’ empty space, all likewise illuminated. Of the six destinies’ sentient beings within, those who encountered this light found all the defilements of the four afflictions utterly dissolved.

Upon seeing and hearing this, those multitudes were overcome with great sorrow. With one voice, they raised their lamentations, saying to one another: *"Let each of us restrain ourselves; let us not be overwhelmed with grief. Rather, let us swiftly go together to the Palace of Primordial Yang."* Arriving before the Heavenly Worthy, they prostrated, their heads touching the ground, and entreated him, bowing and beseeching: *"May the Heavenly Worthy not ascend to Great Luo. Abide here in Primordial Yang for a hundred years, or a thousand ages!"* Clasping one another’s hands, they spoke again: *"The world is hollow and empty; the good fortune of beings is exhausted. Unwholesome karmic deeds increase. We must hasten now, for the Heavenly Worthy will soon depart."* And again they said: *"The world is but empty space. From this day forth, we shall have no refuge, no object of reverence—poor, orphaned, and exposed. Once the Supreme Heavenly Worthy departs, if doubts arise, to whom shall we turn?"*

Then, there were immeasurable great sages, hosts of perfected ones, great immortal Daoists, male and female officials, and all the pure-minded laymen and laywomen who had encountered the Heavenly Worthy’s light. Their bodies trembled violently, unable to contain themselves. Their minds grew dim and confused, disoriented and restless.

At that time, there were also the Perfected Ones Song Ling, Guang Miao, and Yu Luo, along with hundreds of thousands of others whose minds had attained mastery, whose tasks were accomplished, who had left behind all afflictions and subdued their faculties. Like great dragon kings of immense virtue, they had realized the wisdom of emptiness, attained their own benefit, and were surrounded by sandalwood as a sandalwood grove, or as a lion king encircled by lions. They had accomplished such boundless merits, all through the Heavenly Worthy.

Each disciple, at the first light of dawn, left their usual abode, holding incense burners. When they encountered the Heavenly Worthy’s radiance, they said to one another: *"We should swiftly purify ourselves."* Having spoken thus, their entire bodies bristled with hair, unable to contain themselves. Tears filled their eyes, and they were overcome with great sorrow. For the sake of benefiting and bringing peace to beings, accomplishing the foremost emptiness-practice of the Great Vehicle, manifesting the great Dao, and expounding the esoteric teachings through skillful means—to ensure the uninterrupted proclamation of the Dharma in all its forms, and to subdue the causes and conditions of beings—they swiftly came before the Heavenly Worthy. Bowing at his feet, they circumambulated him a hundred times, prostrated in reverence, and withdrew to sit to one side.

At that time, there were also Daoists, male and female officials, male and female functionaries of the twenty-four offices, leading their retinues of hundreds of thousands. Their outflows exhausted, their minds attained mastery, their tasks accomplished, they had left behind all afflictions and subdued their faculties. Like great dragon kings of immense virtue, they had realized the wisdom of emptiness. At the first light of dawn, their entire bodies bristled with hair, tears filled their eyes, and they were overcome with great sorrow. Likewise, for the sake of benefiting and bringing peace to beings, accomplishing the foremost emptiness-practice of the Great Vehicle, manifesting the great Dao, and expounding the esoteric teachings through skillful means—to ensure the uninterrupted proclamation of the Dharma in all its forms, and to subdue the causes and conditions of beings—they swiftly came before the Heavenly Worthy. Bowing at his feet, they circumambulated him hundreds of thousands of times, prostrated in reverence, and withdrew to sit to one side.

Among the dragons of humanity, those who had attained the ten stages and abided in immovability, manifesting themselves through skillful means, were named the Perfected Ones Great King, Na Shan, Jue Li, Most Victorious, Wondrous Thought, and Great Wisdom, who served as their leaders. Their minds all revered the Great Vehicle, abided in the Great Vehicle, deeply understood the Great Vehicle, delighted in the Great Vehicle, and guarded the Great Vehicle. They were skillful in accord with all the world. They made this vow: *"Those who have not yet crossed over, we shall cause to cross over."* In countless eons past, they had upheld pure precepts, maintained their practices, and explained what was unexplained. They perpetuated the lineage of the Three Treasures, ensuring its continuity into the future. They would turn the Wheel of the Dharma, adorning themselves with great splendor, accomplishing boundless merits such as these. They regarded all beings as they would an only child. At the first light of dawn, when they encountered the Heavenly Worthy’s radiance, their entire bodies bristled with hair, tears filled their eyes, and they were overcome with great sorrow. Likewise, for the sake of benefiting and bringing peace to beings, accomplishing the foremost emptiness-practice of the Great Vehicle, manifesting the great Dao, and expounding the esoteric teachings through skillful means—to ensure the uninterrupted proclamation of the Dharma in all its forms, and to subdue the causes and conditions of beings—they swiftly came before the Heavenly Worthy. Bowing at his feet, they circumambulated him hundreds of thousands of times, prostrated in reverence, and withdrew to sit to one side.

At that time, there were also immeasurable pure-minded laymen and laywomen who upheld the Five Precepts with perfect decorum. Their leaders were named Wei De, Gan Ji, Yuan You, Dong Shuang Cheng, Xu Fei Qiong, and Wan Ling Hua. They took deep delight in examining the gates of counteractive practices—such as suffering and joy, permanence and impermanence, self and no-self, reality and unreality, refuge and non-refuge, beings and non-beings, eternity and non-eternity, peace and non-peace, action and non-action, severance and non-severance, constancy and inconstancy—and suchlike gates of counteractive practices. They also delighted in hearing the supreme Great Vehicle. Having heard it, they were able to expound it to others. They upheld pure precepts, yearned for the Great Vehicle, and having fulfilled themselves, they also fulfilled others who yearned likewise.

Skilled in gathering the supreme wisdom, they cherished and delighted in the Great Vehicle, guarding and upholding it. They were well able to accord with all in the world, liberating those not yet liberated, enlightening those not yet enlightened, and perpetuating the lineage of the Three Jewels to ensure its continuity in future ages. They would turn the Wheel of the Dao, adorning themselves with great majesty, their minds ever steeped in the savor of pure precept-observance, and thus accomplished all such merits. Toward all beings, they generated a great compassionate heart, equal and undivided, as if regarding an only child.

At the break of dawn, when the first rays of the sun emerged, desiring to adorn the teachings of the Dao, each person gathered ten thousand bundles of fragrant woods—sandalwood, aloeswood, ox-head sandalwood, celestial wood, and the like. Each piece of wood, with its grain and knots, radiated the subtle luminosity of the seven treasures, resembling intricate multicolored paintings. By the power of the Dao, these woods bore wondrous hues of blue, yellow, red, and white, delighting the eyes of all beings. The woods were anointed with various fragrances—turmeric, aloeswood, resin incense—and adorned with jeweled lotus blossoms. From each fragrant wood hung five-colored banners, soft and exquisite, like celestial silks embroidered with brocade and damask. These fragrant woods were loaded onto jeweled chariots, each chariot emanating multicolored light—blue, yellow, red, and white—with shafts and wheels inlaid with the seven treasures. Each chariot was drawn by a team of four horses, swift as the wind, and before each chariot stood fifty-seven jeweled standards, their golden nets of real gold draped overhead. Each chariot bore fifty exquisite jeweled canopies, and atop them rested various flowers—blue lotuses, white lotuses, red lotuses, golden lotuses, and dark-blue lotuses—each blossom with petals of pure gold and a vajra pedestal. Within the hearts of these flowers gathered many black bees, frolicking and rejoicing, emitting wondrous sounds: the truths of impermanence, suffering, emptiness, and no-self. From these sounds arose the path originally trodden by the true ones. There were also various songs, dances, and musical performances—zithers, flutes, harps, pipes, drums, and horns. From the music emerged these words: *"Alas! Alas! The world is but emptiness!"*

Before each chariot, a virtuous man bore a four-jeweled tray laden with various flowers, turmeric and other incenses, and the finest perfumes. Devout men and women, young and old alike, each set their minds to preparing food for the Heavenly Worthy and his disciples, complete in every variety, all cooked with sandalwood, aloeswood, fragrant fuel, and eight-flavored water, sweet and delectable. There were six flavors: bitter, sour, sweet, pungent, salty, and bland. And three virtues: lightness and softness, purity and cleanliness, and accordance with the Dao. Having made such adornments, they arrived at the Palace of Primordial Yang, where the ground was entirely spread with gold, and silken fabrics, jeweled canopies, and coverings were laid upon it. Throughout the palace, for the Heavenly Worthy and his disciples, they arranged seven-jeweled lion thrones, as lofty and vast as Mount Jade Capital. Upon each throne hung jeweled curtains and garlands, with various exquisite banners and canopies suspended, the thrones anointed with fine fragrances and scattered with myriad blossoms.

The devout men and women each thought: *"May all beings receive whatever they need—food, clothing, heads, eyes, limbs, and bodies."* As they made these offerings, they were free from desire, anger, defilement, and poisonous thoughts, harboring no residual wishes for worldly blessings or happiness, but aspiring solely to the supreme, pure precepts of the Dao. These devout men and women, abiding in the path of the true ones, further thought: *"Once the Heavenly Worthy has accepted our offerings, he will ascend to the Great Luo Upper Realm, leaving us behind."* At this thought, their body hairs stood on end, tears filled their eyes, and great sorrow arose within them. Each bore their offerings—fragrant woods, banners, jeweled canopies, and food—loaded onto jeweled chariots, and proceeded to the Heavenly Worthy’s presence. Bowing at his feet, they presented their offerings, circumambulating him a hundred times, raising their voices in lamentation, their sorrow shaking heaven and earth, tears falling like rain. They said to one another: *"Alas, O Benevolent One! The world is but emptiness!"* Then, casting themselves before the Heavenly Worthy, they addressed him: *"We beseech the Heavenly Worthy, with great compassion and great mercy, to accept our offerings, receive our repentance, and eradicate our past transgressions. From beginningless kalpas through hundreds of thousands of eons to this very day, we have passed through countless births and deaths, bound by the fetters of the six desires and the five aggregates, ensnared by greed, stinginess, and attachment, knowing only how to commit sins and unaware of the Great Vehicle. Now, by the power of the Heavenly Worthy’s Great Vehicle and its luminous karma, we each reproach ourselves. We observe our own bodies as if they were four poisonous snakes. This body is constantly devoured by countless worms. This body is foul and filthy, imprisoned by the dungeon of desire. This body is loathsome, like a dead dog. This body is impure, its nine orifices ever flowing. This body is like a city, its walls of skin enclosing blood, flesh, sinews, and bones, its hands and feet like battlements and watchtowers, its eyes like spy-holes, its head like a palace hall, its heart the ruling king within. Such a bodily city is abandoned by all true immortals, yet foolish and deluded beings cling to it, dwelling within it with greed, lust, anger, and ignorance—rakshasas all. It is as unsubstantial as reeds, e lan trees, water bubbles, or plantain trunks. This body is impermanent, ceasing in every instant, like lightning, a mirage, a phantom flame, or painted water that vanishes as soon as it is drawn."*

This body is fragile, like a tree perched on a sheer riverbank. Before long, this body shall become food for foxes, wolves, owls, vultures, crows, and starving dogs. Only the wise may delight in such a body—yet even to speak of it fully would be as futile as trying to hold the ocean in a cow’s hoofprint.

This body is impermanent, impure, and foul; even if the vast earth were reduced to the size of a jujube, then gradually diminished to the size of a *tingli* seed, or even to a speck of dust, its flaws could still not be fully described. This body is rife with afflictions; thus, it should be abandoned like spittle cast aside.

For these reasons, all men and women should constantly cultivate their minds with the Dharma of emptiness, signlessness, and wishlessness. They should seek joy in studying and receiving the Mahāyāna sutras, and having heard them, expound them to others. They must uphold their original vows, revile this body, and deeply loathe its impermanence and instability. By constantly cultivating such right contemplation, they will shatter the boundless wheel of birth and death. Thirsting for the Mahāyāna, they will first fulfill themselves and then fulfill others who likewise thirst. They will take profound delight in the Mahāyāna, safeguard the Mahāyāna, and though they appear in this body, they are in truth of the same kind as the true immortals.

They will skillfully follow the ways of the world, liberating those not yet liberated, enlightening those not yet enlightened, and perpetuating the lineage of the Three Jewels to ensure it does not vanish in future ages. They will turn the Wheel of Dharma, adorning themselves with great majesty, steadfastly upholding the precepts, and accomplishing all such merits. Toward all beings, they will generate great compassion, equal and undivided, as if regarding an only child.

They will all make this vow: *"We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to accept our offerings and allow our repentance, to abide long in the lower realms, to liberate beings, to bestow the scriptures of deliverance, to grant the blessings of the Dharma, and not to forsake us for the upper realms. For just as parents, before their children are fully reared, would never suddenly depart—leaving their offspring orphaned, destitute, and bereft of shelter—so too, if the Heavenly Worthy returns to the upper realms and abandons us, it would be the same. We implore the Heavenly Worthy to remain in the world, to perfect all Dharma, and to shelter us."*

With such entreaties, they choked with sobs, overcome by grief. The great assembly wept, tears filling their eyes, unable to restrain themselves. Then the Heavenly Worthy emitted from his face manifold rays of light, which illumined the assembly. Upon witnessing this radiance, they understood its significance and relayed the news to one another: *"The Heavenly Worthy now manifests these auspicious signs; soon he will surely return to the upper realms. All offerings should be presented to the Heavenly Worthy and the great assembly."*

The Pine Spirit Immortal and the assembly, knowing that the Heavenly Worthy’s emission of such light was not without cause, remained silent for a long while. The Heavenly Worthy then addressed the Pine Spirit Immortal: *"The time is now right for you to make offerings to the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly. I am about to return to the upper realms."* A second and third time, he spoke likewise.

Upon hearing these words, the Pine Spirit Immortal and the great assembly raised their voices in wailing, choking with sorrow, and cried: *"Alas! Alas! The world is as empty as the void!"* They addressed the assembly: *"Now, let us all prostrate ourselves together, five limbs to the ground, and with one voice entreat the Heavenly Worthy to remain in the lower realms, to shelter us, and not to abandon us for the upper realms."*

Then the Heavenly Worthy said to the Pine Spirit and the others: *"Do not weep so bitterly and disturb yourselves. Each of you should contemplate this body as being like a plantain tree, a mirage in the heat, a water bubble, an illusion, a *gandharva* city, a fragile vessel, lightning, painted water, a prisoner facing execution, ripe fruit, camel flesh, or a pestle rising and falling in a mortar. Contemplate all conditioned things as akin to food mixed with poison, for the Dharma of conditioned existence is fraught with manifold afflictions."*

Thereupon, the Pine Spirit Immortal again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: *"If you do not remain long in the lower realms, how can we not weep? Alas! Alas! The world is as empty as the void! We only beseech the Heavenly Worthy to take pity on us and all beings, to abide long in the lower realms, and not to return to the upper realms."*

The Heavenly Worthy replied to the Pine Spirit Immortal: *"You should not lament so piteously, urging me to remain long in the lower realms. It is out of pity for you and all beings that I now intend to return to the upper realms. Why? Because such is the nature of all noble Dharma, and so too is it with conditioned existence."* Then the Heavenly Worthy spoke these verses:

*"All conditioned things
are by nature impermanent.
Once arisen, they do not abide;
extinction alone is bliss."*

*"Pine Spirit Immortal, you should now contemplate all conditioned things as ever-new, all dharmas as devoid of self, impermanent and unabiding. This body is rife with boundless afflictions, like a water bubble. Therefore, you should not weep."*

Then the Pine Spirit again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: *"So it is, so it is! Truly, as you teach. Though we know the Heavenly Worthy manifests skillful means in returning to the upper realms and leaving us, we cannot help but feel sorrow. Yet upon reflection, we also rejoice."*

The Heavenly Worthy praised the Pine Spirit: *"Excellent! Excellent! You understand that the Heavenly Worthy’s coming and going, like all dharmas, are but illusory appearances. The Great Sage abides within them, employing skillful means without attachment. Why? Because all teachings are adapted to the needs of beings, aiming to liberate them from the sufferings of birth, old age, sickness, and death, so that all may attain the unshakable fruit of rebirth and constantly enjoy bliss. Why? Because I am the true field of merit for all beings. If you also wish to be a field of merit for all beings, swiftly prepare your offerings and do not delay."*

Then the Pine Spirit, for the sake of liberating all beings, bowed his head, tears streaming, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy: *"Excellent! Excellent! If I am capable of being a field of merit, then I will fully understand whether the Heavenly Worthy truly returns to the upper realms or not."*

Now we and all the perfected ones and immortals are like mosquitoes and gnats—truly unable to fathom whether the Heavenly Worthy returns to the upper realms or not.

Then the Perfected Pine Spirit and his followers, sorrowful and weeping, circled the Heavenly Worthy, burning incense and scattering flowers, serving him with utmost devotion. Soon after, they rose from their seats with the assembly of perfected ones and departed to prepare food offerings.

After the Pine Spirit left, the divine continent of Jambudvīpa, both within and beyond the Three Realms, trembled violently. All beings who saw or heard this knew that the Heavenly Worthy was returning to the upper realms, and thus the earth quaked greatly.

At that time, all beings within and beyond the Three Realms, upon hearing these words, stood with hair on end, weeping in unison as they recited this verse:

We bow to the Master of Discipline,
We now beseech and implore:
Parting from humans and immortals,
We shall forever lack refuge.
If you now return to the upper realms,
We shall sink into the sea of suffering.
Grieving and longing, filled with sorrow,
Like a calf bereft of its mother,
Poor and without salvation.
Like one afflicted by illness,
Without a physician, left to their own devices,
Consuming what they should not.
The afflictions of beings are sicknesses,
Constantly harmed by wrong views,
Far from the King of Dharma Physicians,
They ingest poisonous medicines.
Therefore, Great Sage,
You should not abandon us.
As a land without a ruler
Suffers famine among its people,
So too are we—
Deprived of shelter and the flavor of the Dao.
If you return to the upper realms,
Our minds will be lost in confusion,
Like the great earth trembling,
Disoriented in all directions.
Great Immortal ascending to the upper realm,
How can we not grieve today?
Abandoned by the Heavenly Worthy,
Like spittle cast aside.
For example, when the sun first rises,
Its radiance blazes brightly,
Not only illuminating itself
But also dispelling all darkness.
The Heavenly Worthy’s divine light of spiritual power
Can eradicate our suffering and sorrow.
Abiding among the great assembly,
Like Mount Jade Capital.
The Heavenly Worthy said: It is like a king who raises his children with constant love, teaching them benevolence, righteousness, loyalty, and filial piety, ensuring they fully understand. Only then does he allow them freedom, yet unexpectedly, the children turn to unwholesome ways, and the king abandons them.

The Heavenly Worthy addressed the Pine Spirit: Now, for the sake of the Dao, I have instructed you all, ensuring you possess right view. Do not abandon this path. If you do, you will be like those princes.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like one who has mastered many treatises yet still feels fear toward them.

The Heavenly Worthy is likewise—though he has penetrated all dharmas, he still feels fear toward them. If the Heavenly Worthy were to remain in the world for a long time, expounding the flavor of ambrosia to fulfill all, then beings would no longer fear falling into hell.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like one who, newly employed, is seized by officials and imprisoned. When asked, “What have you endured?” they reply, “I now suffer great sorrow. If I escape, I will find peace.”

The Heavenly Worthy is the same—he has undertaken many ascetic practices for our sake. Yet we have not yet escaped the suffering of birth and death. How then can the Heavenly Worthy enjoy peace?

Heavenly Worthy, it is like a master physician skilled in remedies who secretly teaches his own son but not other external students.

The Heavenly Worthy is the same—he has privately taught the profound and secret treasury only to Laozi, abandoning the rest of us without compassion.

The Heavenly Worthy should not be stingy with the Dao, like that physician who taught only his son and not the other students. That physician’s reluctance to teach stemmed from a mind clinging to superiority and inferiority, hence his secrecy. But the Heavenly Worthy’s mind is free from such distinctions—why then does he not instruct us?

We only wish you would remain long in this world and not ascend to the upper realms.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like the old, the young, and the sick who, forsaking distant and safe paths, traverse perilous roads. The perilous road is fraught with hardships, and they endure countless sufferings. Then a compassionate person takes pity and shows them a smooth, good path.

Heavenly Worthy, we are the same.
The “young” are those whose Dharma-body has not yet grown;
The “old” are those burdened by heavy afflictions;
The “sick” are those not yet freed from birth and death;
The “perilous road” is the twenty-five states of existence.
We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to guide us onto the ambrosial right path, to remain long in this world, and not to depart for the upper realms.

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed the assembly: You should not, like ordinary beings or the gods, grieve and weep. Instead, strive diligently and focus your minds on right mindfulness.

Upon hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s words, the gods and the great assembly ceased their weeping, like one who, having buried a beloved child, restrains their tears.

Then the Heavenly Worthy spoke this verse to the great assembly:

Open your minds,
Do not grieve so deeply.
The great Dao is always thus—
Therefore, remain silent.
Delight in the practice of non-negligence,
Guard your minds with right mindfulness,
Stay far from unwholesome dharmas,
Console yourselves and rejoice.

Furthermore, if the Pine Spirit and others have any doubts, they should now ask. Whether it concerns emptiness or non-emptiness, permanence or impermanence, suffering or non-suffering, dependence or non-dependence, departure or non-departure, return or non-return, constancy or inconstancy, cessation or non-cessation, beings or non-beings, existence or non-existence, reality or unreality, truth or untruth, extinction or non-extinction, secrecy or non-secrecy, duality or non-duality—if there are any doubts regarding such matters, ask now. I will, in accordance with your needs, resolve them for you. I will first expound the ambrosia of the Dao, and only then will I return to the upper realms.

All you great assemblies, the Heavenly Worthy has appeared in the world, praising the rarity of obtaining a human body. Encountering the Dao and generating faith—this too is rare.

To endure—this too is difficult. To perfect the precepts, fulfill them without flaw, and attain the supreme fruit of the Dao—this too is difficult. It is as rare as seeking gold, jade, or wondrous treasures and flowers. To escape the eight difficulties and obtain a human body is difficult. Having encountered me, you must not let this opportunity pass in vain.

In the past, I underwent countless austerities to attain this supreme expedient means. For your sake, across immeasurable kalpas, I relinquished my body, hands and feet, head and eyes, marrow and brain. Therefore, you must not be negligent.

All you great assemblies, how do you adorn the true Dharma, the treasure city replete with all virtues, the precious gems of precepts, concentration, and wisdom as its walls and moats? Now that you have encountered this treasure city of the Dao, you must not cling to these false and worthless things. It is like a merchant who, upon finding a true treasure city, gathers mere shards and tiles before returning home—just so have you, having encountered the treasure city, taken up worthless things.

All you great assemblies, do not let a lowly mind breed contentment. Though you have now left the household life, you do not yet yearn for this Great Vehicle. Though your bodies wear the dyed robes of yellow and brown, your minds remain unstained by the pure Dharma of the Great Vehicle. Though you beg for alms, traversing many places, you have never sought the nourishment of the Great Vehicle’s Dharma.

All you great assemblies, though you are vast in number, you have not yet, for the sake of the true Dharma, severed the bonds that bind you. Now I truly command you: I am still present, and the assembly is gathered. The true nature of Dharma is unshaken. Therefore, you must be diligent, gather your minds with courage, and shatter the bonds that fetter you. Once the sun of wisdom in the ten directions has set, you will be shrouded in ignorance.

All you assemblies of Dharma, just as the earth’s mountains and herbs serve the needs of beings, so too does my Dharma give rise to the wondrous, sweet ambrosia of the Dharma, the sovereign remedy for the afflictions of all beings. Now I shall establish all beings—and my fourfold assembly of disciples—within the secret treasury. I too shall abide therein before ascending to the upper realms.

What is this secret treasury? It is like the three times—past, present, and future—unbroken in their continuity. Why? The past does not depart, the present does not abide, the future does not arrive. Arrival has no source, departure no destination. The upper, middle, and lower are likewise: the upper is not above, the middle is not within, the lower is not below; there is no going, no staying. All Dharmas are thus. The three times are distinct, yet they do not point toward the upper realms. You must contemplate them in this way. When the time comes, I shall return to the upper realms.

Then, hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s resolve to ascend, all the assemblies of Dharma were filled with sorrow. Their hair stood on end, tears streamed down their faces, and they bowed at his feet, circumambulating him countless times before addressing the Heavenly Worthy:

“Heavenly Worthy, your wondrous teaching on impermanence, suffering, emptiness, and non-self—among all thoughts, the perception of impermanence is supreme, just as the bird’s footprint is the finest among all tracks. If one diligently cultivates this perception, it can eradicate all craving in the desire realm, attachment to form and the formless, ignorance, arrogance, and the perception of impermanence itself.

Heavenly Worthy, Great Sage, if you were free from the perception of impermanence, you would not now be preparing to ascend. Yet if you have not yet transcended it, how can you say that cultivating the perception of impermanence severs the three realms’ craving, ignorance, arrogance, and the perception of impermanence?

Heavenly Worthy, it is like a farmer who, in autumn, deeply plows the earth to uproot weeds. The perception of impermanence is likewise—it eradicates all craving in the desire realm, attachment to form and the formless, ignorance, arrogance, and the perception of impermanence itself. Just as autumn plowing is supreme among all tilling, and the bird’s footprint is finest among all tracks, so too is the perception of impermanence foremost among all thoughts.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like a king who, knowing his end is near, pardons all prisoners in his realm, releasing them from their bonds before he departs. Heavenly Worthy, you should do the same: liberate all beings from ignorance and delusion, freeing them from their fetters before ascending.

Yet we have not yet been liberated—how can you now abandon us and ascend to the upper realms?

Heavenly Worthy, it is like one possessed by a ghost, who, upon encountering a skilled exorcist, is freed by the power of incantations. So too do you, Heavenly Worthy, dispel the ghost of ignorance for all assemblies of Dharma, enabling them to abide in the great merit of goodness.

It is like a fragrant bird bound by humans—though a skilled master may be present, it cannot be restrained until its bonds are severed, and it flies away at will. We have not yet broken free from the fifty-seven fetters of affliction—how can you now abandon us and ascend?

Heavenly Worthy, it is like one afflicted by malaria, who, upon meeting a skilled physician, is cured of suffering. We too suffer from many afflictions—the illnesses of perverse cold and heat—yet though we have encountered you, our maladies remain unhealed. We have not attained the supreme, secure, and eternal bliss—how can you now abandon us and ascend?

Heavenly Worthy, it is like a drunkard who, unaware of himself, fails to recognize kin or strangers, mother or daughter, elder or younger sister, and wanders in confusion, indulging in reckless speech and lewdness, lying in filth. Then a skilled physician gives him medicine to induce vomiting, and upon regaining sobriety, he recalls his actions with shame, reproaching himself: ‘Wine is evil, the root of all wrongs. If I can sever it, I will distance myself from all transgressions.’

Heavenly Worthy, we too have been intoxicated by the cycle of birth and death, drunk on the passions of the senses, mistaking non-mothers for mothers, non-sisters for sisters, non-daughters for daughters, and non-beings for beings. Thus we revolve in suffering, like the drunkard lying in filth.”

Heavenly Worthy, now bestow upon me the medicinal Dharma, that I may vomit forth the afflictive wine of defilements. Yet I have not yet awakened—why does the Heavenly Worthy now intend to abandon us and ascend to the Upper Realm?

Heavenly Worthy, it is like one who praises the plantain tree, believing it to be solid and firm—there is no such truth in it. Heavenly Worthy, so too are sentient beings: if one extols the self, person, sentient being, or lifespan, nurturing perceptions of knowing, acting, and receiving, claiming these to be real—there is no such truth in it. We, like this, cultivate the thought of no-self.

Heavenly Worthy, as dregs of fermented drink are of no further use, so too is this body—without self, without master. Heavenly Worthy, as the seven-leafed flower has no fragrance, so too is this body—without self, without master. We, like this, constantly cultivate the thought of no-self.

As the Venerable One has said, all dharmas are without the thought of self, and you, the assembly of dharmas, ought to cultivate thus. Having cultivated in this way, you will dispel the arrogance of self; having parted from the arrogance of self, you will ascend to the Upper Realm.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like a bird’s track appearing in the sky—there is no such truth in it. If one cultivates the thought of no-self, yet clings to various views—there is no such truth in it.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy praised the assembly of dharmas: Excellent, excellent! You have skillfully cultivated the thought of no-self.

Then the assembly of dharmas addressed the Heavenly Worthy: We do not merely cultivate the thought of no-self, but further cultivate other thoughts as well—namely, the thoughts of suffering, impermanence, and no-self.

Heavenly Worthy, it is like a drunkard whose mind is dizzy and confused, seeing mountains and rivers, cities and palaces, the sun, moon, and stars all whirling about. Heavenly Worthy, those who do not cultivate the thoughts of suffering, impermanence, no-self, and the like—such persons cannot be called noble. They are full of heedlessness and drift through the cycle of birth and death. Heavenly Worthy, for this reason, we diligently cultivate these thoughts.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the great assembly: Listen carefully, listen carefully. The drunkard analogy you have just cited grasps only the words, not their meaning. What, then, is the meaning?

It is like the drunkard who sees the sun and moon above and, though they do not actually revolve, conceives them as revolving. So too are sentient beings: covered by the defilements of ignorance, they generate inverted thoughts—conceiving no-self as self, impermanence as permanence, impurity as purity, and suffering as happiness. Though they generate these thoughts, they do not grasp their meaning, like the drunkard who, where there is no turning, conceives a turning.

The *self* is the meaning of the Dao; *permanence* is the meaning of the Dharma-body; *happiness* is the meaning of the Upper Realm; *purity* is the meaning of the Dharma.

Why, O assembly of dharmas, do you say that those who cling to the thought of self are haughty, quarrelsome, and drift through the cycle of birth and death? If you cultivate the thoughts of impermanence, suffering, and no-self as I have taught, these three kinds of cultivation are without precious meaning. I shall now expound a cultivation superior to these three.

To conceive suffering as happiness, happiness as suffering—this is inverted Dharma. To conceive impermanence as permanence, permanence as impermanence—this is inverted Dharma. To conceive no-self as self, self as no-self—this is inverted Dharma. To conceive impurity as purity, purity as impurity—this is inverted Dharma. These are the four inverted dharmas. Those who do not know the correct cultivation of dharmas are like this.

You, the assembly of dharmas, in the midst of suffering generate the thought of happiness; in the midst of impermanence, the thought of permanence; in the midst of no-self, the thought of self; in the midst of impurity, the thought of purity. In the world, there is permanence, happiness, self, and purity; in the supramundane, there is also permanence, happiness, self, and purity. The worldly Dharma has words but no meaning; the supramundane has both words and meaning.

Why is this? The worldly Dharma has the four inversions, and thus does not know the meaning. Why? There is the inversion of thought, the inversion of mind, and the inversion of view. Due to these three inversions, worldly people see suffering in happiness, impermanence in permanence, no-self in self, and impurity in purity—this is called inversion. Due to inversion, worldly people know the words but not the meaning.

What, then, is the meaning? *No-self* is birth-and-death. *Self* is the Heavenly Worthy. *Impermanence* is the teaching of the Voice-Hearers and Conditioned. *Permanence* is the Dharma-body of the Heavenly Worthy. *Suffering* is all external paths. *Happiness* is the Upper Realm. *Impurity* is conditioned dharmas. *Purity* is the true Dharma possessed by all Heavenly Worthies and Perfected Ones. This is called non-inversion. Due to non-inversion, one knows both the words and the meaning.

If you wish to be far removed from the four inversions, you should know thus: permanence, happiness, self, and purity.

Then the assembly of dharmas again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: As the Heavenly Worthy has said, those who part from the four inversions come to know permanence, happiness, self, and purity. The Heavenly Worthy is now forever free from the four inversions and has already realized permanence, happiness, self, and purity. If you have realized permanence, happiness, self, and purity, why do you not remain for half an eon or a full eon to teach and guide us, enabling us to part from the four inversions, rather than abandoning us to ascend to the Upper Realm?

If the Heavenly Worthy would but deign to look upon us with compassion and instruct us, we would wholeheartedly receive and cultivate your teachings. If the Heavenly Worthy is to ascend to the Upper Realm, how can we remain here with these poisonous bodies, cultivating the pure practice? We too shall follow the Heavenly Worthy to the Upper Realm.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the assembly of dharmas: You ought not speak thus. I have now entrusted all my supreme true Dharma to the Venerable Lord Lao. This Lord Lao shall serve as your great refuge, just as the Heavenly Worthy serves as the refuge for all sentient beings. Lord Lao shall likewise be your refuge.

It is like a great king who rules over many lands. When he travels abroad, he entrusts all state affairs to his ministers.

The Heavenly Worthy is likewise: all true Dharma has been entrusted to Lord Lao. You ought to know that the impermanent and suffering notions you previously cultivated are not real. It is like in spring, when many people bathe in a great pond and play upon boats, and one loses a beryl jewel, which sinks into the deep water. All then enter the water to seek the jewel, each grasping at tiles, stones, grass, and sand, each claiming to have found the beryl jewel and joyfully bringing it out—only to discover it is not real. The jewel remains in the water, and by its power, the water becomes perfectly clear. The assembly then sees the jewel still beneath the water, as if gazing up at the moon in the empty sky. Among them, one wise person employs skillful means, enters the water calmly, and at once obtains the jewel.

You, the assembly of dharmas, ought not cultivate notions of impermanence, suffering, no-self, and impurity as if they were true, just as those people mistook tiles, stones, grass, and sand for the jewel. You should instead diligently study skillful means, cultivating in every place and at all times the notions of self, permanence, bliss, and purity.

You ought further to know that the four marks you previously cultivated are all inverted. To truly cultivate these notions, you must be like that wise person who skillfully retrieved the jewel—namely, the notions of self, permanence, bliss, and purity.

Thereupon, the assembly of dharmas addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "As the Heavenly Worthy previously taught, all dharmas are without self, and you instructed us to cultivate this. Having cultivated it, one abandons the notion of self; having abandoned the notion of self, one abandons arrogance; having abandoned arrogance, one attains the Upper Realm. How is this to be understood?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied to the assembly of dharmas: "Excellent, excellent! You now skillfully inquire into this meaning to resolve your own doubts. It is like a king who is dull-witted and lacking in discernment, who employs a physician of stubborn ignorance. The king, unable to distinguish, grants him generous emoluments. This physician treats all illnesses with milk alone, unaware of the root causes of disease. Though he knows of milk as a remedy, he does not properly understand illnesses of wind, cold, or heat, and prescribes milk for all ailments. The king, unable to discern the physician’s competence or the quality of the milk, simply accepts it.

Then a skilled physician, versed in the eight branches of medicine and proficient in treating all diseases, arrives from afar. The former physician, failing to seek instruction, instead harbors resentment and contempt. The skilled physician then humbly attaches himself, requesting to become a disciple, and seeks the secret methods of medicine, saying to the former physician: 'I now beseech you to be my teacher. I only wish that you would expound and clarify the teachings.' The former physician replies: 'If you can serve me for forty-eight years, only then will I teach you the medical arts.' The skilled physician immediately accepts his instruction: 'I shall do as you say. I shall do as you say. I shall serve you to the best of my ability.'

Thereupon, the former physician leads the visiting physician to see the king. The visiting physician then explains to the king various medical methods and other arts, saying: 'Great King, you ought to discern carefully: this method may be used to govern the state, and this method may be used to treat illness.' Upon hearing this, the king at last recognizes the former physician’s foolishness and ignorance, immediately banishes him from the kingdom, and thereafter doubles his reverence for the visiting physician.

The visiting physician then thinks: 'Now is the time to instruct the king.' He addresses the king: 'If the Great King truly cherishes me, grant me one wish.' The king replies: 'From my right arm to the rest of my body, I shall grant you whatever you desire.' The visiting physician says: 'Though the king offers me his entire body, I dare not ask for much. My sole request is that the king issue a decree forbidding all within the kingdom from consuming the former physician’s milk remedies from this day forward. Why? Because this medicine is poisonous and causes great harm.'"

"If any still consume it, their heads shall be struck off." Having thus severed the use of milk remedies, there were no longer those who died untimely deaths, and all dwelt in peace and happiness—this was the wish he sought. The king replied: "What you ask is but a trifling matter." He immediately issued a decree throughout the kingdom that no sick person was to use milk as medicine, and if any did so, their heads would be struck off.

At that time, the visiting physician compounded various medicines—pungent, bitter, salty, sweet, and intoxicating flavors—to treat all manner of illnesses, and none failed to recover. Before long, the king fell ill again and summoned the physician: "I am gravely ill now. How should I be treated?" The physician diagnosed the king’s condition and determined that milk medicine was required. He promptly addressed the king: "For Your Majesty’s ailment, milk should be taken. My earlier prohibition of milk was not truthful. If taken now, it would most effectively cure the illness. Your Majesty suffers from heat, and milk is precisely what should be consumed."

The king said to the physician: "Are you now mad or feverish? How can you say that milk will cure this illness? You first called it poison, and now you say it should be taken—are you trying to deceive me? The former physician praised it, and you called it poison, driving him away. Now you say it is good and most effective in curing illness. By your words, my former physician was surely superior to you."

The visiting physician then said to the king: "Your Majesty should not speak thus. Just as worms eating wood may by chance form characters, yet the worms themselves do not know whether they are words or not, and a wise person seeing this would never claim the worms understand writing, nor would they be astonished. Your Majesty should know that the former physician was like this: he did not distinguish between illnesses and prescribed milk for all, just as the worm’s path happened to form characters. The former physician did not understand the good or bad, the wholesome or harmful qualities of milk medicine."

The king asked: "How did he not understand?" The physician replied: "Milk medicine is both poison and ambrosia. Why is milk also called ambrosia? If the cow does not eat distillers’ grains, smooth grass, or wheat chaff; if its calf is well-tempered; if its grazing ground is neither high nor low and damp; if it drinks clear water; if it is not made to run; if it is not kept with the calf in the same herd; if its diet and rest are properly regulated—then such milk can cure all illnesses and is called ambrosial medicine. Apart from this, all other milk is poison."

Upon hearing this, the king praised him: "Great physician, excellent! Excellent! Only today have I come to know the good and bad, the wholesome and harmful qualities of milk medicine." He then consumed it, and his illness was cured. Immediately, he issued a decree throughout the kingdom that from that day forward, milk medicine was to be taken. When the people heard this, they were filled with anger and resentment, saying to one another: "The king is now possessed by a demon or has gone mad with delusion, ordering us to consume milk again." All the people, harboring anger, gathered before the king.

The king said: "You should not be so resentful toward me. Whether milk medicine is taken or not is entirely the physician’s instruction, not my fault." Then the king and all the people leapt for joy, doubling their reverence and offerings to the physician. All who were ill consumed milk medicine. The illnesses [text missing] *The Supreme Numinous Treasure Primordial Yang Wondrous Scripture, Scroll Ten, ends.*
